edition of this work have be call for but i be unwilling to allow a new edition to go forth with all the original fault of the work upon its head and i have be too much engage in the practical construction of steam ship and steam engine to find time for the thorough revision which i know the work require at length however i have sufficiently disengaged myself from these onerous pursuit to accomplish this necessary revision and i now offer the work to the public with the confidence that it will be find better deserving of the favorable acceptation and high praise it have already receive there be very few error either of fact or of inference in the early edition which i have have to correct but there be many omission which i have have to supply and fault of arrangement and classification which i have have to rectify i have also have to bring the information which the work profess to afford up to the present time so as to comprehend the latest improvement for the sake of greater distinctness the work be now divide into chapter some of these chapter be altogether new and the rest have receive such extensive addition and improvement as to make the book almost a new one one purpose of my emendation have be to render my remark intelligible to a tyro as well as instructive to a advanced student with this view i have devote the first chapter to a popular description of the steam engine -- which all may understand who can understand anything -- and in the subsequent gradation of progress i have be careful to set no object before the reader for the first time of which the nature and function be not simultaneously explain the design i have propose to myself in the composition of this work be to take a young lad who know nothing of steam engine and to lead he by easy advance up to the highest point of information i have myself attain and it have be a pleasing duty to I to smooth for other the path which i myself find so rugged and to impart for the general good of mankind the secret which other have guard with so much jealousy i believe i be the first author who have communicate that practical information respect the steam engine which person propose to follow the business of a engineer desire to possess my business have therefore be the rough business of a pioneer and while hew a road through the trackless forest along which all might hereafter travel with ease i have no time to attend to those minute grace of composition and petty perfection of arrangement and collocation which be the attribute of the academic grove or the literary parterre i be nevertheless not insensible to the advantage of method and clear arrangement in any work profess to instruct mankind in the principle and practice of any art and many of the change introduce into the present edition of this work be design to render it less exceptionable in this respect the woodcut now introduce into the work for the first time will i believe much increase its interest and utility and upon the whole i be content to dismiss it into circulation in the belief that those who peruse it attentively will obtain a more rapid and more practical acquaintance with the steam engine in its various application than they would be likely otherwise to acquire i have only to add that i have prepare a sequel to the present work in the shape of a hand-book of the steam engine contain the whole of the rule give in the present work illustrate by example work out at length and also contain such useful table and other datum as the engineer require to refer to constantly in the course of he practice this work may be bind up with the catechism if desire to which it be in fact a key i shall thankfully receive from engineer either abroad or at home account of any engine or other machinery with which they may become familiar in they several locality and i shall be happy in my turn to answer any inquiry on engineering subject which fall within the compass of my information if young engineer meet with any difficulty in they study i shall be happy to resolve it if i can and they may communicate with I upon any such point without hesitation in whatever quarter of the world they may of marine engine management of locomotive mechanical principle of the steam engine classification of engine 1 _ q _ -- what be mean by a vacuum _ a _ -- a vacuum mean a empty space a space in which there be neither water nor air nor anything else that we know of 2 _ q _ -- wherein do a high pressure differ from a low pressure engine _ a _ -- in a high pressure engine the steam after have push the piston to the end of the stroke escape into the atmosphere and the impel force be therefore that due to the difference between the pressure of the steam and the pressure of the atmosphere in the condense engine the steam after have press the piston to the end of the stroke pass into the condenser in which a vacuum be maintain and the impel force be that due to the difference between the pressure of the steam above the piston and the pressure of the vacuum beneath it which be nothing or in other word you have then the whole pressure of the steam urge the piston consist of the pressure show by the safety-valve on the boiler and the pressure of the atmosphere besides 3 _ q _ -- in what way would you class the various kind of condense engine _ a _ -- into single act rotative and rotatory engine single act engine be engine without a crank such as be use for pump water rotative engine be engine provide with a crank by means of which a rotative motion be produce and in this important class stand marine and mill engine and all engine indeed in which the rectilinear motion of the piston be change into a circular motion in rotatory engine the steam act at once in the production of circular motion either upon a revolving piston or otherwise but without the use of any intermediate mechanism such as the crank for derive a circular from a rectilinear motion rotatory engine have not hitherto be very successful so that only the single acting or pump engine and the double acting or rotative engine can be say to be in actual use for some purpose such for example as force air into furnace for smelt iron double acting engine be employ which be nevertheless unfurnished with a crank but engine of this kind be not sufficiently numerous to justify they classification as a distinct species and in general those engine may be consider to be single act by which no rotatory motion be impart 4 _ q _ -- be not the circular motion derive from a cylinder engine very irregular in consequence of the unequal leverage of the crank at the different part of its revolution _ a _ -- no rotative engine be generally provide with a fly-wheel to correct such irregularity by its momentum but where two engine with they respective crank set at right angle be employ the irregularity of one engine correct that of the other with sufficient exactitude for many purpose in the case of marine and locomotive engine a fly-wheel be not employ but for cotton spin and other purpose require great regularity of motion its use with common engine be indispensable though it be not impossible to supersede the necessity by new contrivance 5 _ q _ -- you imply that there be some other difference between single acting and double acting engine than that which lie in the use or exclusion of the crank _ a _ -- yes single act engine act only in one way by the force of the steam and be return by a counter-weight whereas double acting engine be urge by the steam in both direction engine as i have already say be sometimes make double act though unprovided with a crank and there would be no difficulty in so arrange the valve of all ordinary pump engine as to admit of this action for the pump might be contrived to raise water both by the upward and downward stroke as indeed in some mine be already do but engine without a crank be almost always make single act perhaps from the effect of custom as much as from any other reason and be usually speak of as such though it be necessary to know that there be some deviation from the usual practice nature and use of a vacuum 6 _ q _ -- the pressure of a vacuum you have state be nothing but how can the pressure of a vacuum be say to be nothing when a vacuum occasion a pressure of 15 lb on the square inch _ a _ -- because it be not the vacuum which exert this pressure but the atmosphere which like a head of water press on everything immerge beneath it a head of water however would not press down a piston if the water be admit on both of its side for a equilibrium would then be establish just as in the case of a balance which retain its equilibrium when a equal weight be add to each scale but take the weight out of one scale or empty the water from one side of the piston and motion or pressure be produce and in like manner pressure be produce on a piston by admit steam or air upon the one side and withdraw the steam or air from the other side it be not therefore to a vacuum but rather to the existence of a unbalanced plenum that the pressure make manifest by exhaustion be due and it be obvious therefore that a vacuum of itself would not work a engine 7 _ q _ -- how be the vacuum maintain in a condense engine _ a _ -- the steam after have perform its office in the cylinder be permit to pass into a vessel call the condenser where a shower of cold water be discharge upon it the steam be condensed by the cold water and fall in the form of hot water to the bottom of the condenser the water which would else be accumulate in the condenser be continually be pump out by a pump work by the engine this pump be call the air pump because it also discharge any air which may have enter with the water 8 _ q _ -- if a vacuum be a empty space and there be water in the condenser how can there be a vacuum there _ a _ -- there be a vacuum above the water the water be only like so much iron or lead lie at the bottom 9 _ q _ -- be the vacuum in the condenser a perfect vacuum _ a _ -- not quite perfect for the cold water enter for the purpose of condensation be heat by the steam and emit a vapor of a tension represent by about three inch of mercury that be when the common barometer stand at 30 inch a barometer with the space above the mercury communicate with the condenser will stand at about 27 inch 10 _ q _ -- be this imperfection of the vacuum wholly attributable to the vapor in the condenser _ a _ -- no it be partly attributable to the presence of a small quantity of air which enter with the water and which would accumulate until it destroy the vacuum altogether but for the action of the air pump which expel it with the water as already explain all common water contain a certain quantity of air in solution and this air recover its elasticity when the pressure of the atmosphere be take off just as the gas in soda water fly up so soon as the cork of the bottle be withdraw 11 _ q _ -- be a barometer sometimes apply to the condenser of steam engine _ a _ -- yes and it be call the vacuum gauge because it show the degree of perfection the vacuum have attain another gauge call the steam gauge be apply to the boiler which indicate the pressure of the steam by the height to which the steam force mercury up a tube gauge be also apply to the boiler to indicate the height of the water within it so that it may not be burn out by the water become accidentally too low in some case a succession of cock place a short distance above one another be employ for this purpose and in other case a glass tube be place perpendicularly in the front of the boiler and communicate at each end with its interior the water rise in this tube to the same height as in the boiler itself and thus show the actual water level in most of the modern boiler both of these contrivance be adopt 12 _ q _ -- can a condense engine be work with a pressure less than that of the atmosphere _ a _ -- yes if once it be start but it will be a difficult thing to start a engine if the pressure of the steam be not greater than that of the atmosphere before a engine can be start it have to be blow through with steam to displace the air within it and this can not be effectually do if the pressure of the steam be very low after the engine be start however the pressure in the boiler may be lower if the engine be lightly load until there be a partial vacuum in the boiler such a practice however be not to be commend as the gauge cock become useless when there be a partial vacuum in the boiler inasmuch as when they be open the water will not rush out but air will rush in it be impossible also under such circumstance to blow out any of the sediment collect within the boiler which in the case of the boiler of steam vessel require to be do every two hour or oftener this be accomplish by open a large cock which permit some of the supersalted water to be force overboard by the pressure of the steam in some case in which the boiler apply to a engine be of inadequate size the pressure within the boiler will fall spontaneously to a point considerably beneath the pressure of the atmosphere but it be preferable in such case partially to close the throttle valve in the steam pipe whereby the issue of steam to the engine be diminish and the pressure in the boiler be thus maintain while the cylinder receive its former supply 13 _ q _ -- if a hole be open into a condenser of a steam engine will air rush into it _ a _ -- if the hole communicate with the atmosphere the air will be draw in 14 _ q _ -- with what velocity do air rush into a vacuum _ a _ -- with the velocity which a body would acquire by fall from the height of a homogeneous atmosphere which be a atmosphere of the same density throughout as at the earth 's surface and although such a atmosphere do not exist in nature its existence be suppose in order to facilitate the computation it be well know that the velocity with which water issue from a cistern be the same that would be acquire by a body fall from the level of the head to the level of the issue point which indeed be a obvious law since every particle of water descend and issue by virtue of its gravity and be in its descent subject to the ordinary law of fall body air rush into a vacuum be only another example of the same general principle : the velocity of each particle will be that due to the height of the column of air which would produce the pressure sustained and the weight of air be know as well as the pressure it exert on the earth 's surface it become easy to tell what height a column of air a inch square and of the atmospheric density would require to be to weigh 15 lb the height would be 27818 foot and the velocity which the fall of a body from such a height produce would be 1338 foot per second velocity of fall body and momentum of move body 15 _ q _ -- how do you determine the velocity of fall body of different kind _ a _ -- all body fall with the same velocity when there be no resistance from the atmosphere as be show by the experiment of let fall from the top of a tall exhaust receiver a feather and a guinea which reach the bottom at the same time the velocity of fall body be one that be accelerate uniformly accord to a known law when the height from which a body fall be give the velocity acquire at the end of the descent can be easily compute it have be find by experiment that the square root of the height in foot multiply by 8021 will give the velocity 16 _ q _ -- but the velocity in what term _ a _ -- in foot per second the distance through which a body fall by gravity in one second be 16-1\/12 foot in two seconds 64-4\/12 foot in three seconds 144-9\/12 foot in four seconds 257-4\/12 foot and so on if the number of foot fall through in one second be take as unity then the relation of the time to the space will be as follow : -- number of seconds | 1 | 2 | 3 | 4 | 5 | 6 | unit of space pass through | 1 | 4 | 9 | 16 | 25 | 36 | & c so that it appear that the space pass through by a fall body be as the square of the time of fall 17 _ q _ -- be not the urge force which cause body to fall the force of gravity _ a _ -- yes the force of gravity or the attraction of the earth 18 _ q _ -- and be not that a uniform force or a force act with a uniform pressure _ a _ -- it be 19 _ q _ -- therefore during the first second of fall as much impel power will be give by the force of gravity as during every succeed second _ a _ -- undoubtedly 20 _ q _ -- how come it then that while the body fall 64-4\/12 foot in two seconds it fall only 16-1\/12 foot in one second or why since it fall only 16-1\/12 foot in one second should it fall more than twice 16-1\/12 foot in two _ a _ -- because 16-1\/12 foot be the average and not the maximum velocity during the first second the velocity acquire _ at the end _ of the 1st second be not 16-1\/12 but 32-1\/6 foot per second and at the end of the 2d second a velocity of 32-1\/6 foot have to be add so that the total velocity at the end of the 2d second become 64-2\/6 foot at the end of the 3d the velocity become 96-3\/6 foot at the end of the 4th 128-4\/6 foot and so on these number proceed in the progression 1 2 3 4 & c so that it appear that the velocity acquire by a fall body at different point be simply as the time of fall but if the velocity be as the time and the total space pass through be as the square of the time then the total space pass through must be as the square of the velocity and as the _ vis viva _ or mechanical power inherent in a fall body of any give weight be measurable by the height through which it descend it follow that the _ vis viva _ be proportionate to the square of the velocity of two ball therefore of equal weight but one move twice as fast as the other the faster ball have four time the energy or mechanical force accumulate in it that the slower ball have if the speed of a fly-wheel be double it have four time the _ vis viva _ it possess before -- _ vis viva _ be measurable by a reference to the height through which a body must have fall to acquire the velocity give 21 _ q _ -- by what consideration be the _ vis viva _ or mechanical energy proper for the fly-wheel of a engine determine _ a _ -- by a reference to the power produce every half-stroke of the engine join to the consideration of what relation the energy of the fly-wheel rim must have thereto to keep the irregularity of motion within the limit which be admissible it be find in practice that when the power resident in the fly-wheel rim when the engine move at its average speed be from two and a half to four time greater than the power generate by the engine in one half-stroke -- the variation depend on the energy inherent in the machinery the engine have to drive and the equability of motion require -- the engine will work with sufficient regularity for most ordinary purpose but where great equability of motion be require it will be advisable to make the power resident in the fly-wheel equal to six time the power generate by the engine in one half-stroke 22 _ q _ -- can you give a practical rule for determine the proper quantity of cast iron for the rim of a fly-wheel in ordinary land engine _ a _ -- one rule frequently adopt be as follow : -- multiply the mean diameter of the rim by the number of its revolution per minute and square the product for a divisor divide the number of actual horse power of the engine by the number of stroke the piston make per minute multiply the quotient by the constant number 2760000 and divide the product by the divisor find as above the quotient be the requisite quantity of cast iron in cubic foot to form the fly-wheel rim 23 _ q _ -- what be boulton and watt 's rule for find the dimension of the fly-wheel _ a _ -- boulton and watt 's rule for find the dimension of the fly-wheel be as follow : -- multiply 44000 time the length of the stroke in foot by the square of the diameter of the cylinder in inch and divide the product by the square of the number of revolution per minute multiply by the cube of the diameter of the fly-wheel in foot the result number will be the sectional area of the rim of the fly-wheel in square inch central force 24 _ q _ -- what do you understand by centrifugal and centripetal force _ a _ -- by centrifugal force i understand the force with which a revolving body tend to fly from the center and by centripetal force i understand any force which draw it to the center or counteract the centrifugal tendency in the conical pendulum or steam engine governor which consist of two metal ball suspend on rod hang from the end of a vertical revolving shaft the centrifugal force be manifest by the divergence of the ball when the shaft be put into revolution and the centripetal force which in this instance be gravity predominate so soon as the velocity be arrest for the arm then collapse and hang by the side of the shaft 25 _ q _ -- what measure be there of the centrifugal force of body revolve in a circle _ a _ -- the centrifugal force of body revolve in a circle increase as the diameter of the circle if the number of revolution remain the same if there be two fly-wheel of the same weight and make the same number of revolution per minute but the diameter of one be double that of the other the larger will have double the amount of centrifugal force the centrifugal force of the _ same wheel _ however increase as the square of the velocity so that if the velocity of a fly-wheel be double it will have four time the amount of centrifugal force 26 _ q _ -- can you give a rule for determine the centrifugal force of a body of a give weight move with a give velocity in a circle of a give diameter _ a _ -- yes if the velocity in foot per second be divide by 401 the square of the quotient will be four time the height in foot from which a body must have fall to have acquire that velocity divide this quadruple height by the diameter of the circle and the quotient be the centrifugal force in term of the weight of the body so that multiply the quotient by the actual weight of the body we have the centrifugal force in pound or ton another rule be to multiply the square of the number of revolution per minute by the diameter of the circle in foot and to divide the product by 5870 the quotient be the centrifugal force in term of the weight of the body 27 _ q _ -- how do you find the velocity of the body when its centrifugal force and the diameter of the circle in which it move be give _ a _ -- multiply the centrifugal force in term of the weight of the body by the diameter of the circle in foot and multiply the square root of the product by 401 the result will be the velocity of the body in foot per second 28 _ q _ -- will you illustrate this by find the velocity at which the cast iron rim of a fly-wheel 10 foot in diameter would burst asunder by its 4948 -lrb- the weight of the half rim -rrb- be equal to 6063 which be the centrifugal force in term of the weight then by the rule give in the last answer 6063 x 10 = 6063 the square root of which be 78 nearly and 78 x 401 = 31278 the velocity of the rim in foot per second at the moment of rupture 29 _ q _ -- what be the greatest velocity at which it be safe to drive a cast iron fly-wheel _ a _ -- the rim will increase the centrifugal force in the same proportion centre of gravity gyration and oscillation 31 _ q _ -- what do you understand by the center of gravity of a body _ a _ -- that point within it in which the whole of the weight may be suppose to be concentrated and which continually endeavor to gain the lowest possible position a body hang in the center of gravity will remain at rest in any position 32 _ q _ -- what be mean by the center of gyration _ a _ -- the center of gyration be that point in a revolving body in which the whole momentum may be conceive to be concentrated or in which the whole effect of the momentum reside if the ball of a governor be to be move in a straight line the momentum might be say to be concentrate at the center of gravity of the ball but inasmuch as by its revolution round a axis the part of the ball furthest remove from the axis move more quickly than the part nearest to it the momentum can not be suppose to be concentrate at the center of gravity but at a point further remove from the central shaft and that point be what be call the center of gyration 33 _ q _ -- what be the center of oscillation _ a _ -- the center of oscillation be a point in a pendulum or any swinging body such that if all the matter of the body be to be collect into that point the velocity of its vibration would remain unaffected it be in fact the mean distance from the center of suspension of every atom in a ratio which happen not to be a arithmetical one the center of oscillation be always in a line pass through the center of suspension and the center of gravity the pendulum and governor 34 _ q _ -- by what circumstance be the velocity of vibration of a pendulous body determine _ a _ -- by the length of the suspend rod only or more prefer as there be in that case no sensible deviation from the cycloidal curve but in other respects the size of the arc do not signify 35 _ q _ -- if then the length of a pendulum be give can the extend of good bar iron be about 60000 lb or nearly 27 ton per square inch of section and the tensile strength of cast iron be about 15000 lb or say 63\/4 to 7 ton per square inch of section these be the weight which be require to break they the crush strain of cast iron however be about 100000 lb or 441\/2 ton whereas the crush strength of malleable iron be not more than 27000 lb or 12 ton per square inch of section and indeed it be generally less than this the ultimate tensile strength therefore of malleable iron be four time greater than that of cast iron but the crush strength of cast iron be between three and four time greater than that of work iron it may be state in round number that the tensile strength of malleable iron be twice greater than its crush strength or in other word that it will take twice the strain to break a bar of malleable iron by draw it asunder endway than will cripple it by force it together endway like a pillar whereas a bar of cast iron will be draw asunder with one sixth of the force that will be require to break or cripple it when force together endway like a pillar 65 _ q _ -- what be the cohesive strength of steel _ a _ -- the ultimate q _ -- what strain may be apply to malleable iron in practice _ a _ -- a bar of work iron to which a tensile or compress strain be apply be elongate or contract like a very stiff spiral spring nearly in the proportion of the amount of strain apply up to the limit at which the strength begin to give way and within this limit it will recover its original dimension when the strain be remove if however the strain be carry beyond this limit the bar will not recover its original dimension but will be permanently pull out or push in just as would happen to a spring to which a undue strain have be apply this limit be what be call the limit of elasticity and whenever it be exceed the bar though it may not break immediately will undergo a progressive deterioration and will break in the course of time the limit of elasticity of malleable iron when extend or in other word the tensile strain to which a bar of malleable iron a inch square may be subject without permanently derange its structure be usually take at 17800 lb or from that to 10 ton depend on the quality of the iron it have also be find that malleable iron be extend about one ten-thousandth part of its length for every ton of direct strain apply to it 68 _ q _ -- what be the limit of elasticity of cast iron _ a _ -- it be commonly take at 15300 lb per square inch of section but this be certainly much too high as it exceed the tensile strength of iron of medium quality a bar of cast iron if compress by weight will be contract in length twice as much as a bar of malleable iron under similar circumstance but malleable iron when subject to a greater strain than 12 ton per square inch of section gradually crumple up by the mere continuance of the weight a cast-iron bar one inch square and ten foot long be shorten about one tenth of a inch by a compress force of 10000 lb whereas a malleable iron bar of the same dimension would require to shorten it equally a compress force of 20000 lb as the load however approach 12 ton the compression become nearly equal and above that point the rate of the compression of the malleable iron rapidly increase a bar of cast iron when at its breaking point by the application of a tensile strain be stretch about one six-hundredth part of its length and a equal strain employ to compress it would shorten it about one eight-hundredth part of its length 69 _ q _ -- but to what strain may the iron use in the construction of engine be safely subject _ a _ -- the most of the work part of modern engine be make of malleable iron and the utmost strain to which work section be sometimes exceed by nearly one half but such a excess of strain approach the limit of danger 70 _ q _ -- will you explain in what way the various strain subsist in a steam engine may be resolve into tensile and crush strain also in what way the magnitude of those strain may be determine _ a _ -- to take the case of a beam subject to a transverse strain such as the great beam of a engine it be clear if we suppose the beam break through the middle that the amount of strain at the upper and lower edge of the beam where the whole strain may be suppose to be collect will with any give pressure on the piston depend upon the proportion of the length to the depth of the beam one edge of the beam break by extension and the other edge by compression and the upper and lower edge may be regard as pillar one of which be extend by the strain and the other be compress if to make a extreme supposition the depth of the beam be take as equal to its length then the pillar answer to the edge of the beam will be compress and extend by what be virtually a bellcrank lever with equal arm the horizontal distance from the main center to the end of the beam be one of the arm and the vertical height from the main center to the top edge of the beam be the other arm the distance therefore pass through by the fractured edge of the beam during a stroke of the engine will be equal to the length of the stroke and the strain it will have to sustain will consequently be equal to the pressure on the piston if its motion be only half that of the piston as would be the case if its depth be make one half less the strain the beam would have to bear would be twice as great and it may be set down as a axiom that the strain upon any part of a steam engine or other machine be inversely equal to the strain produce by the prime mover multiply by the comparative velocity with which the part in question move if any part of a engine move with a less velocity than the piston it will have a greater strain on it if resist than be throw upon the piston if it move with a greater velocity than the piston it will have a less strain upon it and the difference of strain will in every case be in the inverse proportion of the difference of the velocity 71 _ q _ -- then in compute the amount of metal necessary to give due strength to a beam the first point be to determine the velocity with which the edge of the beam move at that point be the strain be greatest _ a _ -- the web of a cast-iron beam or girder serve merely to connect the upper and lower edge or flange rigidly together so as to enable the extend and compress strain to be counteract in a effectual manner by the metal of those flange it be only necessary therefore to make the flange of sufficient strength to resist effectually the crush and tensile strain to which they be expose and to make the web of the beam of sufficient strength to prevent a distortion of its shape from take place 72 _ q _ -- be the strain greater from be movable or intermittent than if it be stationary _ a _ -- yes it be nearly twice as great from be movable engineer be in the habit of make girder intend to sustain a stationary load about three time stronger than the break weight but if the load be a movable one as be the case in the girder of railway bridge they make the strength equal to six time the breaking weight 73 _ q _ -- then the strain be increase by the suddenness with which it be apply _ a _ -- if a weight be place on a long and slender beam prop up in the middle and the prop be suddenly withdraw so as to allow deflection to take place it be clear that the deflection must be greater than if the load have be gradually apply the momentum of the weight and also of the beam itself fall through the space through which it have be deflect have necessarily to be counteract by the elasticity of the beam and the beam will therefore be momentarily bent to a greater extent than what be due to the load and after a few vibration up and down it will finally settle at that point of deflection which the load properly occasion it be obvious that a beam must be strong enough not merely to sustain the pressure due to the load but also that accession of pressure due to the counteract momentum of the weight and of the beam itself although in steam engine the beam be not load by a weight but by the pressure of the steam yet the momentum of the beam itself must in every case be counteract and the momentum will be considerable in every case in which a large and rapid deflection take place a rapid deflection increase the amount of the deflection as well as the amount of the strain as be see in the cylinder cover of a cornish pump engine into which the steam be suddenly admit and in which the momentum of the particle of the metal put into motion increase the deflection to a extent such as the mere pressure of the steam could not produce 74 _ q _ -- what will be the amount of increase strain consequent upon deflection _ a _ -- the momentum of any move body be proportional to the square of its velocity it follow that the strain will be proportional to the square of the amount of deflection produce in a specify time 75 _ q _ -- but will not the inertia of a beam resist deflection as well as the momentum increase deflection _ a _ -- no doubt that will be so but whether in practical case increase of mass without reference to strength or load will upon the whole increase or diminish deflection will depend very much upon the magnitude of the mass relatively with the magnitude of the deflect pressure and the rapidity with which that pressure be apply and remove thus if a force or weight be very suddenly apply to the middle of a ponderous beam and be as suddenly withdraw the inertia of the beam will as in the case of the collision of body tend to resist the force and thus obviate deflection to a considerable extent but if the pressure be so long continue as to produce the amount of deflection due to the pressure the effect of the inertia in that case will be to increase the deflection 76 _ q _ -- will the pressure give to the beam of a engine in different direction facilitate safety in the case of cast-iron beam 77 _ q _ -- do the same law hold in the case of the deflection of malleable iron bar _ a _ -- in the case of malleable iron bar it have be find that no very section of a wagon boiler the line b represent the top of the grate or fire bar which slope downward from the front at a angle of about 25  give the fuel a tendency to move toward the back of the grate the supply of air ascend from the ash pit through the grate bar and the flame pass over a low wall or bridge and traverse the bottom of the boiler the smoke rise up at the back of the boiler and proceed through the flue f along one side to the front and return along the other side of the boiler and then ascend the chimney the performance of this course by the smoke be what be term a wheel draught as the smoke wheel once round the boiler and then ascend the chimney 86 _ q _ -- be the performance of this course by the smoke universal in wagon boiler _ a _ -- no such boiler sometimes have what be term a split draught the smoke and flame when they reach the end of the boiler pass in this case through a iron flue or tube reach from end to end of the boiler and on arrive at the front of the boiler the smoke split or separate -- one half pass through a flue on the one side of the boiler and the other half pass through a flue on the other side of the boiler -- both of these flue have they debouch in the chimney 87 _ q _ -- what be the appliance usually connect with a wagon boiler _ a _ -- on the top of the boiler near the front be a short cylinder with a lid secure by bolt this be the manhole door the purpose of which be to enable a man to get into the inside of the boiler when necessary for inspection and repair on the top of this door be a small valve opening downward call the atmospheric valve the intention of this valve be to prevent a vacuum from be form accidentally in the boiler which might collapse it for if the pressure in the boiler subside to a point materially below the pressure of the atmosphere the valve will open and allow air to get in a bent pipe which rise up from the top of the boiler immediately behind the position of the manhole be the steam pipe for conduct the steam to the engine and a bent pipe which ascend from the top of the boiler at the back end be the waste-steam pipe for conduct away the steam which escape through the safety valve this valve be set in a chest standing on the top of the boiler at the foot of the waste-steam pipe and it be load with iron or leaden weight to a point answerable to the intended pressure of the steam 88 _ q _ -- how be the proper level of the water in the boiler maintain _ a _ -- by means of a balanced buoy or float this float be attach to a rod which in its turn be attach to a lever set on the top of a large upright pipe the upper part of the pipe be widen out into a small cistern through a short pipe in the middle of which a chain pass to the damper but any water empty into this small cistern can not pass into the pipe except through a small valve fix to the lever to which the rod be attach the water for replenish the boiler be pump into the small cistern on the top of the pipe and it follow from these arrangement that when the buoy fall the rod open the small valve and allow the feed water to enter the pipe which communicate with the water in the boiler whereas when the buoy rise the feed can not enter the pipe and it have therefore to run to waste through a overflow pipe provide for the purpose 89 _ q _ -- how be the strength of the fire regulate _ a _ -- the draught through the furnace of land boiler be regulate by a plate of metal or a damper as it be call which slide like a sluice up and down in the flue and this damper be close more or less when the intensity of the fire have to be moderate in wagon boiler this be generally accomplish by self-acting mechanism in the small cistern pipe which be call a stand pipe the water rise up to a height proportional to the pressure of the steam and the surface of the water in this pipe will rise or fall with the fluctuation in the pressure of the steam in this pipe a float be place which communicate by means of a chain with the damper if the pressure of the steam rise the float will be raise and the damper close whereas if the pressure in the boiler fall the reverse of this action will take place -lrb- other end the pump end of the beam be usually load so as to cause it to preponderate when the engine be at rest and the whole effort of the steam be employ in overcome this preponderance until a stroke be perform when the steam be shut off the heavy end of the beam again fall and the operation be repeat 95 _ q _ -- in the double-acting engine the piston be push by the steam both way whereas from which the machinery to be drive derive its motion 96 _ q _ -- where do the steam enter from the boiler -lrb- illustration : fig 20 -rrb- _ a _ -- at the steam pipe b the throttle valve in that pipe be a elliptical plate of metal swivel on a spindle pass through its edge from side to side and by turn which more or less the opening through the pipe will be more or less close the extent to which this valve be open or close be determine by the governor d the ball of which as they collapse or expand move up or down a collar on the governor spindle which motion be communicate to the throttle valve by suitable rod and bell-crank the governor it will be see consist substantially of two heavy ball attach to arm fix upon a upright shaft which be keep in revolution by means of a cord drive by a pulley on the fly wheel shaft the velocity with which the ball of the governor revolve be proportional to that of the fly wheel it will follow that if by reason of too rapid a supply of steam a undue speed be give to the fly wheel and therefore to the ball a divergence of the ball will take place to a extent correspond to the excess of velocity and this movement be communicate to the throttle valve it will be partly close -lrb- see fig 1 -rrb- the supply of steam to the engine will be diminish and the velocity of its motion will be reduce if on the other hand the motion of the engine be slower than be requisite owe to a deficient supply of steam through b then the ball not be sufficiently affect by centrifugal force will fall towards the vertical spindle and the throttle valve c will be more fully open whereby a more ample supply of steam will be admit to the cylinder and the speed of the engine will be increase to the requisite extent 97 _ q _ -- the piston must be make to fit the cylinder accurately so as to prevent the passage of steam _ a _ -- the piston be accurately fit to the cylinder and make to move in it steam tight by a packing of hemp drive tightly into a groove or recess round the edge of the piston and which be squeeze down by a iron ring hold by screw the piston divide the cylinder into two compartment between which there be no communication by which steam or any other elastic fluid can pass a casing set beside the cylinder contain the valve by means of which the steam which impel the piston be admit and withdraw as the piston commence its motion in each direction the upper steam box b be divide into three compartment by two valve above the upper steam valve v be a compartment communicate with the steam pipe b below the lower valve e be another compartment communicate with a pipe call the eduction pipe which lead downward from the cylinder to the condenser in which vessel the steam be condensed by a jet of cold water by the valve v a communication may be open or close between the boiler and the top of the cylinder so as to permit or prevent a supply of steam from the one to pass to the other by the valve e a communication may be open or closed between the top of the cylinder and the condenser so that the steam in the top compartment of the cylinder may either be permit to escape into the condenser or may be confine to the cylinder the continuation of the steam pipe lead to the lower steam box b ' which like the upper be divide into three compartment by two valve v ' and e ' and the action of the lower valve be in all respects the same as that of the upper 98 _ q _ -- be all these valve connect together so that they act simultaneously _ a _ -- the four valve v e v ' e ' be connect by rod to a single handle h which handle be move alternately up and down by means of pin or tappet place on the rod which work the air pump when the handle h be press down the lever in connexion with it open the upper exhausting valve e and the lower steam valve v ' and close the upper steam valve v and the lower exhausting valve e ' on the other hand when the handle h be press up it open the upper steam valve v and the lower exhausting valve e ' and at the same time close the upper exhausting valve e and the lower steam valve v ' 99 _ q _ -- where be the condenser situate _ a _ -- the condenser k be immerge in a cistern of cold water at its side there be a tube i for the admission of water to condense the steam and which be govern by a cock by open which to any require extent a jet of cold water may be make to play in the condenser from the bottom of the condenser a short pipe lead to the air pump j and in this pipe there be a flap valve call the foot valve open towards the air pump the air pump be a pump set in the same cistern of cold water that hold the condenser and it be fit with a piston or bucket work by the rod l attach to the great beam and fit with a valve opening upward in the manner of a common sucking pump the upper part of the air pump communicate with a small cistern s call the hot well through a valve opening outwards and call the delivery valve a pump m call the hot water pump lift hot water out of the hot well to feed the boiler and another pump n lift cold water from a well or other source of supply to maintain the supply of water to the cold water cistern in which the condenser and air pump be place 100 q -- will you explain now the manner in which the engine act a -- the piston be suppose to be at the top of the cylinder the handle h will be raise by the lower pin or tappet on the air pump rod and the valve v and e ' will be open and at the same time the other pair of valve v ' and e will be close steam will therefore be admit above the piston and the steam or air which have previously fill the cylinder below the piston will be draw off to the condenser it will there encounter the jet of cold water which be keep constantly play there by keep the cock i sufficiently open it will thus be immediately condensed or reduce to water and the cylinder below the piston will have a vacuum in it the steam therefore admit from the steam pipe through the open valve v to the top of the cylinder not be resist by pressure below will press the piston to the bottom of the cylinder as it approach that position the handle h will be strike down by the upper pin or tappet on the air pump rod and the valve v and e ' previously open will be close while the valve v ' and e previously close will be open the steam which have just press down the piston and which now fill the cylinder above the piston will then flow off through the open valve e to the condenser where it will be immediately condensed by the jet of cold water and steam from the boiler admit through the open valve v ' will fill the cylinder below the piston and press the piston upward when the piston have reach the top of the cylinder the lower pin on the air pump rod will have strike the handle upward and will thereby have close the valve v ' and e and open the valve v and e ' the piston will then be in the same situation as in the commencement and will again descend and so will continue to be drive up and down by the steam 101 q -- but what become of the cold water which be let into the condenser to condense the steam a -- it be pump out by the air pump in the shape of hot water its temperature have be raise considerably by the admixture of the steam in it when the air pump piston ascend it leave behind it a vacuum and the foot valve be relieve from all pressure the weight of the water in the condenser force it open and the warm water flow from the condenser into the lower part of the air pump from which its return to the condenser be prevent by the intervene valve when the air pump piston descend its pressure on the liquid under it will force open the valve in it through which the hot water will ascend and when the bucket descend to the bottom of the pump barrel the warm water which be below it will all have pass above it and can not return when the bucket next ascend the water above it not be able to return through the bucket valve will be force into the hot well through the delivery valve s the hot water pump m pump a small quantity of this hot water into the boiler to compensate for the abstraction of the water that have pass off in the form of steam the residue of the hot water run to waste 102 _ q _ -- by what expedient be the piston rod enable to pass through the cylinder cover without leak steam out of the cylinder or air into it _ a _ -- the hole in the cylinder lid through which the piston rod pass be furnish with a recess call a stuffing box into which a stuffing or packing of plaited hemp be force which press on the one side against the interior of the stuffing box and on the other side against the piston rod which be smooth and polished prevent any leakage in this situation the packing of this stuffing box be force down by a ring of metal tighten by screw this ring which accurately fit the piston rod have a project flange through which bolt pass for tighten the ring down upon the packing and a similar expedient be employ in nearly every case in which packing be employ 103 _ q _ -- in what way be the piston rod connect to the great beam _ a _ -- the piston rod be connect to the great beam by means of two link one at each side of the beam show at _ f g _ -lrb- fig 21 -rrb- these link be usually make of the same length as the crank and they purpose be to enable the end of the great beam to move in the arc of a circle while the piston rod maintain the vertical position the point of junction therefore of the link and the piston rod be of the form of a knuckle or bend at some part of the stroke 104 _ q _ -- but what compel the top of the piston rod to maintain the vertical position _ a _ -- some engine have guide rod set on each side of the piston rod and eye on the top of the piston rod engage these guide rod and maintain the piston rod in a vertical position in every part of the stroke more commonly however the desire end be attain by means of a contrivance call the parallel motion 105 _ q _ -- what be the parallel motion _ a _ -- the parallel motion be a arrangement of jointed rod so connect together that the divergence from the vertical line at any point in the arc describe by the beam be correct by a equal and opposite divergence due to the arc perform by the jointed rod during the stroke and as these opposite deviation mutually correct one another the result be that the piston rod move in a vertical direction 106 _ q _ -- will you explain the action more in detail _ a _ -- the pin fig 21 which pass through the end of the beam at _ f _ have a link _ f g _ hang on each side of the beam and a short cross bar call a cross head extend from the bottom of one of these link to the bottom of the other which cross head be perforated with a hole in the middle for the reception of the piston rod there be similar link _ b d _ at the point of the main beam where the air pump rod be attach there be two rod _ d g _ connect the link _ b d _ with the link _ f g _ and these rod as they always continue parallel to the main beam throughout the stroke be call _ parallel bar _ attach to the end of these two rod at _ d _ be two other rod _ c d _ of which the end at _ c _ be attach to stationary pin while the end at _ d _ follow the motion of the lower end of the link _ b d _ these rod be call the _ radius bar _ now it be obvious that the arc describe by the point _ d _ with _ c _ as a center be opposite to the arc describe by the point _ g _ with _ d _ as a center the rod _ d g _ be therefore draw back horizontally by the arc describe at _ d _ to a extent equal to the verse sine of the arc describe at _ g _ or in other word the line describe by the point _ g _ become a straight line instead of a curve -lrb- illustration : fig 21 -rrb- 107 _ q _ -- do the air pump rod move vertically as well as the piston rod _ a _ -- it do the air pump rod be suspend from a cross head pass from the center of one of the link _ b d _ to the center of the other link on the opposite side of the beam now as the distance from the central axis of the great beam to the point _ b _ be equal to the length of the rod _ c d _ it will follow that the upper end of the link will follow one arc and the lower end a equal and opposite arc a point in the center of the link therefore where these opposite motion meet will follow no arc at all but will move up and down vertically in a straight line 108 _ q _ -- the use of the crank be to obtain a circular motion from a reciprocate motion _ a _ -- that be the object of it and it accomplish its object in a very perfect manner as it gradually arrest the velocity of the piston towards the end of the stroke and thus obviate what would otherwise be a injurious shock upon the machine when the crank approach the lowest part of its throw and at the same time the piston be approach the top of the cylinder the motion of the crank become nearly horizontal or in other word the piston be only advance through a very short distance for any give distance measure on the circle describe by the crank pin since then the velocity of rotation of the crank be nearly uniform it will follow that the piston will move very slowly as it approach the end of the stroke and the piston be bring to a state of rest by this gradually retard motion both at the top and the bottom of the stroke 109 _ q _ -- what cause the crank to revolve at a uniform velocity _ a _ -- the momentum of the machinery move by the piston but more especially of the fly wheel which by its operation redress the unequal pressure communicate by the crank and compel the crank shaft to revolve at a nearly uniform velocity everyone know that a heavy wheel if put into rapid rotation can not be immediately stop at the beginning and end of the stroke when the crank be vertical no force of torsion can be exert on the crank shaft by the crank but this force be at its maximum when the crank be horizontal from the vertical point where this force be nothing to the horizontal point where it be at its maximum the force of torsion exert on the crank shaft be constantly vary and the fly wheel by its momentum redress these irregularity and carry the crank through that dead point as it be term where the piston can not impart any rotative force 110 _ q _ -- be the configuration and structure of the steam engine as it leave the hand of watt materially different from those of modern engine _ a _ -- there be not much difference in modern rotative land engine the valve for admit the steam to the cylinder or condenser instead of be clack or pot-lid valve move by tappet on the air pump rod be usually sluice or slide valve move by a eccentric wheel on the crank shaft sometimes the beam be discard altogether and malleable iron be more largely use in the construction of engine instead of the cast iron which formerly so largely prevail but upon the whole the steam engine of the present day be substantially the engine of watt and he who perfectly understand the operation of watt 's engine will have no difficulty in understand the operation of any of the numerous variety of engine since introduce the marine engine 111 _ q _ -- will you describe the principal feature of the kind of steam engine employ for the propulsion of vessel _ a _ -- marine engine be of two kind -- paddle engine and screw engine in the one case the propel instrument be paddle wheel keep in rotation at each side of the ship : in the other case the propel instrument be a screw consist of two or more twisted vane revolve beneath the water at the stern of each class of engine there be many distinct variety 112 _ q _ -- what be the principal variety of the paddle engine -lrb- illustration : fig 22 -rrb- -lrb- illustration : fig 23 -rrb- _ a _ -- there be the side lever engine -lrb- fig engage the water like the board of a common undershot water wheel or they may be form with _ feather _ float board as they be term which be float board movable on a center and so govern by appropriate mechanism that they enter and leave the water in a nearly vertical position the common fix or radial float however be the kind most widely employ and they be attach to the arm of two or more ring of the end of the eccentric rod out of a notch which engage a pin on the valve shaft and the valve be at such time free to be move by hand by a bar of iron apply to a proper part of the valve gear for that purpose this be so the engineer when he wish to start the engine first open a small valve call the _ blow through valve _ which permit steam from the boiler to enter the engine both above and below the piston and also to fill the condenser and air pump this steam expel the air from the interior of the engine and also any water which may have accumulate there and when this have be do the blow through valve be shut and a vacuum very soon form within the engine by the condensation of the steam if now the slide valve be move by hand the steam from the boiler will be admit on one side of the piston while there be a vacuum on the other side and the piston will therefore be move in the desire direction when the piston reach the end of the stroke the valve have to be move in the reverse direction when the piston will return and after be move thus by hand once or twice the connection of the valve with the eccentric be to be restore by allow the notch on the end of the eccentric rod to engage the pin on the valve lever when the valve will be thereafter move by the engine in the proper manner it will of course be necessary when the engine begin to move to open the injection cock a little to enable water to enter for the condensation of the steam in the most recent marine engine a somewhat different mechanism from this be use for give motion to the valve but that mechanism will be afterwards describe 117 _ q _ -- be all marine engine condense engine _ a _ -- nearly all of they be so but recently a number of gunboat have be construct with high pressure engine in general however marine engine be low pressure or condense engine 118 _ q _ -- will you now describe the chief feature of the oscillate paddle marine engine _ a _ -- in the oscillate paddle marine engine the arrangement of the paddle shaft and paddle wheel be the same as in the case already describe but the whole of the side lever side rod cross head cross tail and connect rod be discard the cylinder be set immediately under the crank the top of the piston rod be connect immediately to the crank pin and to enable the piston rod to accommodate itself to the movement of the crank the cylinder be so construct as to be susceptible of vibrate or oscillate upon two external axis or trunnion these trunnion be generally place about half way up on the side of the cylinder and through one of they steam be receive from the boiler while through the other the steam escape to the condenser the air pump be usually work by means of a crank in the shaft which crank move the air pump bucket up and down as the shaft revolve 119 _ q _ -- will you give a example of a paddle oscillate engine _ a _ -- i will take as a example the oscillate engine construct by messr ravenhill & salk for the holyhead packet _ a _ -- the float be support by spur project from the rim of the wheel and they may be move upon the point of the spur to which they be attach by pin by means of short lever proceed from the back of the wheel revolve and impart a corresponding motion to the float in some feather wheel the proper motion be give to the rod by means of a eccentric on the ship 's side the action of paddle wheel whether radial or feathering will be more fully describe in the chapter on steam navigation screw engine 121 _ q _ -- what be the principal variety of screw engine -lrb- illustration : fig 27 -rrb- -lrb- illustration : fig 28 -rrb- _ a _ -- the engine employ for the propulsion of screw vessel be divide into two great class -- gear engine and direct act engine and each of these class again have many variety in screw vessel the shaft on which the screw be set require to revolve at a much greater velocity than be require in the case of the paddle shaft of a paddle vessel and in gear engine this necessary velocity of rotation be obtain by the intervention of toothed wheel -- the engine themselves move with the usual velocity of paddle engine whereas in direct act engine the require velocity of rotation be obtain by accelerate the speed of the engine and which be connect immediately to the screw shaft 122 _ q _ -- will you describe some of the principal variety of gear engine _ a _ -- a good many of the gear engine for screw vessel be make in the same manner as land engine with a beam overhead which by means of a connect rod extend downward give motion to the crank shaft on which be set the cog wheel which give motion to pinion on the screw shaft -- the tooth of the wheel be generally of wood and the tooth of the pinion of iron there be usually several wheel on the crank shaft and several pinion on the screw shaft but the tooth of each do not run in the same line but be set a little in advance of one another so as to divide the thickness of the tooth into as many part as there be independent wheel or pinion by this arrangement the wheel work more smoothly than they would otherwise do 123 _ q _ -- what other form be there of gear screw engine _ a _ -- in some case larger and shorter tube may be employ chapter ii heat combustion and steam heat 134 _ q _ -- what be mean by latent heat _ a _ -- by latent heat be mean the heat exist in body which be not discoverable by the touch or by the thermometer but which manifest its existence by produce a change of state heat be absorb in the liquefaction of ice and in the vaporization of water yet the temperature do not rise during either process and the heat absorb be therefore say to become latent the term be somewhat objectionable as the effect proper to the absorption of heat have in each case be make visible and it would be as reasonable to call hot water latent steam latent heat in the present acceptation of the term mean sensible liquefaction or vaporization but to produce these change heat be as necessary as to produce the expansion of mercury in a thermometer tube which be take as the measure of temperature and it be hard to see on what ground heat can be say to be latent when its presence be make manifest by change which only heat can effect it be the _ temperature _ only that be latent and latent temperature mean sensible vaporization or liquefaction 135 _ q _ -- but when you of the water could be prevent or as would raise 1000 time that quantity of water one degree the boiling point of water be 212 degree be 180 degree above the freezing point of water -- the freezing point be 32 degree so that it require 1180 time as much heat to raise 1 lb of water into steam as to raise 1180 lb of water one degree or it require about as much heat to raise a pound of boiling should be thin whereas in locomotive boiler it require to be much thicker if the stratum of coal be thick while the draught be sluggish the carbonic acid result from combustion combine with a additional atom of carbon in pass through the fire and be convert into carbonic oxide which may be define to be invisible smoke as it carry off a portion of the fuel : if on the contrary the stratum of coal be thin while the draught be very rapid a injurious refrigeration be occasion by the excess of air pass through the furnace the fire should always be spread of uniform thickness over the bar of the grate and should be without any hole or uncovered place which greatly diminish the effect of the fuel by the refrigeratory action of the stream of cold air which enter thereby a wood fire require to be about 6 inch thicker than a coal one and a turf fire require to be 3 or 4 inch thicker than a wood one so that the furnace bar must be place lower where wood or turf be burn to enable the surface of the fire to be at the same distance from the bottom of the boiler 148 _ q _ -- be a slow or a rapid combustion the most beneficial _ a _ -- a slow combustion be find by experiment to 1 divide the logarithm of the remainder by 513 and to the quotient add the logarithm 21327940 find the natural number answer to the sum and subtract therefrom the constant 513 the remainder will be the temperature seek the french academy and the franklin institute have repeat mr southern 's experiment on a larger scale the result obtain by they be not widely different and be perhaps nearer the 167 _ q _ -- what expansion do water undergo in its conversion into steam _ a _ -- a cubic inch of water make about a cubic foot of steam of the atmospheric pressure 168 _ q _ -- and how much at a atmosphere a third of a cubic foot with the pressure of three atmosphere and so on in all other proportion high pressure steam indeed be just low pressure steam force into a less space and the pressure will always be great in the proportion in which the space be contract 169 _ q _ -- if this be so the quantity of heat in a give weight of steam must be nearly the same whether the steam be employ for work engine and it may therefore be consider in practice that a pound of steam contain very nearly the same quantity of heat at all pressure 170 _ q _ -- do not the quantity of heat in any satisfactory result -- jb chapter iv mode of estimate the power and performance of engine and boiler horse power 209 _ q _ -- what do you understand by a horse power _ a _ -- a amount of mechanical determine the relation between the power of a certain size of engine and the power of a horse so that when it be desire to supersede the use of horse by the erection of a engine he might from the per minute and divide by 33000 the quotient be the actual number of horse power of the engine the same result be attain by square the diameter of the cylinder multiply by the pressure per square inch this rule however it be necessary to adopt the speed of piston prescribe by mr watt which vary with the length of the stroke the speed of piston with a 2 foot stroke be accord to he system 160 per without inconvenience 216 _ q _ -- how do you ascertain the power of high pressure engine _ a _ -- the actual power be readily ascertain by the indicator by the same process by which the actual power deduction of a pound and a half from the pressure on that account as in the case of low pressure engine high pressure engine it be true have no air pump to work but the deduction of a pound and a half of pressure be relatively a much smaller one where the pressure be high than where it do not much exceed the pressure of the atmosphere the rule therefore for the actual horse power of a high pressure engine will stand thus : square the diameter of the cylinder in inch multiply by the pressure of the steam in the cylinder per square inch less 1-1\/2 lb and by the speed of the piston in foot per minute and divide by 42017 the quotient be the actual horse power 217 _ q _ -- but how do you ascertain the nominal horse power of high pressure engine _ a _ -- the nominal horse power of a high pressure engine have never be define but it should obviously hold the same relation to the actual power as that which obtain in the case of condense engine so that a engine of a give nominal power may be capable of perform the same work whether high pressure or condense this relation be maintain in the follow rule which express the nominal horse power of high pressure engine : multiply the square of the diameter of the cylinder in inch by the cube root of the length of stroke in foot and divide the product by 156 this rule give the nominal power of a high pressure engine three time greater than that of a low pressure engine of the same dimension the average effective pressure be take at 21 lb per square inch instead of 7 lb and the speed of the piston in foot per minute be in both rule there be a small piston move steam tight in a cylinder of which _ d _ be the piston rod and _ e _ a spiral spring of steel which the piston when force upward by the steam or suck downward by the vacuum either compress or extend _ f _ be a cock attach to the cylinder of the indicator and which be screw into the cylinder cover it be obvious that so soon as this cock be open the piston will be force up when the space above the piston of the engine be open to the boiler and suck down when that space be open to the condenser -- in each case to a extent proportionate to the pressure of the steam or the perfection of the vacuum the top of the piston _ c _ be open to the atmosphere a pencil _ p _ with a knife hinge be insert into the piston rod at _ e _ and the point of the pencil bear upon the surface of the paper wound upon the drum a if the drum a do not revolve this pencil would merely trace on the paper a vertical line but as the drum a move round and back again every stroke of the engine and as the pencil move up and down again every stroke of the engine the combined movement trace upon the paper a species of rectangle which be call a indicator diagram and the nature of this diagram determine the nature of the engine 's performance 236 _ q _ -- how do it do this _ a _ -- it be clear that if the pencil be move up instantaneously to the top of its stroke and be also move down instantaneously to the bottom of its stroke and if it remain without fluctuation while at the top and bottom the figure describe by the pencil would be a perfect rectangle of which the vertical height would represent the total pressure of the steam and vacuum and therefore the total pressure urge the piston of the engine but in practice the pencil will neither rise nor fall instantaneously nor will it remain at a uniform height throughout the stroke if the steam be work expansively the pressure will begin to fall so soon as the steam be cut off and at the end of the stroke when the steam come to be discharge the subsidence of pressure will not be instantaneous but will occupy a appreciable time it be clear therefore that in no engine can the diagram describe by a indicator be a complete rectangle but the more nearly it approach to a rectangle the larger will be the power produce at every stroke with any give pressure and the area of the space include within the diagram will in every case accurately represent the power exert by the engine during that stroke 237 _ q _ -- and how be this area ascertain _ a _ -- it may be ascertain in various way but the usual mode be to take the vertical height of the diagram at a number of equidistant point on a base line and then to take the mean of these several height as representative of the mean pressure actually urge the piston now if you have the pressure on the piston per square inch and if you know the number of square inch in its area and the velocity with which it move in foot per minute you have obviously the dynamical effort of the engine or in other word its actual power 238 _ q _ -- how be the base line you have refer to obtain _ a _ -- in proceed to take a indicator diagram the first thing to be do be to allow the barrel to make two or three reciprocation with the pencil rest against it before open the cock attach to the cylinder there will thus be trace a horizontal line which be call the _ atmospheric line _ and in condense engine a part of the diagram will be above and a part of it below this line whereas in high pressure engine the whole of the diagram will be above this line upon this line the vertical ordinate may be set off at equal distance or upon any base line parallel to it but the usual course be to erect the ordinate on the atmospheric line 239 _ q _ -- will wheel work so contrived that by every stroke of the engine a index hand be move forward a certain space whereby the number of stroke make by the engine in any give time be accurately record in most case the motion be communicate by means of a detent -- attach to some reciprocate part of the engine -- to a ratchet wheel which give motion to the other wheel in its slow revolution but it be preferable to derive the motion from some revolving part of the engine by means of a endless screw as where the ratchet be use the detent will sometimes fail to carry it round the proper distance in the counter contrived by mr adie a endless screw work into the rim of two small wheel situate on the same axis but one wheel have a tooth more than the other whereby a differential motion be obtain and the difference in the velocity of the two wheel or they motion upon one another express the number of stroke perform the endless screw be attach to some revolving part of the engine whereby a rotatory motion be impart to it and the wheel into which the screw work hang down from it like a pendulum and be keep stationary by the action of gravity 244 _ q _ -- what be the nature of the vessel the forward thrust of the screw be measure by a dynamometer construct on the principle of a weigh machine in which a small spring pressure at the index will balance a very great pressure where the thrust be employ and in each case the variation of pressure be record by a pencil on a sheet of paper carry forward by suitable mechanism whereby the mean thrust be easily ascertain the tractive force of paddle wheel steamer be ascertain by a dynamometer fix on shore to which the float vessel be attach by a rope sometimes the power of a engine be ascertain by a friction break dynamometer apply to the shaft 345 _ q _ -- what will determine the amount of thrust show by the dynamometer _ a _ -- in locomotive and in paddle steamer it will be determine by the force turn the wheel and by weight at the pump end of the beam raise up the plunger of the cataract by means of a small rod -- the water enter readily through the valve already refer to and when the engine reach the top of the injection valve will slowly open and the engine will make a gradual stroke as it obtain the water necessary for condensation the extent to which the cock be open therefore will regulate the speed with which the engine work so that by the use of the cataract the speed of the engine may be vary to suit the variation in the quantity of water require to be lift from the mine in some case a air cylinder heating and fire grate surface 252 _ q _ -- what be the consideration which must chiefly be attend to in settle the proportion of boiler _ a _ -- in the first place there must be sufficient grate surface to enable the quantity of coal requisite for the production of the steam to be conveniently burnt take into account the intensity of the draught and in the next place there must be a sufficient flue surface readily to absorb the heat thus produce so that there may be no needless waste of heat by the chimney the flue moreover must have such a area and the chimney must be of such dimension as will enable a suitable draught through the fire to be maintain and finally the boiler must be make capable of contain such supplies of water and steam as will obviate inconvenient fluctuation in the water level and abate the risk of water be carry over into the engine with the steam with all these condition the boiler must be as light and compact as possible and must be so contrived as to be capable of be clean and repair with facility 253 _ q _ -- suppose then that you have to proportion a boiler which should be capable of supply steam sufficient to propel a steam be necessary to overcome it i should then be in a position to know what pressure and volume of steam be require to overcome the resistance at the prescribe rate of motion and finally i should allow a sufficient heating and fire grate surface in the boiler accord to the kind of boiler it be to furnish the requisite quantity of steam or in other word to evaporate the requisite quantity of water 254 impair the vacuum and throw a great load upon the air pump which diminish the speed and available power of the engine and the existence of water within the cylinder unless there be safety valve upon the cylinder to permit its escape will very probably cause some part of the machinery to break by suddenly arrest the motion of the piston when it meet the surface of the water -- the slide valve be close to the condenser before the termination of the stroke in all engine with lap upon the valve so that the water within the cylinder be prevent from escape in that direction at the same time the boiler be empty of its water too rapidly for the feed pump to be able to maintain the supply and the flue be in danger of be burn from a deficiency of water above they 295 _ q _ -- what be the cause of priming _ a _ -- the cause of priming be a insufficient amount of steam room a inadequate area of water level a insufficient width between the flue or tube for the ascent of the steam and the descent of water to supply the vacuity the steam occasion and the use of dirty water in the boiler new boiler prime more than old boiler and steamer enter river from the sea be more addict to priming than if sea or river water have alone be use in the boiler -- probably from the boiling point of salt water be higher than that of fresh whereby the salt water act like so much molten metal in raise the fresh water into steam open the safety valve suddenly may make a boiler prime and if the safety valve be situate near the mouth of the steam pipe the spray or foam thus create may be mingle with the steam pass into the engine and materially diminish its effective power but if the safety valve be situate at a distance from the mouth of the steam pipe the quantity of foam or spray passing into the engine may be diminish by open the safety valve and in locomotive therefore it be find beneficial to have a safety valve on the barrel of the boiler at a point remote from the steam chest by partially open which any priming in that part of the boiler adjacent to the steam chest be check and a purer steam than before puss to the engine 296 _ q _ -- what be the proper remedy for priming _ a _ -- when a boiler prime the engineer generally close the throttle valve partially turn off the injection water and open the furnace door whereby the generation of steam be check and a less violent ebullition in the boiler suffice where the priming arise from a insufficient amount of steam room it may be mitigate by put a higher pressure upon the boiler and work more expansively or by the interposition of a perforated plate between the boiler and the steam chest which break the ascend water and liberate the steam in some case however it may be necessary to set a second steam chest on the top of the exist one and it will be preferable to establish a communication with this new chamber by means of a number of small hole bore through the iron plate of the boiler rather than by a single large orifice where priming arise from the existence of dirty water in the boiler the evil may be remedy by the use of collect vessel or by blow off largely from the surface and where it arise from a insufficient area of water level or a insufficient width between the flue for the free ascent of the steam and the descent of the superincumbent water the evil may be abate by the addition of circulate pipe in some part of the boiler which will allow the water to descend freely to the place from whence the steam rise the width of the water space be virtually increase by restrict they function to the transmission of a current of steam and water to the surface it be desirable to arrange the heating surface in such a way that the feed water enter the boiler at its lowest point be heated gradually as it ascend until toward the superior part of the flue it be raise gradually into steam but in all case there will be current in the boiler for which it be proper to provide the steam pipe proceeding to the engine should obviously be attach to the highest point of the steam chest in boiler of every construction 297 _ q _ -- have now state the proportion proper to be adopt for
