with locomotive tender and carriage about 100 ton experience at a speed of 50 mile a hour a resistance of about 3000 lb or about 30 lb per ton which resistance include the resistance of the engine as well as that of the train this therefore be the force which must be impart at the circumference of the drive wheel except that small part intercept by the engine itself and the force exert by the piston must be greater than that at the circumference of the drive wheel in the proportion of they slower motion or in the proportion of the circumference of the drive wheel to the length of a double stroke of the engine if the diameter of the drive wheel be 5-1\/2 foot its circumference will be 17278 foot and if the length of the stroke be 18 inch the length of a double stroke will be 3 foot the pressure on the piston must therefore be greater than the traction at the circumference of the drive wheel in the proportion of 17278 to 3 or in other word the mean pressure on the piston must be 17278 lb and the area of cylinder and pressure of steam must be such as to produce conjointly this total pressure it thus become easy to tell the volume and pressure of steam require which steam in its turn represent its equivalent of water which be to be evaporate from the boiler and the boiler must be so proportion by the rule already give as to evaporate this water freely in the case of a steam vessel the mode of procedure be the same and when the resistance and speed be know it be easy to tell the equivalent value of steam strength of boiler 298 _ q _ -- what strain should the iron of of boiler explosion be undoubtedly too great a pressure of steam or a insufficient strength of boiler but many explosion have also arise from the flue have be suffer to become red hot if the safety valve of a boiler be accidentally jam or if the plate or stay be much worn by corrosion while a high pressure of steam be nevertheless maintain the boiler necessarily burst and if from a insufficiency of water in the boiler or from any other cause the flue become highly heat they may be force down by the pressure of the steam and a partial explosion may be the result the worst explosion be where the shell of the boiler burst but the collapse of a furnace or flue be also very disastrous generally to the person in the engine room and sometimes the shell burst and the flue collapse at the same time for if the flue get red hot and water be throw upon they either by the feed pump or otherwise the generation of steam may be too rapid for the safety valve to permit its escape with sufficient facility and the shell of the boiler may in consequence be rent asunder sometimes the iron of the flue become highly heat in consequence of the improper configuration of the part which by retain the steam in contact with the metal prevent the access of the water : the bottom of large flue upon which the flame beat down be very liable to injury from this cause and the iron of flue thus act upon may be so soften that the flue will collapse upward with the pressure of the steam the flue of boiler may also become red hot in some part from the attachment of scale which from its imperfect conduct power will cause the iron to be unduly heated and if the scale be accidentally detach a partial explosion may occur in consequence 307 _ q _ -- do the contact of water with heated metal occasion a instantaneous generation of steam _ a _ -- it be find that a sudden disengagement of steam do not immediately follow the contact of water with the hot metal for water throw upon red hot iron be not immediately convert into steam but assume the spheroidal form and roll about in globule over the surface these globule however high the temperature of the metal may be on which they be place never rise above the temperature of 205  and give off but very little steam but if the temperature of the metal be lower the water cease to retain the spheroidal form and come into intimate contact with the metal whereby a rapid disengagement of steam take place if water be pour into a very hot copper flask the flask may be cork up as there will be scarce any steam produce so long as the high temperature be maintain but so soon as the temperature be suffer to fall below 350  or 400  the spheroidal condition be no longer maintainable steam be generate with rapidity and the cork will be project from the mouth of the flask with great force 308 _ q _ -- what precaution can be take to prevent boiler explosion _ a _ -- one useful precaution against the explosion of boiler from too great a internal valve of its own the passage lead to which should have no connection with the passage lead to any of the stop valve use to cut off the connection between the boiler so that the action of the safety valve may be make independent of the action of the stop valve in some case stop valve have jam or have be carry from they seat into the mouth of the pipe communicate between they and the action of the pressure in consequence of which the spindle become jam in the guide and from various other cause which it would be tedious to enumerate but the inaction of the safety valve be at once indicate by the the water carry upward by the steam should never be insert as in some case this cone have become loose and close up the mouth of the waste steam pipe whereby the safety valve be render inoperative the one side to avoid be scald by the rush of steam from the furnace there be no time to begin draw the fire in such a emergency and by this treatment the fire though not altogether extinguish will be render incapable of do harm if the flue be already red hot on no account must cold water be suffer to enter the boiler but the heat should be maintain in the furnace and the blow off cock be open or the mud hole door loosen so as to let all the water escape but at the same time the pressure must be keep quite low in the boiler so that there will be no danger of the hot flue collapse with the opposition to the pressure of the atmosphere that the gain in the vacuum do not equal the loss of power occasion by the additional load upon the pump and there be therefore a clear loss by the reduction of the temperature below 100  if such reduction be cause by the admission of a additional quantity of water if the reduction of temperature however be cause by the use of colder water there be a gain produce by it though the gain will within certain limit be greater if advantage be take of the lowness of the temperature to diminish the quantity of injection 334 _ q _ -- how do you determine the proper area of the injection orifice _ a _ -- the area of the injection orifice proper for any engine can easily be tell when the quantity of water requisite to condense the steam be know and the pressure be specify under which the water enter the condenser the vacuum in the condenser may be take at 26 inch of mercury which be equivalent to a column of water 294 ft high and the square root of 294 multiply by 8021 be 4315 which be the velocity in foot per second that a heavy body would acquire in fall 294 ft or with which the water would enter the condenser now if a cubic foot of water evaporate per hour be equivalent to a actual horse power and 289 cubic inch of water be requisite for the condensation of a cubic inch of water in the form of steam 289 cubic foot of condense water per horse power per hour or 13905 cubic inch per second will be necessary for the engine and the size of the injection orifice must be such that this quantity of water flow with the velocity of 4315 ft per second or 5178 inch per second will gain admission to the condenser divide therefore 13905 the number of cubic inch to be inject by 5178 the velocity of influx in inch per second we get 002685 for the area of the orifice in square inch but inasmuch as it have be find by experiment that the actual discharge of water through a hole in a thin plate be only six tenth of the theoretical discharge on account of the contract vein the area of the orifice must be increase in the proportion of such diminution of effect or be make 004475 or 1\/22d of a square inch per horse power this it will be remark be the theoretical area require per actual horse power but as the friction and contraction in the pipe further reduce the discharge the area be make 1\/15th of a square inch per actual horse power or rather per cubic foot of water evaporate from the boiler 335 _ q _ -- can not the condensation of the steam be accomplish by any other means than by the admission of cold water into the condenser _ a _ -- it may be accomplish by the method of external cold as it be call which consist in the application of a large number of thin metallic surface to the condenser on the one side of which the steam circulate while on the other side there be a constant current of cold water and the steam be condensed by come into contact with the cold surface without mingle with the water use for the purpose of refrigeration the first kind of condenser employ by mr watt be construct after this fashion but he find it in practice to be inconvenient from its size and to become fur up or incrust when the water be bad whereby the conduct power of the metal be impaired he therefore revert to the use of the jet of cold water as be upon the whole preferable the jet enter the condenser instead of the cylinder as be the previous practice and this method be now the one in common use some few year ago a good number of steam vessel be fit with hall 's condenser which operate on the principle of external cold and which consist of a faggot of small copper tube surround by water but the use of those condenser have not be persist in and most of the vessel fit with they have return to the ordinary plan 336 _ q _ -- you state that the capacity of the feed pump be 1\/240th of the capacity of the cylinder in the case of condense engine -- the engine be double acting and the pump single acting -- and that in high pressure engine the capacity of the pump should be greater in proportion to the pressure of the steam can you give any rule that will express the proper capacity for the feed pump at all pressure _ a _ -- that will not be difficult in low pressure engine the pressure in the boiler may be take at 5 lb above the atmospheric pressure or 20 lb altogether and as high pressure steam be merely low pressure steam compress into a smaller compass the size of the feed pump in relation to the size of the cylinder must obviously vary in the direct proportion of the pressure and if it be 1\/240th of the capacity of the cylinder when the total pressure of the steam be 20 lb it must be 1\/120th of the capacity of the cylinder when the pressure be 40 lb per square inch or 25 lb per square inch above the atmospheric pressure this law of variation be express by the follow rule : -- multiply the capacity of the cylinder in cubic inch by the total pressure of the steam in lb per square inch or the pressure per square inch on the safety valve plus 15 and divide the product by 4800 the quotient be the capacity of the feed pump in cubic inch when the feed pump be single act and the engine double act if the feed pump be double acting or the engine single act the capacity of the pump must just be one half of what be give by this rule 337 _ q _ -- but should not some addition be make to the size of pump thus obtain if the pump work at a high rate of speed _ a _ -- no this rule make allowance for defective action all pump lift much less water than be due to the size of they barrel and the number of they stroke moderately good pump lose 50 per cent of they theoretical effect and bad pump 80 per cent 338 _ q _ -- to what be this loss of effect to be chiefly ascribe _ a _ -- mainly to the inertia of the water which if the pump piston be draw up very rapidly can not follow it with sufficient rapidity so that there may be a vacant space between the piston and the water and at the return stroke the momentum of the water in the pipe expend itself in give a reverse motion to the column of water approach the pump messr kirchweger and prusman of hanover have investigate this subject by apply a revolving cock at the end of a pipe lead from a elevated cistern contain water and the water escape at every revolution of the cock in the same manner as if a pump be draw it with a column of water of 17 foot they find that at 80 revolution of the cock per minute the water deliver per minute by the cock be 945 gallon but with 140 revolution of the cock per minute the water deliver per minute by the cock be only 542 gallon they subsequently apply a air vessel to the pipe beside the cock when the discharge rise to 129 gallon per minute with 80 revolution and 1828 gallon with 140 revolution air vessel should therefore be apply to the suction side of fast move pump and this be now do with good result 339 _ q _ -- what be the usual dimension the cylinder of steam engine _ a _ -- in low pressure engine the thickness of metal of the cylinder in engine of a medium size should be about 1\/40th of the diameter of the cylinder which with a strength over other part and it appear expedient that this disparity should be diminish which may best be do by increase the strength of the part which be weakest inasmuch as the frequent fracture of some of the part show that the dimension at present adopt for those part be scarcely sufficient unless the iron of which they be make be of the best quality at the same time it be quite certain that engine proportion by these rule will work satisfactorily where good material be employ but it be important to know in what part good material and larger dimension be the most indispensable in many of the part moreover it be necessary that the dimension should be proportion to meet the wear and the tendency to heat instead of be merely proportion to obtain the necessary strength and the crank pin to 367 -rrb- the pressure on the piston in lb per square inch be take as the sum of the pressure of steam in the boiler and of the vacuum the latter be assume to be 15 lb per square inch chapter vii constructive detail of boiler \* \* \* \* \* land and marine boiler 369 _ q _ -- will you explain the course of procedure in the construction and setting of wagon boiler _ a _ -- most boiler be make of plate three eighth of a inch thick and the rivet be from three eighth to three fourth of a inch in diameter in the bottom and side of a wagon boiler the head of the rivet or the end form on the rivet before they be insert should be large and place next the fire or on the outside whereas on the top of the boiler the head should be on the inside the rivet should be place about two inch distant from center to center and the center of the row of rivet should be about one inch from the edge of the plate the edge of the plate should be truly cut both inside and outside and after the part of the boiler have be rivet together the edge of the plate should be set up or caulk with a blunt chisel about a quarter of a inch thick in the point and strike by a hammer of about three or four pound weight one man hold the caulking tool while another strike 370 _ q _ -- be this the usual mode of caulking _ a _ -- no it be not the usual mode but it be the best mode and be the mode adopt by mr watt the usual mode now be for one man to caulk the seam with a hammer in one hand and a caulking chisel in the other and in some of the difficult corner of marine flue boiler it be not easy for two man to get in a good deal of the caulking have also sometimes to be do with the left hand 371 _ q _ -- should the boiler be prove after caulk _ a _ -- the boiler should be fill with water and caulk afresh in any leaky part when empty again all the joint should be paint with a solution of sal ammoniac in urine and so soon as the seam be well rust they should be dry with a gentle fire and then be paint over with a thin putty form of whiting and linseed oil the heat be continue until the putty become so hard that it can not be readily scratch with the nail and care must be take neither to burn the putty nor to discontinue the fire until it have become quite dry 372 _ q _ -- how should the brickwork setting of a wagon boiler be build _ a _ -- in build the brickwork for the setting of the boiler the part upon which the heat act with most intensity be to be build with clay instead of mortar but mortar be to be use on the outside of the work old bar of flat iron may be lay under the boiler chime to prevent that part of the boiler from be burn out and bar of iron should also run through the brickwork to prevent it from splitting the top of the boiler be to be cover with brickwork lay in the best lime and if the lime be not of the hydraulic kind it should be mix with dutch terrass to make it impenetrable to water the top of the boiler should be well plaster with this lime which will greatly conduce to the tightness of the seam opening into the flue must be leave in convenient situation to enable the flue to be sweep out when require and these opening may be close with cast iron door joint with clay or mortar which may be easily remove when require adjacent to the chimney a slit must be leave in the top of the flue with a groove in the brickwork to enable the slide door or damper to be fix in that situation which by be lower into the flue will obstruct the passage of the smoke and moderate the draught whereby the chimney will be prevent from draw the flame into it before the heat have act sufficiently upon the boiler 373 _ q _ -- be marine construct in the same way as land boiler _ a _ -- there be very little difference in the two case : the whole of the shell of marine boiler however should be double rivet with rivet 11\/16ths of a inch in diameter and 2-3\/8 th inch from center to center the weakening effect of double riveting be much less than that of single riveting the furnace above the line of bar should be of the best lowmoor bowling or staffordshire scrap plate and the portion of each furnace above the bar should consist only of three plate one for the top and one for each side the lower seam of the side plate be situate beneath the level of the bar so as not to be expose to the heat of the furnace the tube plate of tubular boiler should be of the best lowmoor or bowling iron seven eighth to one inch thick : the shell should be of the best staffordshire or thornycroft s crown iron 7\/16ths of a inch thick 374 _ q _ -- of what kind of iron should the angle iron or corner iron be compose _ a _ -- angle iron should not be use in the construction of boiler as in the manufacture it become reedy and be apt to split up in the direction of its length : it be much the safer practice to bend the plate at the corner of the boiler but this must be carefully do without introduce any more sharp bend than can be avoid and plate which require to be bent much should be of lowmoor iron it will usually be find expedient to introduce a ring of angle iron around the furnace mouth though it be discard in the other part of the boiler but it should be use as sparingly as possible and any that be use should be of the best quality 375 _ q _ -- be it not important to have the hole in the plate opposite to one another _ a _ -- the whole of the plate of a boiler should have the hole for the rivet punch and the edge cut straight by means of self-acting machinery in which a travel table carry forward the plate with a equal progression every stroke of the punch or shears and machinery of this kind be now extensively employ the practice of force the part of boiler together with violence by means of screw-jack and drift through the hole should not be permit as a great strain may thus be throw upon the rivet even when there be no steam in the boiler all rivet should be of the best lowmoor iron the work should be caulk both within and without wherever it be accessible but in the more confine situation within the flue the caulking will in many case have to be do with the hand or chip hammer instead of the heavy hammer previously prescribe 376 _ q _ -- how be the setting of marine boiler with internal furnace effect _ a _ -- in the setting of marine boiler care must be take that no copper bolt or nail project above the wooden platform upon which they rest and also that no project copper bolt in the side of the ship touch the boiler as the galvanic action in such a case would probably soon wear the point of contact into hole the platform may consist of three inch plank lay across the keelson nail with iron nail the head of which be well punch down and caulk and putty like a deck the surface may then be paint over with thin putty and fore and aft board of half the thickness may then be lay down and nail securely with iron nail have the head well punch down this platform must then be cover thinly and evenly with mastic cement and the boiler be set down upon it and the cement must be caulk beneath the boiler by means of wooden caulking tool so as completely to fill every vacuity cooming of wood slope on the top must next be set round the boiler and the space between the cooming and the boiler must be caulk full of cement and be smooth off on the top to the slope of the cooming so as to throw off any water that might be dispose to enter between the cooming and the boiler 377 _ q _ -- how be the cement use for set marine boiler compound _ a _ -- mastic cement proper for the setting of boiler be sell in many place ready make hamelin 's mastic be compound as follow : -- to any give weight of sand or pulverize earthenware add two third such give weight of powdered bath portland or other similar stone and to every 560 lb weight of the mixture add 40 lb weight of litharge 2 lb of powdered glass or flint 1 lb of minium and 2 lb of gray oxide of lead pass the mixture through a sieve and keep it in a powder for use when want for use a sufficient quantity of the powder be mix with some vegetable oil upon a board or in a trough in the manner of mortar in the proportion of 605 lb of the powder to 5 gallon of linseed walnut or pink oil and the mixture be stir and trodden upon until it assume the appearance of moistened sand when it be ready for use the cement should be use on the same day as the oil be add else it will be set into a solid mass 378 _ q _ -- what be the best length of the furnace of marine boiler _ a _ -- it have already be state that furnace bar should not much exceed six foot in length as it be difficult to manage long furnace but it be a frequent practice to make the furnace long and narrow the consequence of which be that it be impossible to fire they effectually at the after end especially upon long voyage and in stormy weather and air escape into the flue at the after end of the bar whereby the efficacy of the boiler be diminish where the bar be very long it will generally be find that a increase supply of steam and a diminish consumption of coal will be the consequence of shorten they and the bar should always lie with a considerable inclination to facilitate the distribution of the fuel over the after part of the furnace when there be two length of bar in the furnace it be expedient to make the central cross bar for bear up the end double and to leave a space between the end of the bar so that the ash may fall through between they the space thus leave enable the bar to expand without injury on the application of heat whereas without some such provision the bar be very liable to get burn out by bend up in the center or at the end as they must do if the elongation of the bar on the application of heat be prevent and this must be the effect of permit the space at the end of the bar to be fill up with ash at each end of each bed of bar it be expedient to leave a space which the ash can not fill up so as to cause the bar to jam and care must be take that the heel of the bar do not come against any of the furnace bearer whereby the room leave at the end of the bar to permit the expansion would be render of no avail 379 _ q _ -- have you any remark to offer respect the construction and arrangement of the furnace bridge and damper of marine boiler _ a _ -- the furnace bridge of marine boiler be wall or partition build up at the end of the furnace to narrow the opening for the escape of heat into the flue they be either make of fire brick or of plate iron contain water : in the case of water bridge the top part of the bridge should be make with a large amount of slant so as to enable the steam to escape freely but notwithstanding this precaution the plate of water bridge be apt to crack at the bend so that fire brick bridge appear on the whole to be preferable in shallow furnace the bridge often come too near the furnace top to enable a man to pass over they and it will save expense if in such bridge the upper portion be construct of two or three fire block which may be lift off where a person require to enter the flue to sweep or repair they whereby the perpetual demolition and reconstruction of the upper part of the bridge will be prevent 380 _ q _ -- what be the benefit of bridge _ a _ -- bridge be find in practice to have a very sensible operation in increase the production of steam and in some boiler in which the brick bridge have be accidentally knock down by the fireman a very considerable diminution in the supply of steam have be experience they chief operation seem to lie in concentrate the heat within the furnace to a higher temperature whereby the heat be more rapidly transmit from the furnace to the water and less heat have consequently to be absorb by the flue in this way the bridge render the heating surface of a boiler more effective or enable a smaller amount of heating surface to suffice 381 _ q _ -- be the bridge behind the furnace the only bridge use in steam boiler _ a _ -- it be not a uncommon practice to place a hang bridge consist of a plate of iron descend a certain distance into the flue at that part of the flue where it enter the chimney whereby the stratum of hot air which occupy the highest part of the flue be keep in protracted contact with the boiler and the cooler air occupy the lower part of the flue be that which alone escape the practice of introduce a hang bridge be a beneficial one in the case of some boiler but be not applicable universally as boiler with a small calorimeter can not be further contract in the flue without a diminution in they evaporate power in tubular boiler a hanging bridge be not applicable but in some case a perforated plate be place against the end of the tube which by suitable connection be make to operate as a slide damper which partially or totally close up the end of every tube and at other time a damper construct in the manner of a venetian blind be employ in the same situation these variety of damper however have only yet be use in locomotive boiler though applicable to tubular boiler of every description 382 _ q _ -- be it a benefit to keep the flue or tube appertain to each furnace distinct _ a _ -- in a flue boiler this can not be do but in a tubular boiler it be a advantage that there should be a division between the tube pertain to each furnace so that the smoke of each furnace may be keep apart from the smoke of the furnace adjoining it until the smoke of both enter the chimney as by this arrangement a furnace only will be render inoperative in clean the fire instead of a boiler and the tube belong to one furnace may be sweep if necessary at sea without interfere injuriously with the action of the rest in a steam vessel it be necessary at interval to empty out one or more furnace every watch to get rid of the clinker which would otherwise accumulate in they and it be advisable that the connection between the furnace should be such that this operation when be perform on one furnace shall injure the action of the rest as little as possible 383 _ q _ -- can any constructive precaution be take to prevent the furnace and tube plate of the boiler from be burn by the intensity of the heat _ a _ -- the side of the internal furnace or flue in all boiler should be so construct that the steam may readily escape from they surface with which view it be expedient to make the bottom of the flue somewhat wider than the top or slightly conical in the cross section and the upper plate should always be overlap by the plate beneath so that the steam can not be retain in the overlap but will escape as soon as it be generate if the side of the furnace be make high and perfectly vertical they will speedily be buckle and crack by the heat as a film of steam in such a case will remain in contact with the iron which will prevent the access of the water and the iron of the boiler will be injure by the high temperature it must in that case acquire to moderate the intensity of the heat act upon the furnace side it be expedient to bring the outside fire bar into close contact with the side of the furnace so as to prevent the entrance of air through the fire in that situation by which the intensity of the heat would be increase the tube plate nearest the furnace in tubular boiler should also be so inclined as to facilitate the escape of the steam and the short bent plate or flange of the tube plate connect the tube plate with the top of the furnace should be make with a gradual bend as if the bend be sudden the iron will be apt to crack or burn away from the concretion of salt where the furnace mouth be contract by bend in the side and top of the furnace as be the general practice the bend should be gradual as salt be apt to accumulate in the pocket make by a sudden bend and the plate will then burn into hole 384 _ q _ -- in what manner be the tubing of boiler perform _ a _ -- the tube of marine boiler be generally iron tube three inch in diameter and between six and seven foot long but sometimes brass tube of similar dimension be employ when brass tube be employ the use of ferule drive into the end of the tube be sometimes employ to keep they tight but when the tube be of malleable iron of the thickness of russell 's boiler tube they may be make tight merely by firmly drive they into the tube plate and the same may be do with thick brass tube the hole in the tube plate next the front of the boiler be just sensibly larger in diameter than the hole in the other tube plate and the hole upon the outer surface of both tube plate be very slightly countersunk the whole of the tube be drive through both tube plate from the front of the boiler -- the precaution however be take to drive they in gently at first with a light hand hammer until the whole of the tube have be insert to a equal depth and then they may be drive up by degree with a heavy hammer whereby any distortion of the hole from unequal driving will be prevent finally the end of the tube should be rivet up so as to fill the countersink the tube should be leave a little longer than the distance between the outer surface of the tube plate so that the countersink at the end may be fill by stave up the end of the tube rather than by riveting it over and the stave will be best accomplish by means of a mandril with a collar upon it which be drive into the tube so that the collar rest upon the end of the tube to be rivet or a tool like a blunt chisel with a recess in its point may be use as be the more usual practice 385 _ q _ -- should not stay be introduce in substitution of some of the tube _ a _ -- it appear expedient in all case that some of the tube should be screw at the end so as to serve as stay if the riveting at the tube end happen to be burn away and also to act as abutment to the rivet tube -- or else to introduce very strong rod of about the same diameter as a tube in substitution of some of the tube and these stay should have nut at each end both within and without the tube plate which nut should be screw up with white lead interpose before the tube be insert if the tube be long they expansion when the boiler be be blow off will be apt to start they at the end unless very securely fix and it be difficult to prevent brass tube of large diameter and proportionate length from be start at the end even when secure by ferule but the brass tube commonly employ be so small as to be susceptible of sufficient compression endway by the adhesion due to the ferule to compensate for the expansion whereby they be prevent from start at the end in some of the early marine boiler fit with brass tube a galvanic action at the end of the tube be find to take place and the iron of the tube plate be waste away in consequence with rapidity but further experience prove the injury to be attributable chiefly to imperfect fitting whereby a leakage be cause that induce oxidation and when the tube be well fit any injurious action at the end of the tube be find to cease 386 _ q _ -- what be the best mode of construct the chimney and the part in connection therewith _ a _ -- in sea-going steamer the funnel plate be usually about nine foot long and 3\/16ths thick and where different flue or boiler have they debouch in the same chimney it be expedient to run division plate up the chimney for a considerable distance to keep the draught distinct the damper should not be in the chimney but at the end of the boiler flue so that they may be available for use if the funnel by accident be carry away the waste steam pipe should be of the same height as the funnel so as to carry the waste steam clear of it for if the waste steam strike the funnel it will wear the iron into hole and the waste steam pipe should be make at the bottom with a faucet joint to prevent the working of the funnel when the vessel roll from break the pipe at the neck there should be two hoop round the funnel for the attachment of the funnel shroud instead of one so that the funnel may not be carry overboard if one hoop break or if the funnel break at the upper hoop from the corrosive action of the waste steam as sometimes happen the deck over the steam chest should be form of a iron plate support by angle iron beam and there should be a high angle iron cooming round the hole in the deck through which the chimney ascend to prevent any water upon the deck from leak down upon the boiler around the lower part of the funnel there should be a sheet iron case to prevent any inconvenient dispersion of heat in that situation and another short piece of casing of a somewhat larger diameter and rivet to the chimney should descend over the first casing so as to prevent the rain or spray which may beat against the chimney from be pour down within the case upon the top of the boiler the pipe for conduct away the waste water from the top of the safety valve should lead overboard and not into the bilge of the ship as inconvenience arise from the steam occasionally pass through it if it have its termination in the engine room 387 _ q _ -- be not the chimney of some vessel make so that they may be lower when require _ a _ -- the chimney of small river vessel which have to pass under bridge be generally form with a hinge so that they may be lower backward when pass under a bridge and the chimney of some screw standing piece on deck which however do not project above the bulwark 388 _ q _ -- will you explain any further detail in the construction of marine boiler which occur to you as important _ a _ -- the the hole in the tube plate and the tube should not be place too close together else they heating efficacy will be impaired incrustation and corrosion of boiler 389 _ q _ -- what be the cause of the formation of scale in marine boiler _ a _ -- scale be form in all boiler which contain earthy or saline matter just in the way in which a scaly deposit or rock as it be sometimes term be form in a tea kettle in sea water the chief ingredient be common salt which exist in solution : the water admit to the boiler be take away in the shape of steam and the saline matter which be not vaporizable accumulate in process of time in the boiler until its amount be so great that the water be saturated or unable to hold any more in solution the salt be then precipitated and form a deposit which harden by heat the formation of scale therefore be similar to the process of make salt from sea water by evaporation the boiler be in fact a large salt pan 390 _ q _ -- but be the scale soluble in fresh water like the salt in a salt pan _ a _ -- no it be not or if soluble at all be only so to a very limited extent the several ingredient in sea water begin to be precipitate from solution at give it its insoluble character piece of waste or other similar object leave within a marine boiler appear when take out as if they have be petrified and the scale deposit upon the flue of a marine
