of the rapid corrosion of marine boiler _ a _ -- marine boiler be corrode externally in the region of the steam chest by the drip of water from the deck the bottom of the boiler be corrode by the action of the bilge water and the ash pit by the practice of quench the ash with salt water these source of injury however admit of easy remedy the top of the boiler may be preserve from external corrosion by cover it with feel upon which be lay sheet lead solder at every joint so as to be impenetrable to water the ash pit may be shield by guard plate which be plate fitting into the ash pit and attach to the boiler by a few bolt so that when wear they may be remove and new one substitute whereby any wear upon the boiler in that part will be prevent and there will be very little wear upon the bottom of a boiler if it be imbed in mastic cement lay upon a suitable platform 401 _ q _ -- be not marine boiler subject to internal corrosion _ a _ -- yes the greatest part of the corrosion of a boiler take place in the inside of the steam chest and the origin of this corrosion be one of the obscurest subject in the whole range of engineering it can not be from the chemical action of the salt water upon the iron for the flue and other part of the boiler beneath the water suffer very little from corrosion and in steam vessel provide with hall 's condenser which supply the boiler with fresh water not much increase durability of the boiler have be experience nevertheless marine boiler seldom last more than for 5 or 6 year whereas land boiler make of the same quality of iron often last 18 or 20 year and it do not appear probable that land boiler would last a very much shorter time if salt water be use in they the thin film of scale spread over the part of a marine boiler situate beneath the water effectually protect they from corrosion and when the other part be completely wear out the flue generally remain so perfect that the hammer mark upon they be as conspicuous as at they first formation the operation of the steam in corrode the interior of the boiler be most capricious -- the part which be most rapidly wear away in one boiler be untouch in another and in some case one side of a steam chest will be very much waste away while the opposite side remain uninjured sometimes the iron exfoliate in the shape of a black oxide which come away in flake like the leaf of a book while in other case the iron appear as if eat away by a strong acid which have a solvent action upon it the application of feel to the outside of a boiler have in several case be find to accelerate sensibly its internal corrosion boiler in which there be a large accumulation of scale appear to be more corroded than where there be no such deposit and where the funnel pass through the steam chest the iron of the steam chest be invariably much more corroded than where the funnel do not pass through it 402 _ q _ -- can you suggest no reason for the rapid internal corrosion of marine boiler _ a _ -- the fact which i have enumerate appear to indicate that the internal corrosion of marine boiler be attributable chiefly to the existence of surcharged steam within they which be steam to which a additional quantity of heat have be communicate subsequently to its generation so that its temperature be greater than be due to its elastic force and on this hypothesis the observe fact relative to corrosion become to some extent explicable feel apply to the outside of a boiler may accelerate its internal corrosion by keep the steam in a surcharged state when by the dispersion of a part of the heat it would cease to be in that state boiler in which there be a large accumulation of scale must have work with the water very salt which necessarily produce surcharged steam for the temperature of steam can not be less than that of the water from which it be generate and inasmuch as the boiling point of water under any give pressure rise with the saltness of the water the temperature of the steam must rise with the saltness of the water the pressure remain the same or in other word the steam must have a higher temperature than be due to its elastic force or be in the state of surcharged steam the circumstance of the chimney flue pass through the steam will manifestly surcharge the steam with heat so that all the circumstance which be find to accelerate corrosion be it appear such as would also induce the formation of surcharged steam 403 _ q _ -- be it the natural effect of surcharged steam to waste away iron _ a _ -- it be the natural effect of surcharged steam to oxidate the iron with which it be in contact as be illustrate by the familiar process for make hydrogen gas by send steam through a red hot tube fill with piece of iron and although the action of the surcharged steam in a boiler be necessarily very much weaker than where the iron be red hot it manifestly must have _ some _ oxidize effect and the amount of corrosion produce may be very material where the action be perpetual boiler with a large extent of heating surface or with descend flue circulate through the cooler water in the bottom of the boiler before ascend the chimney will be less corroded internally than boiler in which a large quantity of the heat pass away in the smoke and the corrosion of the boiler will be diminish if the interior of any flue pass through the steam be coat with fire brick so as to present the transmission of the heat in that situation the best practice however appear to consist in the transmission of the smoke through a suitable passage on the outside of the boiler so as to supersede the necessity of carry any flue through the steam at all or a column of water may be carry round the chimney into which as much of the feed water may be introduce as the heat of the chimney be capable of raise to the boiling point as under this limitation the presence of feed water around the chimney in the steam chest will fail to condense the steam 404 _ q _ -- in steam vessel there be usually several boiler _ a _ -- yes in steam vessel of considerable power and size 405 _ q _ -- be these boiler generally so construct that any one of they may be throw out of use _ a _ -- marine boiler be now generally supply with stop valve whereby one boiler may be throw out of use without impair the efficacy of the remainder these stop valve be usually spindle valve of large size and they be for the most part set in a pipe which run across the steam chest connect the several boiler together the spindle of these valve should project through stuff box in the cover of the valve chest and they should be balance by a weighted lever and keep in continual action by the steam if the valve be lift up and be suffer to remain up as be the usual practice they will become fix by corrosion in that position and it will be impossible after some time to shut they on a emergency these valve should always be easily accessible from the engine room and it ought not to be necessary for the coal box to be empty to gain access to they 406 _ q _ -- should each boiler have at least one safety valve for itself _ a _ -- yes it would be quite unsafe without this provision as the stop valve might possibly jam sometimes valve jam from a distortion in the shape of the boiler when a considerable pressure be put upon it 407 _ q _ -- how be the admission of the water into the boiler regulate _ a _ -- the admission of feed water into the boiler be regulate by hand by the engineer by means of cock and sometimes by spindle valve raise and lower by a screw cock appear to be the preferable expedient as they be less liable to accident or derangement than screw valve and in modern steam vessel they be generally employ 408 _ q _ -- at what point of the boiler be the feed introduce _ a _ -- the feed water be usually conduct from the feed cock to a point near the bottom of the boiler by means of a internal pipe the object of this arrangement be to prevent the rise steam from be condensed by the enter water by be introduce near the bottom of the boiler the water come into contact in the first place with the bottom of the furnace and flue and extract heat from they which could not be extract by water of a higher temperature whereby a saving of fuel be accomplish in some case the feed water be introduce into a case around the chimney from whence it descend into the boiler this plan appear to be a expedient one when the boiler be short of heating surface and more than a usual quantity of heat ascend the chimney but in well proportioned boiler a water case round the chimney be superfluous when a water casing be use the boiler be generally feed by a head of water the feed water be force up into a small tank from whence it descend into the boiler by the force of gravity while the surplus run to waste as in the feeding apparatus of land engine 409 _ q _ -- suppose that the engineer should shut off the feed water from the boiler while the engine be work what would be the result _ a _ -- the result would be to burst the feed pipe except for a safety valve place on the feed pipe between the engine and the boiler which safety valve open when any undue pressure come upon the pipe and allow the water to escape there be however generally a cock on the suction side of the feed pump which regulate the quantity of water draw into the pump but there must be cock on the boiler also to determine into which boiler the water shall be chiefly discharge and these cock be sometimes all shut accidentally at the same time 410 _ q _ -- be there no expedient in use in steam vessel for enable the position of the water level in the boiler to determine the quantity of feed water admit _ a _ -- in some steam vessel float have be introduce to regulate the feed but they action can not be depend on in agitate water if apply after the common fashion float would probably answer if place in a cylinder which communicate with the water in the boiler by means of small hole and a disc of metal might be attach to the end of a rod extend beneath the water level so as to resist irregular movement from the motion of the ship at sea which would otherwise impair the action of the apparatus 411 _ q _ -- how be the proper level of the water in the boiler of a steam vessel maintain when the engine be stop for some time and the boiler be blow off steam _ a _ -- by means of a separate pump work sometimes by hand but usually by a small separate engine call the donkey engine this pump by the aid of suitable cock will pump from the sea into the boiler from the sea upon deck either to wash deck or to extinguish fire and from the bilge overboard through a suitable orifice in the side of the ship locomotive boiler 412 _ q _ -- will you recapitulate the general feature of locomotive boiler _ a _ -- locomotive boiler consist of three portion -lrb- see fig 29 -rrb- : the barrel e e contain the tube the fire box b and the smoke box f of which the barrel smoke box and external fire box be always of iron but the internal fire box be generally make of copper though sometimes also it be make of iron the tube be sometimes of iron but generally of brass fix in by ferule the whole of the iron plate of a locomotive boiler which be subject to the pressure of steam should be lowmoor or bowling plate of the best quality and the copper should be coarse grain rather than rich or soft and be perfectly free from irregularity of structure and lamination 413 _ q _ -- what be the usual dimension of the barrel _ a _ -- the thickness of the plate compose the barrel of the boiler vary generally from 5\/16ths to 3\/8ths of a inch and the plate should run in the direction of the circumference so that the fiber of the iron may be in the direction of the strain the diameter of the barrel commonly vary from 3 ft to 3 ft 6 inch the diameter of the rivet should be from 11\/16ths to 3\/4ths of a inch and the pitch of the rivet or distance between they centre should be from 17\/8th to 2 inch 414 _ q _ -- how be the fire box of a locomotive construct _ a _ -- the space between the external and internal fire box form a water space which must be stay every 4-1\/2 or 5 inch by means of copper or iron stay bolt screw through the outer fire box into the metal of the inner fire box and securely rivet within it : iron stay bolt be as durable as copper and they superior tenacity give they a advantage sometimes tube be employ as stay the internal and external fire box be join together at the bottom by a n-shaped iron and round the fire door they be connect by means of a copper ring 1-1\/4 in thick and 2 in broad -- the inner fire box be dish sufficiently outward at that point and the outer fire box sufficiently inward to enable a circle of rivet 3\/4 of a inch in diameter pass through the copper ring and the two thickness of iron to make a water-tight joint the thickness of the plate compose the external fire box be in general 3\/8ths of a inch if the fire box be circular and from 3\/8ths to 1\/2 inch if the fire box be square and the thickness of the internal fire box be in most case 7\/16ths if copper and from 3\/8ths to 7\/16ths of a inch if of iron circular internal fire box if make of iron should be weld rather than rivet as the rivet head be liable to be burn away by the action of the fire and when the fire box be square each side should consist of a single plate turn over at the edge with a radius of 3 inch for the introduction of the rivet 415 _ q _ -- be there any provision for stiffen the crown of the furnace in a locomotive _ a _ -- the roof of the internal fire box whether flat as in stephenson 's engine or dome shape as in bury 's require to be stiffen with cross stay bar but the bar require to be stronger and more numerous when apply to a flat surface the end of these stay bar rest above the vertical side of the fire box and to the stay bar thus extend across the crown the crown be attach at interval by means of stay bolt there be project boss upon the stay bar encircle the bolt at every point where a bolt go through but in the other part they be keep clear of the fire box crown so as to permit the access of water to the metal and with the view of facilitate the ascent of the steam the bottom of each stay bar should be sharpen away in those part where it do not touch the boiler 416 _ q _ -- be any inconvenience experience from the intense heat in a locomotive furnace _ a _ -- the fire bar in locomotive have always be a source of trouble as from the intensity of the heat in the furnace they become so hot as to throw off a scale and to bend under the weight of the fuel the best alleviation of these evil lie in make the bar deep and thin : 4 or 5 inch deep by five eighth of a inch thick on the upper side and three eighth of a inch on the under side be find in practice to be good dimension in some locomotive a frame carry a number of fire bar be make so that it may be drop suddenly by loosen a catch but it be find that any such mechanism can rarely be long keep in work order as the molten clinker by run down between the frame and the boiler will generally glue the frame into its place it be therefore find preferable to fix the frame and to lift up the bar by the dart use by the stoker when any cause require the fire to be withdraw the furnace bar of locomotive be always make of malleable iron and indeed for every species of boiler malleable iron bar be to be prefer to bar of cast iron as they be more durable and may if thin be set closer together whereby the small coal or coke be save that would otherwise fall into the ash pit the ash box of locomotive be make of plate iron a quarter thick : it should not be less than 10 in deep and its bottom should be about 9 in above the level of the rail the chimney of a locomotive be make of plate iron one eighth of a inch thick : it be usually of the same diameter as the cylinder but be better smaller and must not stand more than 14 ft high above the level of the rail 417 _ q _ -- be locomotive boiler provide with a steam chest _ a _ -- the upper portion of the external fire box be usually form into a steam chest which be sometimes dome shaped sometimes semicircular and sometimes of a pyramidical form and from this steam chest the steam be conduct away by a internal pipe to the cylinder but in other case a independent steam chest be set upon the barrel of the boiler consist of a plate iron cylinder 20 inch in diameter 2 foot high and three eighth of a inch thick with a dome shape top and with the seam weld and the edge turn over to form a flange of attachment to the boiler the pyramidical dome of the form employ in stephenson 's locomotive present a considerable extent of flat surface to the pressure of the steam and this flat surface require to be very strongly stay with angle iron and tension rod whereas the semiglobular dome of the kind employ in bury 's engine require no stay whatever latterly however these dome over the fire box have be either much reduce in size or abandon altogether 418 _ q _ -- be any beneficial use make of the surplus steam of a locomotive _ a _ -- to save the steam which be form when the engine be stationary a pipe be usually fit to the boiler which on a cock be turn conduct the steam into the water in the tender whereby the feed water be heated and less fuel be subsequently require this method of dispose of the surplus steam may be adopt when the locomotive be descend incline or on any occasion where more steam be produce than the engine can consume 419_q _ -- what means be provide to facilitate the inspection and cleaning of locomotive boiler _ a _ -- the man hole or entrance into the boiler consist of a circular or oval aperture of about 15 in diameter place in bury 's locomotive at the apex of the dome and in stephenson 's upon the front of the boiler a few inch below the level of the round part and the cover of the man hole in bury 's engine contain the safety valve seat in whatever situation this man hole be place the surface of the ring encircle the hole and of the internal part of the door or cover should be accurately fit together by scrape or grind so that they need only the interposition of a little red lead to make they quite tight when screw together lead or canvas joint if of any considerable thickness will not long withstand the action of high pressure steam and the whole of the joint about a locomotive should be such that they require nothing more than a little paint or putty or a ring of wire gauze smear with white or red lead to make they perfectly tight there must be a mud hole opposite the edge of each water space if the fire box be square to enable the boiler to be easily clean out and these hole be most conveniently close by screw plug make slightly taper a cock for empty the boiler be usually fix at the bottom of the fire box and it should be so place as to be accessible when the engine be at work in order that the engine driver may blow off some water if necessary but it must not be in such a position as to send the water blow off among the machinery as it might carry sand or grit into the bearing to they manifest injury 420 _ q _ -- will you state the dimension of the tube plate and the means of secure the tube in it _ a _ -- the tube plate be generally make from five eighth to three fourth of a inch thick but seven eighth of a inch thick appear to be preferable as when the plate be thick the hole will not be so liable to change they figure during the process of ferule the tube : the distance between the tube should never be make less than three fourth of a inch and the hole should be slightly taper so as to enable the tube to hold the tube plate together the tube be secure in the tube plate by means of taper ferule drive into the end of the tube the ferule be for the most part make of steel at the fire box end and of work iron at the smoke box end though ferule of malleable cast iron have in some case be use with advantage : malleable cast iron ferule be almost as easily expand when hammer cold upon a mandrel as the common work iron one be at a work heat spring steel roll with a feather edge to facilitate its conversion into ferule be supply by some of the steel-maker of sheffield and it appear expedient to make use of steel thus prepare when steel ferule be employ in case where ferule be not employ it may be advisable to set out the tube behind the tube plate by means of a expand mandrel there be various form of this instrument one form be that know as prosser 's expand mandrel in which there be six or eight segment which be force out by means of a hexagonal or octagonal wedge which be force forward by a screw when the wedge be withdraw the segment collapse sufficiently to enable they to enter the tube and there be a annular protuberance on the exterior circle of the segment which protuberance when the mandrel be put into the tube just come behind the inner edge of the tube plate when the wedge be tighten up by the screw the protuberance on the exterior of the segment compose the mandrel cause a corresponding bulge to take place in the tube at the back of the tube plate and the tube be thereby bring into more intimate contact with the tube plate than would otherwise be the case there be a steel ring indent into the segment of prosser 's mandrel to contract the segment when the central wedge be withdraw a more convenient form of the instrument however be obtain by place the segment in a circular box with one end project and support each segment in the box by a tenon which fit into a mortise in the cylindrical box to expand the segment a round taper piece of steel like a drift be force into a central hole round which the segment be arrange a piece of steel tube also slit up to enable a central drift to expand it answer very well but the thickness of that part of the tube in which there require to be spring enough to let the mandrel expand require to be sufficiently reduce to prevent the piece from crack when the central drift be drive in by a hammer the drift be better when make with a globular head so that it may be strike back by the hammer as well as be drive in a expand mandrel with a central drift be more rapid in its operation than when the expansion be produce by means of a screw 421 _ q _ -- will you explain the means that be adopt to regulate the admission of steam to the cylinder _ a _ -- in locomotive the admission of the steam from the boiler to the cylinder be regulate by a valve call the regulator which be generally place immediately above the internal fire box and be connect with two copper pipe -- one conduct steam from the highest point of the dome down to it and the other conduct the steam that have pass through it along the boiler to the upper part of the smoke box regulator may be divide into two sort viz those with slide valve and steam port and those with conical valve and seat of which the latter kind be the best the former kind have for the most part consist of a circular valve and face with radial aperture the valve resemble the outstretched wing of a butterfly and be make to revolve on its central pivot by connect link between its outer edge or by its central spindle in some of stephenson 's engine the regulator consist of a slide valve cover a port on the top of the valve chest a rod pass from this valve through the smoke box below the boiler and by means of a lever parallel to the start lever be bring up to the engineer 's reach cock be at first use as regulator but be give up as they be find liable to stick fast a gridiron slide valve have be use by stephenson which consist of a perforated square move upon a face with a equal number of hole this plan of a valve give with a small movement a large area of opening in bury 's engine a sort of conical plug be use which be withdraw by turn the handle in front of the fire box : a spiral grove of a very large pitch be make in the valve spindle in which fit a pin fix to the boiler and by turn the spindle a end motion be give to it which either shut or open the steam passage accord to the direction in which it be turn the best regulator would probably be a valve of the equilibrium description such as be use in the cornish engine : there would be no friction in such a regulator and it could be open or shut with a small amount of force such valve indeed be now sometimes employ for regulator in locomotive chapter viii constructive detail of engine pump engine 422 _ q _ -- will you explain the course of procedure in the erection of a pump engine such as boulton and watt introduce into cornwall _ a _ -- the best instruction on this subject be those of mr watt himself which be as follow : -- have fix on the proper situation of the pump in the pit from its center measure out the distance to the center of the cylinder from which set off all the other dimension of the house include the thickness of the wall and dig out the whole of the include ground to the depth of the bottom of the cellar so that the bottom of the cylinder may stand on a level with the natural ground of the place or lower if convenient for the less the height of the house above the ground the firmer it will be the foundation of the wall must be lay at least two foot lower than the bottom of the cellar unless the foundation be firm rock and care must be take to leave a small drain into the pit quite through the lowest part of the foundation of the lever wall to let off any water that may be spill in the engine house or may naturally come into the cellar if the foundation at that depth do not prove good you must either go down to a better if in you reach or make it good by a platform of wood or pile or both 423 _ q _ -- these direction refer to the foundation _ a _ -- yes but i will now proceed to the other part within the house low wall must be build to carry the cylinder beam so as to leave sufficient room to come at the hold down bolt and the end of these beam must also be lodge in the wall the lever wall must be build in the firmest manner and run solid course by course with thin lime mortar care be take that the lime have not be long slake if the house be build of stone let the stone be large and long and let many header be lay through the wall : it should also be a rule that every stone be lay on the broadest bed it have and never set on its edge a course or two above the lintel of the door that lead to the condenser build into the wall two parallel flat thin bar of iron equally distant from each other and from the outside and inside of the wall and reach the whole breadth of the lever wall about a foot higher in the wall lay at every four foot of the breadth of the front other bar of the same kind at right angle to the former course and reach quite through the thickness of the wall and at each front corner lay a long bar in the middle of the side wall and reach quite through the front wall if these bar be 10 foot or 12 foot long it will be sufficient when the house be build up nearly to the bottom of the opening under the great beam another double course of bar be to be build in as have be direct at the level of the upper cylinder beam hole must be leave in the wall for they end with room to move they laterally so that the cylinder may be get in and smaller hole must be leave quite through the wall for the introduction of iron bar which be firmly fasten to the cylinder beam at one end and screw at the other or outer end will serve by they go through both the front and back wall to bind the house more firmly together the spring beam or iron bar fasten to they must reach quite through the back wall and be key or screw up tight and they must be firmly fasten to the lever wall on each side either by iron bar firm piece of wood or long strong stone reach far back into the wall they must also be bed solidly and the residue of the opening must be build up in the firmest manner 424 _ q _ -- if there be a deficiency of water for the purpose of condensation what course should be pursue _ a _ -- if there be no water in the neighborhood that can be employ for the purpose of condensation it will be necessary to make a pond dig in the earth for the reception of the water deliver by the air pump to the end that it may be cool and use again for the engine the pond may be three or four foot deep and line with turf puddle or otherwise make water tight throw up the water into the air in the form of a jet to cool it have be find detrimental as the water be then charge with air which vitiate the vacuum 425 _ q _ -- how be the piston of a pump engine pack _ a _ -- to pack the piston take sixty common-sized white or untarred rope-yarn and with they plait a gasket or flat rope as close and firm as possible taper for eighteen inch at each end and long enough to go round the piston and overlap for that length coil this rope the thin way as hard as possible and beat it with a sledge hammer until its breadth answer the place put it in and beat it down with a wooden drift and a hand mallet pour some melt tallow all around then pack in a layer of white oakum half a inch thick so that the whole packing may have the depth of five to six inch depend on the size of the engine finally screw down the junk ring the packing should be beat solid but not too hard otherwise it will create so great a friction as to prevent the easy going of the engine abundance of tallow should be allow especially at first the quantity require will be less as the cylinder grow smooth in some of the more modern pump engine the piston be provide with metallic packing consist for the most part of a single ring with a tongue piece to break the joint and packed behind with hemp the upper edge of the metallic ring be sharpen away from the inside so as to permit more conveniently the application of hemp packing behind it and the junk ring be make much the same as if no metallic packing be employ 426 _ q _ -- will you explain the mode of put the engine into operation _ a _ -- to set the engine go the steam must be raise until the pressure in the steam pipe be at least equal to three pound on the square inch and when the cylinder jacket be fully warm and steam issue freely from the jacket cock open all the valve or regulator the steam will then forcibly blow out the air or water contain in the eduction pipe and to get rid of the air in the cylinder shut the steam valve after have blow through the engine for a few minute the cold water round the condenser will condense some of the steam contain in the eduction pipe and its place will be supply by some of the air from the cylinder the steam valve must again be open to blow out that air and the operation be to be repeat until the air be all draw out of the cylinder when that be the case shut all the valve and observe if the vacuum gauge show a vacuum in the condenser when there be a vacuum equivalent to three inch of mercury open the injection a very little and shut it again immediately and if this produce any considerable vacuum open the exhausting valve a very little way and the injection at the same time if the engine do not now commence its motion it must be blow through again until it move if the engine be lightly load or if there be no water in the pump the throttle valve must be keep nearly close and the top and exhaustion regulator must be open only a very little way else the engine will make its stroke with violence and perhaps do mischief if there be much unbalanced weight on the pump end the plug which open the steam valve must be so regulate that the valve will only be open very slightly and if after a few stroke it be find that the engine go out too slowly the valve may be then so adjust as to open wider the engine should always be make to work full stroke that be until the catch pin be make to come within half a inch of the spring at each end and the piston should stand high enough in the cylinder when the engine be at rest to spill over into the perpendicular steam pipe any water which may be condensed above it for if water remain upon the piston it will increase the consumption of steam when the engine be to be stop shut the injection valve and secure it and adjust the tappet so as to prevent the exhausting valve from open and to allow the steam valve to open and remain open otherwise a partial vacuum may arise in the cylinder and it may be fill with water from the injection or from leak a single act engine when it be in good order ought to be capable of go as slow as one stroke in ten minute and as fast as ten stroke in one minute and if it do not fulfil these condition there be some fault which should be ascertain and remedy 427 _ q _ -- you explanation have reference to the pump engine as introduce into cornwall by watt : have any modification be since make upon it _ a _ -- in the modern cornish engine the steam be use very expansively and a high pressure of steam be employ in some case a double cylinder engine be use in which the steam after have give motion to a small piston on the principle of a high pressure engine pass into a larger cylinder where it operate on the principle of a condense engine but there be no superior effect gain by the use of two cylinder and there be greater complexity in the apparatus instead of the lever wall cast iron column be now frequently use for support the main beam in pump engine and the cylinder end of the main beam be generally make longer than the pump end in engine make in cornwall so as to enable the cylinder to have a long stroke and the piston to move quickly without communicate such a velocity to the pump bucket as will make they work with such a shock as to wear themselves out quickly a high pressure of steam too can be employ where the stroke be long without involve the necessity of make the work part of such large dimension as would otherwise be necessary for the strength of the part of a single act engine will require to be much the same whatever the length of the stroke may be 428 _ q _ -- what kind of pump be mostly use in drain deep mine _ a _ -- the pump now universally prefer be the plunger pump which admit of be pack or tighten while the engine be at work but the lowest lift of a mine be generally supply with a pump on the suction principle both with the view of enable the lowest pipe to follow the water with facility as the shaft be sink deeper and to obviate the inconvenience of the valve of the pump be render inaccessible by any flooding in the mine the pump valve of deep mine be a perpetual source of expense and trouble as from the pressure of water upon they it be difficult to prevent they from close with violence and many expedient have be contrived to mitigate the evil of which the valve know as harvey and west 's valve have perhaps gain the widest acceptation 429 _ q _ -- will you describe harvey and west 's pump valve _ a _ -- this valve be a compromise between the equilibrium valve of the kind employ for admit the steam to and from the cylinder in single act engine and the common spindle valve formerly use for that purpose and to comprehend its action it be necessary that the action of the equilibrium valve which have be already represent fig 34 should first be understand this valve consist substantially of a cylinder open at both end and capable of slide upon a stationary piston fix upon a rod the length of the cylinder which proceed from the center of the orifice the valve be intend to close it be clear that when the cylinder be press down until its edge rest upon the bottom of the box contain it the orifice of the pipe must be close as the steam can neither escape past the edge of the cylinder nor between the cylinder and the piston and it be equally clear that as the pressure upon the cylinder be equal all around it and the whole of the downward pressure be maintain by the stationary piston the cylinder can be raise or lower without any further exertion of force than be necessary to overcome the friction of the piston and of the rod by which the cylinder be raise instead of the rub surface of a piston however a conical valve face between the cylinder and piston be employ which be tight only when the cylinder be in its lowest position and there be a similar face between the edge of the cylinder and the bottom of the box in which it be place the move part of the valve too instead of be a perfect cylinder be bulge outward in the middle so as to permit the steam to escape past the stationary piston when the cylindrical part of the valve be raise it be clear that if such a valve be apply to a pump no pressure of water within the pump would suffice to open it neither would any pressure of water above the valve cause it to shut with violence and if a equilibrium valve therefore be use as a pump valve at all it must be open and shut by mechanical means in harvey and west 's valve however the equilibrium principle be only partially adopt the lower face be considerably larger in diameter than the upper face and the difference constitute a annulus of pressure which will cause the valve to open or shut with the same force as a spindle valve of the area of the annulus to deaden the shock still more effectually the lower face of the valve be make to strike upon end wood drive into a annular recess in the pump bucket and valve thus construct work with very little noise or tremor but it be find in practice that the use of harvey and west 's valve or any contrivance of a similar kind add materially to the load upon the pump especially in low lift where the addition of a load to the valve make a material addition to the total resistance which the engine have to overcome instead of end wood drive into a recess for the valve to strike upon a mixture of tin and lead cast in a recess be now frequently use and be find to be preferable to the wood 430 _ q _ -- be there any other kind of pump valve which be free from the shock incidental to the working of common valve _ a _ -- in some case canvass valve be use for pump with the effect of materially mitigate the shock but they require frequent renewal and be of inferior eligibility in they action to the slide valve which might in many case be apply to pump without inconvenience 431 _ q _ -- could not a form of pump be devise capable of work without valve at all _ a _ -- it appear probable that by work a common reciprocating pump at a high speed a continuous flow of water might be maintain through the pipe in such a way as to render the existence of any valve superfluous after once the action be begin the momentum of the move water act in fact as valve the centrifugal pump however threaten to supersede pump of every other kind and if the centrifugal pump be employ there will be no necessity for pump valve at all there be less loss of effect by the centrifugal pump than by the common pump 432 _ q _ -- what be the best form of the centrifugal pump _ a _ -- there be two form in which the centrifugal pump may be apply to mine -- that in which the arm diverge from the bottom like the letter v and that in which revolving arm be set in a tight case near the bottom of the mine and be turn by a shaft from the surface such pump both draw and force and either by arrange they in a succession of lift in the shaft of the mine or otherwise the water may be draw without inconvenience from any depth the introduction of the centrifugal pump would obviously extinguish the single act engine as rotative engine work at a high speed would be the most appropriate form of engine where the centrifugal pump be employ 433 _ q _ -- this would not be a heavy deprivation _ a _ -- the single act engine be a remnant of engineering barbarism which must now be supersede by more compendious contrivance the cornish engine though rudely manufacture be very expensive in production as a large engine do but little work whereas by employ a smaller engine move with a high speed the dimension may be so far diminish that the most refined machinery may be obtain at less than the present cost 434 _ q _ -- be not the cornish engine more economical in fuel than other engine _ a _ -- it be a mistake to suppose that there be any peculiar virtue in the existing form of cornish engine to make it economical in fuel or that a less lethargic engine would necessarily be less efficient the large duty of the engine in cornwall be traceable to the large employment of the principle of expansion and to a few other cause which may be make of quite as decisive efficacy in smaller engine work with a quicker speed and there be therefore no argument in the performance of the present engine against the propose substitution various form of marine engine 435 _ q _ -- what species of paddle engine do you consider to be the best _ a _ -- the oscillate engine 436 _ q _ -- will you explain the grounds of that preference _ a _ -- the engine occupy little space consist of few part be easily accessible for repair and may be both light and strong at the same time in the case of large engine the crank in the intermediate shaft be a disadvantage as it be difficult to obtain such a forge quite sound but by forge it in three crank flat bar which be then lay together and weld into a square shaft a sound forge will be more probable and the bar should be round a little on the side which be weld to allow the scoria to escape during that operation it be important in so large a forge not to let the fire be too fierce else the surface of the iron will be burn before the heart be bring to a welding heat in some case in oscillate engine the air pump have be work by a eccentric and that may at any time be do where doubt of obtain a sound intermediate shaft be entertain but the precaution must be take to make the eccentric very wide so as to distribute the pressure over a large surface else the eccentric will be apt to heat 437 _ q _ -- have not objection be bring against the oscillate engine _ a _ -- in common with every other improvement the oscillate engine at the time of its introduction encounter much opposition the cylinder it be say would become oval the trunnion bearing would be liable to heat and the trunnion joint to leak the strain upon the trunnion would be apt to bend in or bend out the side of the cylinder and the circumstance of the cylinder be fix across its center while the shaft require to accommodate itself to the working of the ship might it be think be the occasion of such a strain upon the trunnion as would either break they or bend the piston rod it be a sufficient reply to these objection to say that they be all hypothetical and that none of they in practice have be find to exist -- to such a extent at least as to occasion any inconvenience but it be not difficult to show that they be altogether unsubstantial even without a recourse to the disproof afford by experience 438 _ q _ -- be there not a liability in the cylinder to become oval from the strain throw on it by the piston _ a _ -- there be no doubt a tendency in oscillate engine for the cylinder and the stuffing box to become oval but after a number of year ' wear it be find that the amount of ellipticity be less than that which be find to exist in the cylinder of side lever engine after a similar trial the resistance oppose by friction to the oscillation of the cylinder be so small that a man be capable of move a large cylinder with one hand whereas in the side lever engine if the parallel motion be in the least untrue which be at some time or other a almost inevitable condition the piston be push with great force against the side of the cylinder whereby a large amount of wear and friction be occasion the trunnion bearing instead of be liable to heat like other journal be keep down to the temperature of the steam by the flow of steam pass through they and the trunnion packing be not liable to leak when the packing before be introduce be squeeze in a cylindrical mould 439 _ q _ -- might not the eduction trunnion be immerse in water _ a _ -- in some case a hollow or lantern brass about one third or one fourth the length of the packing space and supply with steam or water by a pipe be introduce in the middle of the packing so that if there be any leakage through the trunnion it will be a leakage of steam or water which will not vitiate the vacuum but in ordinary case this device will not be necessary and it be not commonly employ it be clear that there can be no buckling of the side of the cylinder by the strain upon the trunnion if the cylinder be make strong enough and in cylinder of the ordinary thickness such a action have never be experience nor be it the fact that the intermediate shaft of steam vessel to which part alone the motion be communicate by the engine require to adapt itself to the alter form of the vessel as the engine and intermediate shaft be rigidly connect although the paddle shaft require to be capable of such a adaptation even if this objection exist however it could easily be meet by make the crank pin of the ball and socket fashion which would permit the position of the intermediate shaft relatively with that of the cylinder to be slightly change without throw a undue strain upon any of the work part 440 _ q _ -- be the trunk engine inferior to the oscillate _ a _ -- a very elegant and efficient arrangement of trunk engine suitable for paddle vessel have latterly be employ by messr rennie of which all the part resemble those of penn 's oscillate engine except that the cylinder be stationary instead of be movable and a round trunk or pipe set upon the piston and move steam tight through the cylinder cover enable the connect rod which be fix to the piston to vibrate within it to the requisite extent but the vice of all trunk engine be that they be necessarily more wasteful of steam as the large mass of metal enter into the composition of the trunk move as it do alternately into the atmosphere and the steam must cool and condense a part of the steam the radiation of heat from the interior of the trunk will have the same operation though in vertical trunk engine the loss from this cause might probably be reduce by fill the trunk with oil so far as this could be do without the oil be spill over the edge 441 _ q _ -- what species of screw engine do you consider the best _ a _ -- i be incline to give the preference to a variety of the horizontal steeple engine such as be first use in hm amphion in this engine the cylinder lie on they side and they be place near the side of the vessel with they mouth point to the keel from each cylinder two long piston rod proceed across the vessel to a cross head work in guide and from this cross head a connect rod return back to the center of the vessel and give motion to the crank the piston rod be so place in the piston that one of they pass above the crank shaft and the other below the crank shaft the cross head lie in the same horizontal plane as the center of the cylinder and a lug project upward from the cross head to engage one piston rod and downward from the cross head to engage the other piston rod the air pump be double act and its piston or bucket have the same stroke as the piston of the engine the air pump bucket derive its motion from a arm on the cross head and a similar arm be usually employ in engine of this class to work the feed and bilge pump 442 _ q _ -- be not inconvenience experience in direct act screw engine from the great velocity of they motion _ a _ -- not if they be properly construct but they require to be much stronger to be fit with more care and to have the bearing surface much larger than be necessary in engine move slowly the momentum of the reciprocate part should also be balance by a weight apply to the crank or crank shaft as be do in locomotive a very convenient arrangement for obtain surface be to form the crank of each engine of two cast iron disc cast with heavy side the excess of weight upon the heavy side be nearly equal to that of the piston and its connection when the piston be travel in one direction the weight be travel in the opposite and the momentum of the piston and its attachment which be arrest at each reciprocation be just balance by the equal and opposite momentum of the weight one advantage of the horizontal engine be that a single engine may be employ whereby greater simplicity of the machinery and greater economy of fuel will be obtain since there will be less radiate surface in one cylinder than in two cylinder piston and valve 443 _ q _ -- be it a beneficial practice to make cylinder with steam jacket _ a _ -- in cornwall where great attention be pay to economy of fuel all the engine be make with steam jacket and in some case a flue wind spirally round the cylinder for keep the steam hot mr watt in he early practice discard the steam jacket for a time but resume it again as he find its discontinuance occasion a perceptible waste of fuel and in modern engine it have be find that where a jacket be use less coal be consume than where the use of a jacket be reject the cause of this diminished effect be not of very easy perception for the jacket expose a larger radiate surface for the escape of the heat than the cylinder nevertheless the fact have be establish beyond doubt by repeat trial that engine provide with a jacket be more economical than engine without one the exterior of the cylinder or jacket should be cover with several ply of feel and then be case in timber which must be very narrow the board be first dry in a stove and then bind round the cylinder with hoop like the stave of a cask in many of the cornish engine the steam be let into casing form in the cylinder cover and cylinder bottom for the further economisation of the heat and the cylinder stuffing box be make very deep and a lantern or hollow brass be introduce into the center of the packing into which brass the steam gain admission by a pipe provide for the purpose so that in the event of the packing become leaky it will be steam that will be leak into the cylinder instead of air which be incondensable would impair the efficiency of the engine a lantern brass of a similar kind be sometimes introduce into the stuff box of oscillate engine but its use there be to receive the lateral pressure of the piston rod and thus take any strain off the packing 444 _ q _ -- will you explain the proper course to pursue in the production of cylinder _ a _ -- in all engine the valve case if make in a separate piece from the cylinder should be attach by means of a metallic joint as such a barbarism as a rust joint in such situation be no longer permissible in the case of large engine with valve casing suitable for long slide a expansion joint in the valve casing should invariably be insert otherwise the steam by gain admission to the valve case before it can enter the cylinder expand the case while the cylinder remain unaltered in its dimension and the joint be damage and in some case the cylinder be crack by the great strain thus introduce the chest of the blow-through valve be very commonly cast upon the valve casing and in engine where the cylinder be stationary this be the most convenient practice all engine where the valve be not of such a construction as to leave the face when a pressure exceed that of the steam be create in the cylinder by priming or otherwise should be provide with a escape valve to let out the water and such valve should be so construct that the water can not fly out with violence over the attendant but it should be conduct away by a suitable pipe to a place where its discharge can occasion no inconvenience the stuff box of all engine which can not be stop frequently to be repack should be make very deep metallic packing in the stuffing box have be use in some engine consist in most instance of one or more ring cut spring and slip upon the piston rod before the cross head be put on and pack with hemp behind this species of packing answer very well when the parallel motion be true and the piston rod free from scratch and it accomplish a material saving of tallow in some case a piece of sheet brass pack behind with hemp have be introduce with good effect a flange be turn over on the under edge of the brass to prevent it from slip up or down with the motion of the rod the sheet brass speedily put a excellent polish upon the rod and such a packing be more easily keep and require less tallow than where hemp alone be employ in side lever marine engine the attachment of the cylinder to the diagonal stay be generally make of too small a area and the flange be make too thick a very thick flange cast on any part of a cylinder endanger the soundness of the cylinder by induce a unequal contraction of the metal and it be a preferable course to make the flange for the attachment or the frame thin and the surface large -- the bolt be turn bolt and nicely fit if from malformation in this part the frame work to a inconvenient extent the best expedient appear to be the introduction of a number of steel taper bolt the hole have be previously bore out and if the flange be thick enough square key may also be introduce half into one flange and half into the other so as to receive the strain if the jaw crack or break away however it will be best to apply a malleable iron hoop around the cylinder to take the strain and this will in all case be the preferable expedient where from any peculiarity of structure there be a difficulty in introduce bolt and key of sufficient strength 445 _ q _ -- which be the most eligible species of piston _ a _ -- for large engine piston with a metallic packing consist of a single ring with the end mortice into one another and a piece of metal let in flush over the joint and rivet to one end of the ring appear to be the best species of piston and if the cylinder be oscillate it will be expedient to chamfer off the upper edge of the ring on the inner side and to pack it at the back with hemp if the cylinder be a stationary one spring may be substitute for the hemp packing but in any case it will be expedient to make the vertical joint of the end of the ring run a little obliquely so as to prevent the joint form a ridge in the cylinder for small piston two ring may be employ make somewhat eccentric internally to give a greater thickness of metal in the center of the ring these ring must be set one above the other in the cylinder and the joint which be oblique must be set at right angle with one another so as to obviate any disposition of the ring in they expansion to wear the cylinder oval the ring must first be turn a little larger than the diameter of the cylinder and a piece be then to be cut out so that when the end be bring together the ring will just enter within the cylinder the ring while retain in a state of compression be then to be put in the lathe and turn very truly and finally it be to be hammer on the inside with the small end of the hammer to expand the metal and thus increase the elasticity 446 _ q _ -- the ring should be carefully fit to one another laterally _ a _ -- the ring be to be fit laterally to the piston and to one another by scrape -- a steady pin be fix upon the flange of the piston and fitting into a corresponding hole in the lower ring to keep the lower ring from turn round and a similar pin be fix into the top edge of the lower ring to prevent the upper ring from turn round but the hole into which these pin fit must be make oblong to enable the ring to press outward as the rub surface wear in most case it will be expedient to press the packing ring out with spring where they be not pack behind with hemp and the spring should be make very strong as the prevail fault of spring be they weakness sometimes short bent spring set round at regular interval between the packing ring and body of the piston be employ the center of each spring be secure by a steady pin or bolt screw into the side of the piston but it will not signify much what kind of spring be use provide they have sufficient tension when piston be make of a single ring or of a succession of single ring the strength of each ring should be test previously to its introduction into the piston by means of a lever load by a heavy weight 447 _ q _ -- what kind of piston be employ by messr penn _ a _ -- messr penn 's piston for oscillate engine have a single packing ring with a tongue piece or mortice end make in the manner already describe the ring be pack behind with hemp packing and the piece of metal which cover the joint be a piece of thick sheet copper or brass and be indented into the iron of the ring so as to offer no obstruction to the application of the hemp the ring be fit to the piston only on the under edge the top edge be round to a point from the inside and the junk ring do not bear upon it but the junk ring squeeze down the hemp packing between the packing ring and the body of the piston 448 _ q _ -- how should the piston rod be secure to the piston _ a _ -- the piston rod where it fit into the piston should have a good deal of taper for if the taper be too small the rod will be draw through the hole and the piston will be split asunder small groove be sometimes turn out of the piston rod above and below the cutter hole and hemp be introduce in order to make the piston eye tight most piston rod be fix to the piston by means of a gib and cutter but in some case the upper portion of the rod within the eye be screw and it be fix into the piston by means of a indented nut this nut be in some case hexagonal and in other case the exterior form a portion of a cone which completely fill a corresponding recess in the piston but nut make in this way become rust into they seat after some time and can not be start again without much difficulty messr miller ravenhill & co fix in they piston rod by means of a indented hexagonal nut which may be start by means of a open box key the thread of the screw be make flat upon the one side and much slant on the other whereby a greater strength be secure without create any disposition to split the nut in side lever engine it be a judicious practice to add a nut to the top of the piston rod in addition to the cutter for secure the piston rod to the cross head in a good example of a engine thus provide the piston rod be 7 in in diameter and the screw 5 in the part of the rod which fit into the cross head eye be 1 ft 5-1\/2 in long and taper from 6-1\/2 in to 6-13\/16 in diameter this proportion of taper be a good one if the taper be less or if a portion of the piston rod within the cross head eye be leave untapered as be sometimes the case it be very difficult to detach the part from one another 449 _ q _ -- which be the most beneficial construction of slide valve _ a _ -- the best construction of slide valve appear to be that adopt by the eccentric by which the valve be move _ a _ -- in marine engine whether paddle or screw if move at a slow rate of speed the eccentric be generally loose upon the shaft for the purpose of backing and be furnish with a back balance and catch so that it may stand either in the position for go ahead or in that for go astern the body of the eccentric be of cast iron and it be put on the shaft in two piece the half be put together with rebate joint to keep they from separate laterally and they be prevent from slide out by round steel pin each ground into both half square key would probably be preferable to round pin in this arrangement as the pin tend to wedge the jaw of the eccentric asunder in some case the half of the eccentric be bolt together by means of flange which be perhaps the preferable practice the eccentric hoop in marine and land engine be generally of brass it be expedient to cast a oil cup on the eccentric hoop and where practicable a pan should be place beneath the eccentric for the reception of the oil dropping the notch of the eccentric rod for the reception of the pin of the valve shaft be usually steel to prevent inconvenient wear for when the side of the notch wear the valve movement be not only disturbed but it be very difficult to throw the eccentric rod out of gear it be find to be preferable however to fit this notch with a brass bush for the wear be then less rapid and it be a easy thing to replace this bush with another when it become wear the eccentric catch of the kind usually employ in marine engine sometimes break off at the first bolt hole and it be preferable to have a bolt in advance of the catch face or to have a hoop encircle the shaft with the catch weld on it the hoop itself be fix by bolt or a key this hoop may either be put on before the crank in one piece or afterwards in two piece 453 _ q _ -- be such eccentric use in direct act screw engine _ a _ -- no direct act screw engine be usually fit with the link motion and two fix eccentric air pump and condenser 454 _ q _ -- what be the detail of the air pump _ a _ -- the air pump bucket and valve be all of brass in modern marine engine and the chamber of the pump be the place by hammer the copper on the inside air pump rod of muntz 's metal or copper be much use iron rod cover with brass be generally waste away where the bottom cone fit into the bucket eye and if the case be at all porous the water will insinuate itself between the casing and the rod and eat away the iron if iron rod cover with brass be use the brass casing should come some distance into the bucket eye the cutter should be of brass and a brass washer should cover the under side of the eye so as to defend the end of the rod from the salt water rod of muntz 's metal be probably on the whole to be prefer it be a good practice to put a nut on the top of the rod to secure it more firmly in the cross head eye where that plan can be conveniently adopt the part of the rod which fit into the cross head eye should have more taper when make of copper or brass than when make of iron as if the taper be small the rod may get stave into the eye whereby its detachment will be difficult 455 _ q _ -- what species of packing be use in air pump _ a _ -- metallic packing have in some instance be employ in air pump bucket but its success have not be such as to lead to its further adoption the 459 _ q _ -- what be the proper area through the valve grating _ a _ -- the collective area should be at least equal to the area of the pump piston and the lower edge of the perforation should be round off to afford more free ingress or egress to the water 460 _ q _ -- be there much strain throw on the plate in which the valve be set _ a _ -- a good deal of strain and in the earlier direct act screw engine these plate be nearly in every case make too light they should be make thick have strong feather upon they and be very securely bolt down with split pin at the point of the bolt to prevent they from unscrew the plate will be very apt to be break should some of the bolt become loose of course all the bolt and split pin as well as the plate and guard must be of brass 461 _ q _ -- how be the plate to be take out should that become necessary _ a _ -- they be usually take out through a door in the top of the hot well provide for that purpose which door should be as large as the plate themselves and it be a good precaution to cast upon this door -- which will be of cast iron -- six or eight stout project foot which will press upon the top of the outlet or delivery valve plate when the door be screw down the upper or delivery valve plate and the lower or foot valve plate should have similar foot a large part of the strain will thus be transfer from the plate to the door which can easily be make strong enough to sustain it it be advisable that the plate should lie at a angle so that the shock of the water may not come upon the whole surface at once 462 _ q _ -- do the double acting air pump usual in direct act screw engine produce as good a vacuum as the single act air pump usual in paddle engine _ a _ -- it will do so if properly construct but i do not know of any case of a double acting air pump with indium rubber valve which have be properly construct 463 _ q _ -- what be the fault of such pump _ a _ -- the pump frequently work by start as if at time it do not draw at all and then again on a sudden gorge itself with water so as to throw a great strain upon the work part the vacuum moreover be by no means so good as it should be and it be a universal vice of direct act screw engine that the vacuum be defective i have be at some pain to investigate the cause of this imperfection and in a sugar house engine fit with pump like those of a direct act screw engine to maintain a vacuum in the pan i find that a better vacuum be produce when the engine be go slowly than when it be go fast which be quite the reverse of what be to have be expect as the hot water which have to be remove by the condensation of the steam proceeding from the pan be a constant quantity in this engine too which be a high pressure one the irregularity of the engine consequent upon the fitful catch of the water by the pump be more conspicuous as the working of this vacuum pump be the only work that the engine have to perform 464 _ q _ -- and be you able to discover the cause of these irregularity _ a _ -- the main cause of they i find to be the largeness of the space leave between the valve plate in this class of pump and out of which there be nothing to press the air or water which may be lie there it consequently happen that if there be the slightest leakage of air into the pump this air be merely compress and not expel by the advance of the air pump piston it expand again to its former bulk on the return of the pump piston and prevent the water from enter until there be such a accumulation of pressure in the condenser as force the water into the pump when the air be expel by the water cause a good vacuum to be momentarily form in the pump when it gorge itself by take a sudden gulp of water so soon however as the pressure fall in the condenser and some more air leak into the pump the former imperfect action recur and be again redress in the same violent manner 465 _ q _ -- be this irregular action of the pump the cause of the imperfect vacuum _ a _ -- it be one cause sometimes one end of the pump will alone draw and the other end will be inoperative although it be equally open to the condenser and this will chiefly take place at the stuffing box end where a leakage of air be more likely to occur i find however that even when both end of the pump be act equally and there be no leakage of air at all the vacuum maintain by a double act horizontal pump with indium rubber valve be not so good as that maintain by a single act pump of the kind usual in old engine 466 _ q _ -- will you specify more precisely what be the result you obtain _ a _ -- when the vacuum pan be exhaust by the pump without any boil be carry on in the pan but only a little cold water be let into it and also into the pump to enable they to act in they best manner it be find that whereas with the old pump a vacuum of 114 on the sugar boiler 's gauge could be readily obtain equal to about 29-1\/2 inch of mercury the lowest that could possibly be get with the new horizontal pump be 122 degree of the sugar boiler 's gauge or 29 inch of mercury and to get that the engine must not go faster than 10 or 12 stroke per minute the proper speed of the engine be 75 stroke per minute but if allow to go at that speed the vacuum fall to 130 of the sugar maker 's gauge or 28-1\/2 inch of mercury when the steam be let into the worm of the pan so as to boil the water in it the vacuum be 134 at 75 revolution of the engine and go down to 132 at 40 revolution but rise again to 135 equal to about 28-1\/4 inch of mercury at 20 revolution 467 _ q _ -- to what do you attribute the circumstance of a better vacuum be get at low speed than at high speed _ a _ -- it be difficult to assign the precise reason but it appear to be a consequence of the largeness of the vacant space between the valve plate when the piston of the air pump be draw back the air contain in this large collection of water will cause it to boil up like soda water and when the piston of the pump be force forward this air instead of be expel will be again drive into the water there will consequently be a quantity of air in the pump which can not be get rid of at all and which will impair the vacuum as a matter of course 468 _ q _ -- what expedient do you adopt to improve the vacuum in the engine to which you have refer _ a _ -- i put block of wood on the air pump piston which at the end of its stroke project between the valve plate and force the water out i also introduce a cock of water at each end of the pump between the valve plate to insure the presence of water at each end of the pump to force the air out with these amelioration the pump work steadily and the vacuum obtain become as good as in the old pump i have previously introduce a injection cock into each end of the air pump in steam vessel from which i have obtain advantageous result and in all horizontal air pump i would recommend the piston and valve plate to be so construct that the whole of the water will be express by the piston i would also recommend a injection cock to be introduce at each end of the pump pump cock and pipe 469 _ q _ -- will you explain the arrangement of the feed pump _ a _ -- in steam vessel the feed pump plunger be generally of brass and the barrel of the pump be sometimes of brass but generally of cast iron there should be a considerable clearance between the bottom of the plunger and the bottom of the barrel as otherwise the bottom of the barrel may be knock out should coal dust or any other foreign substance gain admission as it probably would do if the injection water be draw at any time from the bilge of the vessel as be usually do if the vessel spring a leak the valve of the feed pump in marine engine be generally of the spindle kind and be most conveniently arrange in a chest which may be attach in any accessible position to the side of the hot well there be two nozzle upon this chest of which the lower one lead to the pump and the upper one to the boiler the pipe lead to the pump be a suction pipe when the plunger ascend and a force pipe when the plunger descend the plunger in ascend draw the water out of the hot well through the lowest of the valve and in descend force it through the center valve into the space above it which communicate with the feed pipe should the feed cock be shut so as to prevent any feed water from pass through it the water will raise the topmost valve which be load to a pressure considerably above the pressure of the steam and escape into the hot well this arrangement be neater and less expensive than that of have a separate loaded valve on the feed pipe with a overflow through the ship 's side as be the more usual practice 470 _ q _ -- will you describe what precaution be to be observe in the construction of the cock use in engine _ a _ -- all the cock about a engine should be provide with bottom and stuff box and reliance should never be place upon a single bolt pass through a bottom washer for keep the plug in its place in the case of any cock communicate with the boiler for a great strain be throw upon that bolt if the pressure of the steam be high and if the plug be make with much taper and should the bolt break or the thread strip the plug will fly out and person stand near may be scald to death in large cock it appear the preferable plan to cast the bottom in and the metal of which all the cock about a marine engine be make should be of the same quality as that use in the composition of the brass and should be without lead or other deteriorate material in some case the bottom of cock be burn in with hard solder but this method can not be depend upon as the solder be soften and waste away by the hot salt water and in time the bottom leak or be force out the stuffing box of cock should be make of adequate depth and the gland should be secure by means of four strong copper bolt the taper of blow-off cock be a important element in they construction as if the taper be too great the plug will have a continual tendency to rise which if the packing be slack will enable grit to get between the face while if the taper be too little the plug will be liable to jam and a few time grind will sink it so far through the shell that the waterway will no longer correspond one eighth of a inch deviation from the perpendicular for every inch in height be a common angle for the side of the cock which correspond with one quarter of a inch difference of diameter in a inch of height but perhaps a somewhat greater taper than this or one third of a inch difference in diameter for every inch of height be a preferable proportion the bottom of the plug must be always keep a small distance above the bottom of the shell and a adequate surface must be leave above and below the waterway to prevent leakage cock form accord to these direction will be find to operate satisfactorily in practice while they will occasion perpetual trouble if there be any malformation 471 _ q _ -- what be the best arrangement and configuration of the blow-off cock _ a _ -- the blow-off cock of a boiler be generally place some distance from the boiler but it appear preferable that they should be place quite close to it as there be no means of shut off the water from the pipe between the blow-off cock and the boiler should fracture or leakage there arise every boiler must be furnish with a blow-off cock of its own independently of the main blow-off cock on the ship 's side so that the boiler may be blow off separately and may be shut off from one another the preferable arrangement appear to be to cast upon each blow-off cock a bend for attach the cock to the bottom of the boiler and the plug should stand about a inch in advance of the front of the boiler so that it may be remove or re-ground with facility the general arrangement of the blow-off pipe be to run a main blow-off pipe beneath the floor plate across the ship at the end of the engine and into this pipe to lead a separate pipe furnish with a cock from each boiler the main blow-off pipe where it penetrate the ship 's side be furnish with a cock : and in modern steam vessel kingston 's valve be also use which consist of a spindle or plate valve fit to the exterior of the ship so that if the internal pipe or cock break the external valve will still be operative some expedient of this kind be almost necessary as the blow-off cock require occasional regrinding and the sea cock can not be re-ground without put the vessel into dock except by the use of kingston 's valve or some equivalent expedient 472 q -- what be the proper construction and situation of the injection cock and waste water valve a -- the sea injection cock be usually make in the same fashion as the sea blow-off cock and of about the same size or rather larger the injection water be generally admit to the condenser by means of a slide valve but a cock appear to be preferable as it be more easily open and have not any disposition to shut of its own accord in paddle vessel the sea injection pipe should be put through the ship 's side in advance of the paddle so that the water draw in may not be injuriously charge with air the waste water pipe pass from the hot well through the vessel 's side be provide with a stop valve call the discharge valve which be usually make of the spindle kind so as to open when the water come from the air pump press against it in some case this valve be a sluice valve but the hot well be then almost sure to be split if the engine be set on without the valve have be open the opening of the waste water pipe should always be above the load water line as it will otherwise be difficult to prevent leakage through the engine into the ship when the vessel be lie in harbor 473 q -- what be the best arrangement of gauge cock and glass gauge a -- gauge cock be generally very inartificially make and occasion needless annoyance they be rarely make with bottom or with stuff box and be consequently for the most part adorn with stalactite of salt after a short period of service the water discharge from they too from the want of a proper conduit disfigure the front of the boiler and add to the corrosion in the ash pit it would be preferable to combine the gauge cock appertain to each boiler into a single upright tube connect suitably with the boiler and the water flow from they could be direct downward into a funnel tube communicate with the bilge the cock of the glass tube as well as of the gauge cock should be furnish with stuff box and with bottom unless the water enter through the bottom of the plug which in gauge cock be sometimes the case the glass gauge tube should always be fit with a cock at each neck communicate with the boiler so that the water and steam may be shut off if the tube break and the cock should be so make as to admit of the tube be blow through with steam to clear they as in muddy water they will become so soil that the water can not be see the gauge cock frequently have pipe run up within the boiler to the end that a high water level may be make consistent with a easily accessible position of the gauge cock themselves with the glass tube however this species of arrangement be not possible and the glass tube must always be place in the position of the water level 474 q -- what be the proper material of the pipe in steam vessel a -- most of the pipe of marine engine should be make of copper the steam pipe may be of cast iron if make very strong but the waste water pipe should be of copper cast iron blow-off pipe have in some case be employ but they be liable to fracture and be dangerous the blow-off and feed pipe should be of copper but the waste steam pipe may be of galvanized iron every pipe pass through the ship 's side and every pipe fix at both end and liable to be heat and cool should be furnish with a faucet or expansive joint and in the case of the cast iron pipe the part of the pipe fitting into the faucet should be turn in the distribution of the faucet of the pipe expose to pressure care must be take that they be so place that the part of the pipe can not be force asunder or turn round by the strain as serious accident have occur from the neglect of this precaution 475 _ q _ -- what be the best mode of make pipe tight where they penetrate the ship 's side _ a _ secure in its place by means of eight thick key the shaft should be burr up against the head of these key with a chisel so as to prevent the key from come back of they own accord if the key be want to railway _ a _ -- upon well form railway with carriage of good construction the average tractive force require for low speed be about 7-1\/2 lb per ton or 1\/300th of the load though in some experimental case where particular care be take to obtain a favorable result the tractive force have be reduce as low as 1\/500th of the load at low speed the whole of the tractive force be expend in overcome the friction which be make up partly of the friction of attrition in the axle and partly of the roll friction or the obstruction to the rolling of the wheel upon the rail the roll friction be very small when the surface be smooth and in the case of railway carriage do not exceed 1\/1000th of the load whereas the draught on common road of good construction which be chiefly make up of the roll friction be as much as 1\/36th of the load 494_q _ -- in reference to friction you have already state that the friction of iron slide upon brass which have be oil and then wipe dry so that no film of oil be interpose be about 1\/11th of the pressure but that in machine in actual operation where there be a film of oil between the rub surface the friction be only about one third of this amount or 1\/33d of the weight how then can the tractive resistance of locomotive at low speed which you say be entirely make up of friction be so little as 1\/500th of the weight _ a _ -- i do not
