attrition must be 1\/429th of the load and if the diameter of the wheel be 36 in and the diameter of the axle be 3 in which be common proportion the friction of attrition must be increase in the of a locomotive of modern construction vary from 20 to 25 ton 496 _ q _ -- and what be its cost and average performance _ a _ -- the cost of a common narrow gauge locomotive of average power vary from expense of traction increase much with a increase speed _ a _ -- yes it increase very rapidly partly from the undulation of the earth when a heavy train pass over it at a high velocity but chiefly very much increase at a speed of 30 mile a hour a engine evaporate 200 cubic foot of water in the hour and therefore exert about 200 horse power will draw a load of 110 ton take the friction of the foot high in the minute which divide by 33000 give 973 horse power as the power which would draw 110 ton upon a railway at a speed of 30 mile a hour if there be no atmospheric resistance the of the engine the same as the resistance per ton of the train _ a _ -- no it be more since the engine have not merely the resistance of the atmosphere and of the wheel to encounter but the resistance of the machinery besides accord to mr gooch 's experiment upon a train weigh 100 ton the resistance of the engine and tender at 131 mile per hour be find by the indicator to be 1238 lb the resistance per ton of the train as ascertain by the dynamometer be at the same speed 758 lb and the average resistance of locomotive and train be 904 lb at 202 mile per hour these resistance respectively become 190 819 and 122 lb at 441 mile per hour the resistance become 340 2110 and 255 lb and at 574 mile a hour they become 355 1781 and 238 lb 499 _ q _ -- be it not maintain that the resistance of the atmosphere to the progress of railway train increase as the square of the velocity _ a _ -- the atmospheric resistance no doubt increase as the square of the velocity and the power therefore necessary to overcome it will increase as the cube of the velocity since in double the speed four time the power must be expend in overcome the atmospheric resistance in half the time at low speed the resistance do not increase very rapidly but at high speed as the rapid increase in the atmospheric resistance cause the main resistance to be that arise from the atmosphere the total resistance will vary nearly as the square of the velocity thus the resistance of a train include locomotive and tender will at 15 mile a hour be about 93 lb per ton at 30 mile a hour it will be 132 lb per ton and at 60 mile a hour 29 lb per ton if we suppose the same law of progression to continue up to 120 mile a hour the resistance at that speed will be 922 lb per ton and at 240 mile a hour the resistance will be 3448 lb per ton thus in double the speed from 60 to 120 mile per hour the resistance do not fall much short of be increase fourfold and the same remark apply to the increase of the speed from 120 to 240 mile a hour these deduction and other deduction from mr gooch 's experiment on the resistance of railway train be fully discuss by mr clark in he treatise on railway machinery who give the follow rule for ascertain the resistance of a train suppose the line to be in good order and free from curve : -- to find the total resistance of the engine tender and train in pound per ton at any give speed square the speed in mile per hour divide it by 171 and add 8 to the quotient the result be the total resistance at the rail in lb per ton 500_q _ -- how come it that the resistance of fluid increase as the square of the velocity instead of the velocity simply _ a _ -- because the height necessary to generate the velocity with which the move object strike the fluid or the fluid strike the object increase as the _ square _ of the velocity and the resistance or the weight of a column of any fluid vary as the height a fall body as have be already explain to have acquire twice the velocity must have fall through four time the height the velocity generate by a column of any fluid be equal to that acquire by a body fall through the height of the column and it be therefore clear that the pressure due to any give velocity must be as the square of that velocity the pressure be in every case as twice the altitude of the column the work do however by a stream of air or other fluid in a give time will vary as the cube of the velocity for if the velocity of a stream of air be double there will not only be four time the pressure exert per square foot but twice the quantity of air will be employ and in windmill accordingly it be find that the work do vary nearly as the cube of the velocity of the wind if however the work do by _ a give quantity _ of air move at different speed be consider it will vary as the square of the speed 501 _ q _ -- but in a case where there be no work do and the resistance vary as the square of the speed should not the power requisite to overcome that resistance vary as the square of the speed _ a _ -- it should if you consider the resistance over a give distance and not the resistance during a give time suppose the resistance of a railway train to increase as the square of the speed it would take four time the power so far as atmospheric resistance be concern to accomplish a mile at the rate of 60 mile a hour that it would take to accomplish a mile at 30 mile a hour but in the former case there would be twice the number of mile accomplish in the same time so that when the velocity of the train be double we should require a engine that be capable of overcome four time the resistance at twice the speed or in other word that be capable of exert eight time the power so far as regard the element of atmospheric resistance we know by experience however that it be easier to attain high speed on railway than in steam vessel where the resistance do increase nearly as the square of the speed 502 _ q _ -- will you describe generally the arrangement of a locomotive engine _ a _ -- the boiler and engine be hang upon a framework set on wheel and together with this frame or carriage constitute what be commonly call the locomotive behind the locomotive run another carriage call the tender for hold coke and water a common mode of connect the engine and tender be by means of a rigid bar with a eye at each end through which pin be pass between the engine and tender however buffer should always be interpose as they pressure contribute greatly to prevent oscillation and other irregular motion of the engine 503 _ q _ -- how be the respect the relative merit of outside and inside framing which have terminate however in the universal adoption of the inside frame it be difficult in engine intend for the narrow gauge to get cylinder within the framing of sufficient diameter to meet the exigency of railway locomotion by cast both cylinder in a piece however a considerable amount of room may be make available to increase they diameter it be very desirable that the cylinder of locomotive should be as large as possible so that expansion may be adopt to a large extent and with any give speed of piston the power of a engine either to draw heavy load or achieve high velocity will be increase with every increase of the dimension of the cylinder the framing of locomotive to which the boiler and machinery be attach and which rest upon the spring situate above the axle be form generally of malleable iron but in some engine the side frame consist of oak with iron plate rivet on each side the guard plate be in connect across the end and cross stay be introduce beneath the boiler to stiffen the frame sideways and prevent the end of the connect or eccentric rod from fall down if they should be break 504 _ q _ -- what be the nature and arrangement of the spring of locomotive _ a _ -- the spring be of the ordinary carriage kind with plate connect at the center and allow to slide on each other at they end the to make the plate of a common spring with different curve so that the leaf though in contact at the center would not be in contact with the end with light load but would be bring into contact gradually as the strain cony on : a spring would thus be obtain that be suitable for all load 505 _ q _ -- what be the difference between inside and outside cylinder engine _ a _ -- outside cylinder themselves to crank in the drive axle 506 _ q _ -- whether be inside or outside cylinder engine to be prefer _ a _ -- a diversity of opinion obtain as to the relative merit of outside and inside cylinder the chief objection to outside cylinder be that they occasion a sinuous motion in the engine which be apt to send the train off the rail but this action may be make less perceptible or be remedy altogether by place a weight upon one side of the wheel the momentum of which will just balance the momentum of the piston and its connection the sinuous or rock motion of locomotive be traceable to the arrest momentum of the piston and its attachment at every stroke of the engine and the effect of the pressure thus create will be more operative in induce oscillation the farther it be exert from the central line of the engine if both cylinder be set at right angle in the center of the carriage and the piston be both attach to a central crank there would be no oscillation produce or the same effect would be realize by place one cylinder in the center of the carriage and two at the side -- the piston of the side cylinder move simultaneously : but it be impossible to couple the piston of a upright cylinder direct to the axle of a locomotive without cause the spring to work up and down with every stroke of the engine : and the use of three cylinder though adopt in some of stephenson 's engine involve too much complication to be a beneficial innovation 507 _ q _ -- whether be four-wheeled or six-wheeled engine preferable _ a _ -- much controversial ingenuity have be expend upon the question of the relative merit of the four and six-wheeled engine one party maintain that four-wheeled engine be most unsafe and the other that six-wheeled engine be unmechanical and be more likely to occasion accident the four-wheeled engine however appear to have be charge with fault that do not really attach to they when properly construct for it by no means follow that if the axle of a four-wheeled engine break or even altogether come away that the engine must fall down or run off the line inasmuch as if the engine be properly couple with the tender it have the tender to sustain it it be obvious enough that such a connection may be make between the tender and the engine that either the fore or hind axle of the engine may be take away and yet the engine will not fall down but will be keep up by the support which the tender afford and the argument hitherto parade against the four-wheeled engine be so far as regard the question of safety nothing more than argument against the existence of the suggest connection it be no doubt the fact that locomotive engine be now become too heavy to be capable of be bear on four wheel at high speed without injury to the rail but the objection of damage to the rail apply with at least equal force to most of the six-wheeled engine hitherto construct as in those engine the engineer have the power of put nearly all the weight upon the drive wheel and if the rail be wet or greasy there be a great temptation to increase the bite of those wheel by screw they down more firmly upon the rail a greater strain be thus throw upon the rail than can exist in the case of any equally heavy four-wheeled engine and the engine be make very unsafe as a pitch motion will inevitably be induce at high speed when a engine be thus poise upon the central drive wheel and there will also be more of the rock or sinuous motion locomotive however intend to achieve high speed or to draw heavy load be now generally make with eight wheel and vary as the square of the velocity of they motion or nearly so and the power necessary to impart a increase velocity vary nearly as the cube of such increase velocity to double the velocity of a steam vessel therefore will require four time the amount of tractive force and as that quadruple force must act through twice the distance in the same time a engine capable of exert eight time the original power will be require -lrb- 1 -rrb- 534 _ q _ -- in the case of a board move in water in the manner of a paddle float or in the case of move water impinging on a stationary board what will be the pressure produce by the impact _ a _ -- the pressure produce upon a flat board by striking water at right angle to the surface of the board will be equal to the weight of a column of water have the surface strike as a base and for its altitude twice the height due to the velocity with which the board move through the water if the board strike the water obliquely the resistance will be less but no very reliable law have yet be discover to determine its amount 535 _ q _ -- will not the resistance of a vessel in move through the water be much less than that of a flat board of the area of the influence she speed since the vessel of the same sectional area must manifestly put in motion a column of water of the same magnitude and with the same velocity _ a _ -- a vessel will not strike the _ -- do the resistance produce by this friction increase with the velocity _ a _ -- it increase nearly as the square of the velocity at two nautical mile per hour the thrust necessary to overcome the call this resistance by the name of friction it be partly perhaps mainly due to the viscidity or adhesion of the water 539 _ q _ -- perhaps at high velocity this resistance may become less _ a _ -- solid body but any such conclusion be mere speculation since no experiment illustrative of this question have yet be make 540 _ q _ -- will a vessel experience more resistance in move in salt water water but as the notation be proportionably greater in the salt water the resistance will be the same with the same weight carry 541 _ q _ -- discard for the present the subject of friction and look instead of be away drive forcibly from the bow be open gradually so that every particle of water may be move aside slowly at first and then faster like the ball of a pendulum until it reach the position of the midship frame at which point it will have come to a state of rest and then again like a return pendulum vibrate back in the same way until it come to rest at the stern it be not difficult to describe mechanically the line which the water should pursue if a endless web of paper be put into uniform motion and a pendulum carry a pencil or brush be hang in front of it then such pendulum will trace on the paper the proper water line of the ship or the line which the water should pursue in order that no power may be lose except that which be lose in friction it be find however in practice that vessel form with water line on this principle be not much superior to ordinary vessel in the facility with which they pass through the water : and this point to the conclusion that in ordinary vessel of good form the amount of power consume in overcome the resistance due to the wave at the bow and the partial vacuity at the stern be not so great as have heretofore be suppose and fairy at that speed equal to 624 nominal horse power structure and operation of paddle wheel 551 _ q _ -- will you describe the configuration and mode of action of the paddle wheel in general use _ a _ -- there be two kind of paddle wheel in extensive use the one be the ordinary radial wheel in which the float be fix on arm radiate from the center and the other the feather wheel in which each float be hang upon a center and be so govern by suitable mechanism as to be always keep in nearly the vertical position in the radial wheel there be some loss of power from oblique action whereas in the feather wheel there be little or no loss from this cause but in every kind of paddle there be a loss of power from the recession of the water from the float board or the _ slip _ as it be commonly call and this loss be the necessary condition of the resistance for the propulsion of the vessel be create in a fluid the slip be express by the difference between the speed of the wheel and the speed of the vessel and the larger this difference be the greater the loss of power from slip must be -- the consumption of steam in the engine be proportionate to the velocity of the wheel and the useful effect be proportionate to the speed of the ship 552 _ q _ -- the resistance necessary for propulsion will not be situate at the circumference of the wheel _ a _ -- in the feather wheel where every part of any one immerged float move forward with the same horizontal velocity the pressure or resistance may be suppose to be concentrate in the center of the float whereas in the common radial wheel this can not be the case for as the outer edge of the float move more rapidly than the edge nearest the center of the wheel the outer part of the float be the most effectual in propulsion the point at which the outer and inner portion of the float just balance one another in propel effect be call the _ center of pressure _ and if all the resistance be concentrate in this point they would have the same effect as before in resist the rotation of the wheel the resistance upon any one move float board totally immerse in the water will when the vessel be at rest obviously vary as the square of its distance from the center of motion -- the resistance of a fluid vary with the square of the velocity but except when the wheel be sink to the axle or altogether immerse in the water it be impossible under ordinary circumstance for one float to be totally immerse without other be immerse partially whereby the arc describe by the extremity of the paddle arm will become greater than the arc describe by the inner edge of the float and consequently the resistance upon any part of the float will increase in a higher ratio than the square of its distance from the center of motion -- the position of the center of pressure be at the same time correspondingly affect in the feather wheel the position of the center of pressure of the enter and emerge float be continually change from the lower edge of the float -- where it be when the float be enter or leave the water -- to the center of the float which be its position when the float be wholly immerged but in the radial wheel the center of pressure can never rise so high as the center of the float 553 _ q _ -- all this relate to the action of the paddle when the vessel be at rest : will you explain its action when the vessel be in motion _ a _ -- when the wheel of a coach roll along the ground any point of its periphery describe in the air a curve which be term a cycloid any point within the periphery trace a prolate or protracted cycloid and any point exterior to the periphery trace a curtate or contract cycloid -- the prolate cycloid partaking more of the nature of a straight line and the curtate cycloid more of the nature of a circle the action of a paddle wheel in the water resemble in this respect that of the wheel of a carriage run along the ground : that point in the radius of the paddle of which the rotative speed be just equal to the velocity of the vessel will describe a cycloid point nearer the center prolate cycloid and point further from the center curtate cycloid the circle describe by the point whose velocity equal the velocity of the ship be call the _ roll circle _ and the resistance due to the difference of velocity of the rolling circle and center of pressure be that which operate in the propulsion of the vessel the resistance upon any part of the float therefore will vary as the square of its distance from the rolling circle suppose the float to be totally immerged but take into account the greater length of time during which the extremity of the paddle act whereby the resistance will be make greater we shall not err far in estimate the resistance upon any point at the third power of its distance from the rolling circle in the case of light immersion and the 25 power in the case of deep immersion 554 _ q _ -- how be the position of the center of pressure to be determine _ a _ -- with the foregoing assumption which accord sufficiently with experiment to justify its acceptation the position of the center of pressure may be find by the follow rule : -- from the radius of the wheel substract the radius of the rolling circle to the remainder add the depth of the paddle board and divide the fourth power of the sum by four time the depth from the cube root of the quotient subtract the difference between the radius of the wheel and roll circle and the remainder will be the distance of the center of pressure from the upper edge of the paddle 555 _ q _ -- how do you find stroke per minute the quotient will be the diameter in foot of the rolling circle the diameter of the circle in which the center of pressure move or the effective diameter of the wheel be know and also the diameter of the rolling circle we at once find the excess of the velocity of the wheel over the vessel 556 _ q _ -- will you illustrate these rule by a example _ a _ -- a steam vessel of large diameter of screw can be employ the ordinary screw or helix with two blade seem to be as effective as any other and it be the most easily construct if however the screw be restricted in diameter or if the vessel be require to tow or will have to encounter habitually strong head wind it will be preferable to employ a screw with a increase pitch and also of such other configuration that it will recover from the water some portion of the power that have be expend in slip 593 _ q _ -- how can this be do _ a _ -- there be screw which be intend to accomplish this object already in actual use when there be much slip a centrifugal velocity be give to the water and the screw indeed if the engine be set on when the vessel be at rest act very much as a centrifugal fan would do if place in the same situation the water project outward by the centrifugal force escape in the line of least resistance which be to the surface and if there be a high column of water over the screw or in other word if the screw be deeply immerse then the centrifugal action be resist to a greater extent and there will be less slip produce the easiest expedient therefore for obviate loss by slip be to sink the screw deeply in the water but as there be obvious limit to the application of this remedy the next best device be to recover and render available for propulsion some part of the power which have be expend in give motion to the water one device for do this consist in place the screw well forward in the dead wood so that it shall be overhang by the stern of the ship the water force upward by the centrifugal action of the screw will by impinge on the overhang stern press the vessel forward in the water just in the same way as be do by the wind when act on a oblique sail i believe the two revolving vane without any twist or obliquity on they at all would propel a vessel if set well forward in the dead wood or beneath the bottom merely by the ascent of the water up the inclined plane of the vessel 's run and at all event a screw so place would in my judgment aid materially in propel the vessel when she progress be resist by head wind 594 _ q _ -- but you say there be some kind of screw which profess to accomplish this -lrb- illustration : fig 49 the earl of dundonald 's propeller -rrb- _ a _ -- there be screw which profess to counteract the centrifugal velocity give to the water by impart to it a equal centripetal force the consequence of which will be that the water project backward by the screw instead of take the form of the frustum of a cone with its small end next the screw will take the form of a cylinder one of these form of screw be that patent by the earl of dundonald in 1843 and which be represent in fig 49 another be the form of screw already represent in fig 48 and which be patent by mr hodgson in 1844 mr hodgson bend the arm of he propeller backward not into the form of a triangle but into the form of a parabola to the end that the impact of the screw on the particle of the water may cause they to converge to a focus as the ray of light would do in a parabolic reflector but this particular configuration be not important see that the same convergence which be give to the particle of the water with a screw of uniform pitch bent back into the form of a parabola will be give with a screw bent back into the form of a triangle if the pitch be suitably vary between the center and the circumference 595 _ q _ -- then the pitch may be vary in two way _ a _ -- yes : a screw may have a pitch increase in the direction of the length as would happen in the case of a spiral stair if every successive step in the ascent be thicker than the one below it or it may increase from the center to the circumference as would happen in the case of a spiral stair if every step be thinner at the center of the lower than at its outer wall when the pitch of a screw increase in the direction of its length the lead edge of the screw enter the water without shock or impact as the advance of the lead edge per revolution will not be greater than the advance of the vessel when the pitch of a screw increase in the direction of its diameter the central part of the screw will advance with only the same velocity as the water so that it can not communicate any centrifugal velocity to the water and the whole slip as well as the whole propel pressure will occur at the outer part of the screw blade 596 _ q _ -- be there any advantage derive from these form of screw _ a _ -- there be a slight advantage but it be so slight as hardly to balance the increase trouble of manufacture and consequently they be not generally or widely adopt 597 _ q _ -- what other kind of screw be there propose to themselves the same or similar object _ a _ -- there be the corrugated screw the arm of which be corrugated so as it be to gear with the water during its revolution and thereby prevent it from acquire a centrifugal velocity then there be griffith 's screw which have a large ball at its center which by the suction it create at its hinder part in pass through the water produce a converge force which partly counteract the divergent action of the arm finally there be holm 's screw which have now be apply to a good number of vessel with success 598 _ q _ -- will you describe the configuration and action of holm 's screw _ a _ -- first then the screw increase in the direction of its length and this increase be very rapid at the follow edge so that in fact the follow edge stand in the plane of the shaft or in the vertical longitudinal plane of the vessel then the end of the arm be bent over into a curved flange the edge of which point astern and the point where this curved flange join the follow edge of the screw be form not into a angle but into a portion of a sphere so that this corner resemble the bowl of a spoon when the screw be put into revolution the water be encounter by the lead edge of the screw without shock as its advance be only equal to the advance of the vessel and before the screw leave the water it be project directly astern at the same time the curved flange at the rim of the screw prevent the dispersion of the water in a radial direction and it consequently assume the form of a column or cylinder of water project backward from the ship 599 _ q _ -- what be the nature of beattle 's and be less affect by the listing or heel over of the ship a small steam power however act very advantageously in aid of sail for not only do the operation of the sail in reduce the resistance of the hull virtually increase the screw 's diameter but the screw by reduce the resistance which have to be overcome by the sail and by increase the speed of the vessel enable the sail to act with greater efficiency of the screw and that the screw also add to the efficiency of the sail 611 _ q _ -- what be the comparative cost of transport merchandise in paddle steamer of full power in screw steamer of the aid of uniform and constant wind such as the trade wind or the monsoon sailing ship of large size will be able to carry more cheaply than any other species of vessel but where the wind be irregular and there be not much sea room or for such circumstance as exist in the channel or mediterranean trade screw vessel with auxiliary power will constitute the cheapest instrument of conveyance 612 _ q _ -- be there any fact record illustrative of the accuracy of this conclusion _ a _ -- a full paddle vessel of 1000 ton burden and 350 horse power will carry about 400 ton of cargo besides ton burden and 100 horse power will carry the same amount of cargo besides she coal on the same voyage and the expense of the voyage include wear and tear depreciation & c will be not much more than 60_l _ a auxiliary screw vessel therefore can carry merchandise at one third of the cost of a full-powered paddle vessel by similar comparison make between the expense of convey merchandise in auxiliary screw steamer and sailing ship on coast voyage it appear that the cost in screw steamer be about one third less than in the sailing ship the greater expedition of the screw steamer much more than compensate for the expense which the maintenance of the machinery involve screw and paddle combine 613 _ q _ -- would not a screw combine with paddle act in a similarly advantageous way as a -- if the vessel require new boiler the best course of procedure would be to work a single engine give motion to the screw with high pressure steam and to let the waste steam from the high pressure engine work the paddle engine in this way the power might be double without any increase expenditure of fuel per hour and there would be a diminish expenditure per voyage in the proportion of the increase speed 616 _ q _ -- what would the increase speed be by double the power _ a _ -- the increase would be in the proportion of the cube root of 1 to the cube root of 2 or it would be 125 time greater if therefore the exist speed be 10 mile it would be increase to 12-1\/2 mile by double the power and the vessel would ply with about a fourth less coal by increase the power in the manner suggest 617 _ q _ -- be not high pressure steam dangerous in steam vessel _ a _ -- not necessarily so and it have now be introduce into a good number of steam vessel with satisfactory result in the case of locomotive engine where it be use so widely very few accident have occur and in steam vessel the only additional source of danger be the salting of the boiler this may be prevent either by the use of fresh water in the boiler or by practise a larger amount of blow off to insure which it should be impossible to diminish the amount of water send into the boiler by the feed pump and the excess should be discharge overboard through a valve near the water level of the boiler which valve be govern by a float that will rise or fall with the fluctuating level of the water if the float be a copper ball a little water should be introduce into it before it be solder or braze up which will insure a equality of pressure within and without the ball and a leakage of water into it will then be less likely to take place a stone float however be cheaper and if properly balance will be equally effective all steam vessel should have a large excess of boil feed water constantly flow into the boiler and a large quantity of water constantly blow off through the surface valve which be govern by float will open and let the superfluous water escape whenever the water level rise too high in this way the boiler will be keep from salt and priming will be much less likely to occur the great problem of steam navigation be the economy of fuel since the quantity of fuel consume by a vessel will very much determine whether she be profitable or otherwise notwithstanding the momentous nature of this condition however the consumption of fuel in steam vessel be a point to which very little attention have be pay and no efficient means have yet be adopt in steam vessel to insure that measure of economy which be know to be attainable and which have be attain already in other department of engineering in which the benefit of such economy be of less weighty import it need nothing more than the establishment of a efficient system of registration in steam vessel to insure a large and rapid economy in the consumption of fuel as this quality would then become the test of a engineer 's proficiency and would determine the measure of he fame in the case of the cornish engine a saving of more than half the fuel be speedily effect by the introduction of the simple expedient of registration in agricultural engine a like economy have speedily follow from a like arrangement yet in both of these case the benefit of a large saving be less eminent than they would be in the case of steam navigation and it be to be hope that this expedient of improvement will now be speedily adopt chapter x its place the air pump barrel be of brass to which be bolt a cast iron mouth piece with a port for carry the water to the hot well within the hot well the delivery valve which consist of a common flap the condenser -- the jet striking against the barrel of the air pump the air pump rod be maintain in its vertical position by means of guide the lower end of which be bolt to the mouth of the pump and between the cylinder and condenser _ a _ -- the pipe lead to the condenser from the cylinder be make somewhat bell mouth where it join the condenser and the gland for compress the packing be make of a gland may be draw back without be jam upon the enlarged part of the pipe and the enlargement of the pipe toward the condenser prevent the air pump barrel from offer any impediment to the free egress of the steam the gland be make altogether in four piece : the ring which press the packing be make distinct from the flange to which the bolt be attach which force the gland against the packing and both ring and flange be make in two piece to enable they to be get over the pipe the ring be half check in the direction of its depth and be introduce without any other support to keep the half together than what be afford by the interior of the stuffing box and the flange be half check in the direction of its thickness so that the bolt which press down the ring by pass through this into the jacket but the eduction pipe do not fit quite tight into this contract part but while in close contact on the lower side have about 1\/32nd of a inch of space between the top of the pipe and the cylinder so as to permit the trunnion to wear to that extent without throw a strain upon the pipe the eduction pipe be attach to the condenser by a flange joint and the bolt hole be all make somewhat oblong in the perpendicular direction so as to permit the pipe to be slightly lower should such a operation be render necessary by the wear of the trunnion bearing but in practice the wear of the trunnion bearing be find to be so small as to be almost inappreciable 624 _ q _ -- will you describe the valve and valve casing _ a _ -- the length of the valve casing be 16-1\/2 inch and its however the upper brass will generally acquire a good deal of play after some amount of wear the bolt be work slack in the hole though accurately fit at first and it appear expedient therefore either to make the bolt very large and the socket through which they pass very deep or to let one brass fit into the other 632 _ q _ -- how be the trunnion plummer block make _ a _ -- the trunnion plummer plummer block upon the lower frame as be sometimes do for the cylinder be press from the steam trunnion by the steam and draw in the direction of the condenser by the vacuum have a continual tendency to approach one another and as they wear slightly toward midship there would be no power of readjustment unless the plummer block be movable the flange of the trunnion should always fit tight against the plummer block side but there should be a little play sideways at the neck of the trunnion so that the cylinder may be enable to expand when heat without throw a undue strain upon the trunnion support 633 _ q _ -- what kind of paddle wheel be supply with these oscillate engine _ a _ -- the wheel be of the feather kind 9 foot 8 inch in diameter measure to the edge of the float and there be of play leave upon they for if any upward motion be permit it will be impossible to prevent the trunnion packing from leak direct act screw engine 640 _ q _ -- will you describe the configuration and another but numerous paddle vessel be ply successfully that be propel by a single engine and the screw offer still greater facility than paddle for such a mode of construction in the screw engine refer to as the cylinder be lay upon its side there be no unbalanced weight to be lift up every stroke and the crank whereby the screw shaft be turn round consist of two disc with a heavy side intend to balance the momentum of the piston and its connection but these counter-weight by they gravitation also prevent the connect rod and crank from continue in the same line when the engine be stop and inch long and to relieve the valve from the great friction due to the pressure on so large a surface a balance piston be place over the back of the valve to which it be connect by a strong link and the upward pressure on this piston be nearly the same as the downward pressure on the valve it follow that the friction be extinguish and the valve can be move with great case with one hand the balance piston be 21 inch in diameter in the original construction of this balance piston two fault be commit the passage communicate between the condenser and the top of the balance piston be too small and the pin at the end of the link connect the valve and balance piston be form with a inadequate amount of bear surface it follow from this misproportion that the balance piston be adjust to take off nearly the whole of the pressure lift the valve off the face at the beginning of each stroke for the escape of the steam into the eduction passage momentarily impair the vacuum subsist there and owe to the smallness of the passage lead to the space above the balance piston the vacuum subsist in that space could not be impair with equal rapidity the balance piston therefore rise by the upward pressure upon it momentarily predominate over the downward pressure on the valve but this fault be correct by enlarge the communicate passage between the top of the balance piston and the eduction pipe the smallness of the pin at the end of the link connect the valve and balance piston cause the surface to cut into one another and to wear very rapidly and the pin and eye in this situation should be large in diameter and as long as they can be get as they be not so easily lubricate as the other bearing about the engine and be moreover keep at a high temperature by the steam the balance piston be pack in the same way as the main piston of the engine its cylinder which be only a few inch in length be set on the top of the valve casing and a trunk project upward from its center to enable the connect link to rise up in it to attain the necessary length -lrb- illustration : fig 52 connect rod messr bourne & co -rrb- 647 _ q _ -- what be the diameter of the piston rod the result of this arrangement be that a large part of the oil or water feed into the bearing of the shaft be drive by the centrifugal action of the disc to the surface of the crank pin and in this way the crank pin may be oil or cool with water in a very effectual manner to intercept the water or oil which the disc thus drive out by they centrifugal action a light paddle box or splash board of thin sheet brass be make to cover the upper part of each of the disc and a oil cup with depend wick be support by the top of these paddle box which wick be touch at each revolution of the crank by a bridge standing in the middle of a oil cup attach to the crank pin the oil be wipe from the wick by the project bridge at each revolution and subside into the cup from whence it proceed to lubricate the crank pin bearing this be the expedient commonly employ to oil the crank pin of direct act engine but in the engine now describe there be over and above this expedient the communicate passage from the shaft bearing to the surface of the pin by which mean any amount of cooling or lubrication can be administer to the crank pin bearing without the necessity of stop or slow the engine -lrb- there be still much room for improvement and indeed various source of economy be at present visible which if properly develop would materially reduce the expense of the locomotive power in all engine the great source of expense be the fuel and although the consumption of fuel have be greatly reduce within the last ten or fifteen year it be capable of be still further reduce by certain easy expedient of improvement which therefore it be important should be universally apply one of these expedient consist in heat the feed water by the waste steam and the feed water should in every case be send into the boiler _ boil hot _ instead of be quite cold as be at present generally the case the port of the cylinder should be as large as possible the expansion of the steam should be carry to a greater extent and in the case of engine with outside cylinder the waste steam should circulate entirely round the cylinder before escape by the blast pipe the escape of heat from the boiler should be more carefully prevent and the engine should be balance by weight on the wheel to obviate a waste of power by yaw on the rail the most important expedient of all however lie in the establishment of a system of register the performance of all new engine in order that competition may stimulate the different constructor to the attainment of the utmost possible economy and under the stimulus of comparison and notoriety a large measure of improvement would speedily ensue the benefit consequent on public competition be abundantly illustrate by the rapid diminution of the consumption of fuel in the case of agricultural engine when this stimulus be present chapter xi of various form application and appliance of the steam engine in the english edition of this work the first part of this and to messr ab & e latta of cincinnatus work on the right principle be due the credit which they claim in they circular as follow : we claim to be the _ original _ and first _ projector _ of the _ first successful steam fire engine _ in the world 's history there have be many attempt at make a machine of such construction as would answer to extinguish fire but none of they prove to be available in a sufficiently short space of time to warrant they use as a fire apparatus we hold that a steam fire engine should be of such nature as to be bring into requisition in as short a space of time as be necessary to get the machine on the ground and the hose lay and ready to work : that be suppose the fire to be within one square of the place where the steamer be located the object in locate a machine at any point be to protect that immediate vicinity and it be therefore absolutely necessary to have it available in the shortest space of time and that with unerring certainty we think that reliability be of the greatest importance to the protection of a city from fire as everything be dependent on the _ work _ of such apparatus in time and for this reason no expense should be spare on
