steam engine construction of engine 700 _ q _ -- what be the quality which should be possess by the iron of which the cylinder of steam engine be make _ a _ -- the general ambition in make cylinder be to make they sound and hard but it be expedient also to make they tough so as to approach as nearly as possible to the state of malleable iron this may be do by mix in the furnace as many different kind of iron as possible and it may be set down as a general rule in iron founding that the greater the number of the kind of metal enter into the composition of any cast the denser and tougher it will be the constituent atom of the different kind of iron appear to be of different size and the mixture of different kind maintain the toughness while it add to the density and cohesive power hot blast iron be at one time generally believe to be weaker than cold blast iron but it be now question whether it be not the stronger of the two the cohesive strength of unmixed iron be not in proportion to its specific gravity and its elasticity and power to resist shock appear to become greater as the specific gravity become less no 3 and 4 be the strongest iron in most case iron melt in a cupola be not so strong as when remelt in a air furnace and when run into green sand it be not reckon so strong as when run into dry sand or loam the quality of the fuel and even the state of the weather exert a influence on the quality of the iron : smelting furnace on the cold blast principle have long be know to yield better iron in winter than in summer probably from the existence of less moisture in the air and it would probably be find to accomplish a improvement in the quality of the iron if the blast be make to pass through a vessel contain muriate of lime by which the moisture of the air would be extract the expense of such a preparation would not be considerable as by subsequent evaporation the salt might be use over and over again for the same purpose 701 _ q _ -- will you explain the process of cast cylinder _ a _ -- the mould into which the metal be pour be build up of brick and loam the loam be clay and sand ground together in a mill with the addition of a little horse-dung to give it a fibrous structure and prevent crack the loam board by which the circle of the cylinder be to be sweep be attach to a upright iron bar at the distance of the radius of the cylinder and a cylindrical shell of brick be build up which be plaster on the inside with loam and make quite smooth by traverse the perpendicular loam board round it a core be then form in a similar manner but so much smaller as to leave a space between the shell and the core equal to the thickness of the cylinder and into this space the melt metal be pour whatever nozzle or projection be require upon the cylinder must be form by means of wooden pattern which be build into the shell and subsequently withdraw but where a number of cylinder of the same kind be require it be advisable to make these pattern of iron which will not be liable to warp or twist while the loam be be dry before the iron be cast into the mould the interior of the mould must be cover with finely powdered charcoal -- or blacken as it be technically term and the secret of make finely skin casting lie in use plenty of blacken in loam and dry sand casting the charcoal should be mix with thick clay water and apply until it be a eighth of a inch thick or more the surface should be then very carefully smooth or sleek and if the metal have be judiciously mixed and the mould thoroughly dry the casting be sure to be a fine one dry sand and loam casting should be as much as possible make in box the mould may thereby be more rapidly and more effectually dry and better casting will be get with a less expense 702 _ q _ -- will you explain the next operation which a cylinder undergo _ a _ -- the next stage be the boring and in boring cylinder of 74 inch diameter the boring bar must move so as to make one revolution in about 4-1\/2 minute at which speed the cutter will move at the rate of about 5 foot per minute in boring brass the speed must be slower the common rate at which the tool move in boring brass air pump be about 3 foot per minute if this speed be materially exceed the tool will be spoil and the pump make taper the speed proper for bore a cylinder will answer for bore the brass air pump of the same engine a brass air pump of 36-1\/2 inch diameter require the bar to make one turn in about three minute which be also the speed proper for a cylinder 60 inch in diameter to bear a brass air pump 36-1\/2 inch in diameter require a week a iron one require 48 hour and a copper one 24 hour in turn a malleable iron shaft 12-3\/4 inch in diameter the shaft should make about five turn per minute which be equivalent to a speed in the tool of about 16 foot per minute but this speed may be exceed if soap and water be plentifully run on the point of the tool a boring mill of which the speed may be vary from one turn in six minute to twenty-five turn in one minute will be suitable for all ordinary want that can occur in practice 703 _ q _ -- be there any precaution necessary to be observe in order that the boring may be truly effect _ a _ -- in fix a cylinder into the boring mill great care must be take that it be not screw down unequally and indeed it will be impossible to bear a large cylinder in a horizontal mill without be oval unless the cylinder be carefully gauge when stand on end and be set up by screw when lay in the mill until it again assume its original form a large cylinder will inevitably become oval if lay upon its side and if while under the tension due to its own weight it be bore round it will become oval again when set upon end if the bottom be cast in the cylinder will be probably find to be round at one end and oval at the other unless a vertical boring mill be employ or the precaution here suggest be adopt 704 _ q _ -- do the boring tool make the cylinder sufficiently smooth for the reception of the piston _ a _ -- many engine maker give no other finish to they cylinder but messr penn grind they cylinder after they be bore by lay they on they side and rub a piece of lead with a cross iron handle like that of a rolling stone and smear with emery and oil backward and forward -- the cylinder be gradually turn round so as to subject every part successively to the operation the lead by which this grind be accomplish be cast in the cylinder whereby it be form of the right curve but the part of the cylinder in which it be cast should be previously heat by a hot iron else the metal may be crack by the sudden heat 705 _ q _ -- how be the part of a piston fit together so as to be perfectly steam tight _ a _ -- the old practice be to depend chiefly upon grind as the means of make the ring tight upon the piston or upon one another but scrape be now chiefly rely on some maker however finish they steam surface by grind they with powdered turkey stone and oil a slight grind or polish with powdered turkey stone and oil appear to be expedient in ordinary case and may be conveniently accomplish by set the piston on a revolving table and hold the ring stationary by a cross piece of wood while the table turn round piece of wood may be interpose between the ring and the body of the piston to keep the ring nearly in its right position but these piece of wood should be fit so loosely as to give some side play else the disposition would arise to wear the flange of the piston into a groove 706 _ q _ -- what kind of tool be use for finish surface by scrape _ a _ -- a flat file bent and sharpen at the end make a eligible scraper for the first stage or a flat file sharpen at the end and use like a chisel for wood a three-cornered file sharpen at all the corner be the best instrument for finish the operation the scrape tool should be of the best steel and should be carefully sharpen at short interval on a turkey stone so as to maintain a fine edge 707 _ q _ -- will you explain the method of fitting together the valve and cylinder face _ a _ -- both face must first be plane then file accord to the indication of a metallic straight edge and subsequently of a thick metallic face plate and finally scrape very carefully until the face plate bear equally all over the surface in plane any surface the catch which retain the surface on the plane machine should be relax previously to the last cut to obviate distortion from spring to ascertain whether the face plate bear equally smear it over with a little red ochre and oil and move the face plate slightly which will fix the color upon the prominent point this operation be to be repeat frequently and as the work advance the quantity of color matter be to be diminish until finally it be spread over the face plate in a thin film which only dim the brightness of the plate the surface at this stage must be rub firmly together to make the point of contact visible and the higher point will become slightly cloud while the other part be leave more or less in shade if too small a quantity of color matter be use at first it will be difficult to form a just conception of the general state of the surface as the prominent point will alone be indicate whereas the use of a large quantity of color matter in the latter stage would destroy the delicacy of the test the face plate afford the number of bear point which it be desirable to establish on the surface of the work depend on the use to which the surface be to be apply but whether it be to be finish with great elaboration or otherwise the bearing point should be distribute equally over the surface face plate or planometer as they be sometimes term be supply by most of the maker of engineering tool every factory should be abundantly supply with they and also with steel straight edge and there should be a master face plate and a master straight edge for the sole purpose of testing from time to time the accuracy of those in use 708 _ q _ -- be the operation of surface which you have describe necessary in the case of all slide valve _ a _ -- yes and in fitting the face of a d valve great care must in addition be take that the valve be not make conical for unless the back be exactly parallel with the face it will be impossible to keep the packing from be rapidly cut away when the valve be lay upon the face plate the back must be make quite fair along the whole length by draw filing accord to the indication of a straight edge and the distance from the face to the extreme height of the back must be make identical at each extremity 709 _ q _ -- when you describe the operation of bore the cylinder you state that the cylinder when lay upon its side become oval will not this change of figure distort the cylinder face _ a _ -- it be not only in the boring of the cylinder that it be necessary to be careful that there be no change of figure for it will be impossible to face the valve truly in the case of large cylinder unless the cylinder be place on end or internal prop be introduce to prevent the collapse due to the cylinder 's weight it may be add that the change of figure be not instantaneous but become greater after some continuance of the strain than it be at first so that in gauge a cylinder to ascertain the difference of diameter when it be place on its side it should have lie some day upon its side to ensure the accuracy of the operation 710 _ q _ -- how be any flaw in the valve or cylinder face remedy _ a _ -- should a hole occur either in the valve in the cylinder or any other part where the surface require to be smooth it may be plug up with a piece of cast iron as nearly as possible of the same texture bear out the faulty part and afterward widen the hole with a eccentric drill so that it will be of the least diameter at the mouth the hole may go more than half through the iron : fit then a plug of cast iron roughly by filing and hammer it into the hole whereby the plug will become rivet in it and its surface may then be file smooth square piece may be let in after the same fashion the hole be make dovetail and the piece thus fit will never come out 711 _ q _ -- when cylinder be face with brass how be the face attach to the cylinder _ a _ -- brass face be put upon valve or cylinder by means of small brass screw tap into the iron with conical neck for the retention of the brass : they be screw by means of a square head which when the screw be in its place be cut off and file smooth in some case the face be make of extra thickness and a rim not so thick run round it form a step or recess for the reception of brass rivet the head of which be clear of the face 712 _ q _ -- what be the best material for valve face _ a _ -- much trouble be experience with every modification of valve face but cast iron work upon cast iron be perhaps the best combination yet introduce a usual practice be to pin brass face on the cylinder allow the valve to retain its cast iron face some maker employ brass valve and other pin brass on the valve leave the cylinder with a cast iron face if brass valve be use it be advisable to plane out two groove across the face and to fill they up with hard cast iron to prevent rutting speculum metal and steel have be try for the cylinder face but only with moderate success in some case the brass get into rut but the most prevalent affection be a degradation of the iron owe to the action of the steam and the face assume a granular appearance something like loaf sugar this action show itself only at particular spot and chiefly about the angle of the port or valve face at first the action be slow but when once the steam have work a passage for itself the cut away become very rapid and in a short time it will be impossible to prevent the engine from heating when stop owe to the leakage of steam through the valve into the condenser copper steam pipe seem to have some galvanic action on valve face and malleable iron pipe have sometimes be substitute but they be speedily wear out by oxidation and the scale of rust which be carry on by the steam scratch the valve and cylinder so that the use of copper pipe be the least evil 713 _ q _ -- will you explain in what manner the joint of a engine be make _ a _ -- rust joint be not now much use in engine of any kind yet it be necessary that the engineer should be acquaint with the manner of they formation one ounce of sal-ammoniac in powder be mingle with 18 ounce or a pound of boring of cast iron and a sufficiency of water be add to wet the mixture thoroughly which should be do some hour before it be want for use some person add about half a ounce of flower of brimstone to the above proportion and a little sludge from the grindstone trough this cement be caulk into the joint with a caulking iron about three quarter of a inch wide and one quarter of a inch thick and after the caulking be finish the bolt of the joint may be try to see if they can not be further tighten the skin of the iron must in all case be break where a rust joint be to be make and if the place be greasy the surface must be well rub over with nitric acid and then wash with water till no grease remain the oil about engine have a tendency to damage rust joint by recover the oxide coppersmith staunch the edge of they plate and rivet by means of a cement form of pounded quicklime with serum of blood or white of egg and in copper boiler such a substance may be useful in stop the impalpable leak which sometimes occur though roman cement appear to be nearly as effectual 714 _ q _ -- will you explain the method of case harden the part of engine _ a _ -- the most common plan for case harden consist in the insertion of the article to be operate upon among horn or leather cutting hone dust or animal charcoal in a iron box provide with a tight lid which be then put into a furnace for a period answerable to the depth of steel require in some case the plan pursue by the gunsmith may be employ with convenience the article be insert in a sheet iron case amid bone dust often not burn the lid of the box be tie on with wire and the joint lute with clay the box be heat to redness as quickly as possible and keep half a hour at a uniform heat : its contents be then suddenly immerse in cold water the more unwieldy portion of a engine may be case harden by prussiate of potash -- a salt make from animal substance compose of two atom of carbon and one of nitrogen and which operate on the same principle as the charcoal the iron be heat in the fire to a dull red heat and the salt be either sprinkle upon it or rub on in a lump or the iron be rub in the salt in powder the iron be then return to the fire for a few minute and finally immerse in water by some person the salt be suppose to act unequally as if there be greasy spot upon the iron which the salt refuse to touch and the effect under any circumstance be exceedingly superficial nevertheless upon all part not expose to wear a sufficient coating of steel may be obtain by this process 715 _ q _ -- what kind of iron be most suitable for the work part of a engine _ a _ -- in the malleable iron work of engine scrap iron have long be use and consider preferable to other kind but if the part be to be case harden as be now the usual practice the use of scrap iron be to be reprehend as it be almost sure to make the part twist in the case harden process in case harden iron absorb carbon which cause it to swell and as some kind of iron have a greater capacity for carbon than other kind in case harden they will swell more and any such unequal enlargement in the constituent portion of a piece of iron will cause it to change its figure in some case case hardening have cause such a twist of the part of a engine that they could not afterward be fit together it be preferable therefore to make such part as be to be case harden to any considerable depth of lowmoor bowling or indian iron which be homogeneous will absorb carbon equally and will not twist 716 _ q _ -- what be the composition of the brass use for engine bearing _ a _ -- the brass bearing of a engine be compose principally of copper and tin a very good brass for steam engine bearing consist of old copper 112 lb tin 12-1\/2 lb zinc 2 or 3 oz and if new tile copper be use there should be 13 lb of tin instead of 12-1\/2 lb a tough brass for engine work consist of 1-1\/2 lb tin 1-1\/2 lb zinc and 10 lb copper a brass for heavy bearing 2-1\/2 oz tin 1\/2 oz zinc and 1 lb copper there be a great difference in the length of time brass wear as make by different manufacturer but the difference arise as much from a different quantity of surface as from a vary composition of the metal brass should always be make strong and thick as when thin they collapse upon the bearing and increase the friction and the wear 717 _ q _ -- how be babbitt 's metal for line the bush of machinery compound _ a _ -- babbitt 's patent lining metal for bush have be largely employ in the bush of locomotive axle and other machinery : it be compose of 1 lb of copper 1 lb regulus of antimony and 10 lb of tin or other similar proportion the presence of tin be the only material condition the copper be first melted then the antimony be add with a small proportion of tin-charcoal be strew over the surface of the metal in the crucible to prevent oxidation the bush or article to be line have be cast with a recess for the soft metal be to be fit to a iron mould form of the shape and size of the bearing or journal allow a little in size for the shrinkage drill a hole for the reception of the soft metal say 1\/2 to 3\/4 inch diameter wash the part not to be tin with a clay wash to prevent the adhesion of the tin wet the part to be tin with alcohol and sprinkle fine sal-ammoniac upon it heat the article until fume arise from the ammonia and immerse it in a kettle of banca tin care be take to prevent oxidation when sufficiently tin the bush should be soak in water to take off any particle of ammonia that may remain upon it as the ammonia would cause the metal to blow wash with pipe clay and dry then heat the bush to the melting point of tin wipe it clean and pour in the metal give it sufficient head as it cool the bush should then be scour with fine sand to take off any dirt that may remain upon it and it be then fit for use this metal wear for a longer time than ordinary gun metal and its use be attend with very little friction if the bearing heat however from the stop of the oil hole or otherwise the metal will be melt out a metallic grease contain particle of tin in the state of a impalpable powder would probably be preferable to the lining of metal just describe 718 _ q _ -- can you state the composition of any other alloy that be use in engine work _ a _ -- the ordinary range of good yellow brass that file and turn well be about 4-1\/2 to 9 ounce of zinc to the pound of copper flange to stand brazing may be make of copper 1 lb zinc 1\/2 oz lead 3\/8 oz brazing solder when state in the order of they hardness be : - three part copper and one part zinc -lrb- very hard -rrb- eight part brass and one part zinc -lrb- hard -rrb- six part brass one part tin and one part zinc -lrb- soft -rrb- a very common solder for iron copper and brass consist of nearly equal part of copper and zinc muntz 's metal consist of forty part zinc and sixty of copper any proportion between the extreme of fifty part of zinc and fifty part copper and thirty-seven zinc and sixty-three copper will roll and work at a red heat but forty zinc to sixty copper be the proportion prefer bell metal such as be use for large bell consist of 4-1\/2 ounce to 5 ounce of tin to the pound of copper speculum metal consist of from 7-1\/2 ounce to 8-1\/2 ounce of tin to the pound of copper erection of engine 719 _ q _ -- will you explain the operation of erect a pair of side lever engine in the workshop a -- in begin the erection of side lever marine engine in the workshop the first step be to level the bed plate lengthway and across and strike a line up the center as near as possible in the middle which indent with a chisel in various place so that it may at any time be easily find again strike another line at right angle with this either at the cylinder or crank center by draw a perpendicular in the usual manner lay the other sole plate alongside at the right distance and strike a line at the cylinder or crank center of it also shift either sole plate a little endway until these two transverse line come into the same line which may be ascertain by apply a straight edge across the two sole plate strike the rest of the centre across and drive a pin into each corner of each sole plate which file down level so as to serve for point of reference at any future stage next try the cylinder or plumb it on the inside roughly and see how it be for height in order to ascertain whether much will be require to be chip off the bottom or whether more require to be chip off the one side than the other chip the cylinder bottom fair set it in its place plumb the cylinder very carefully with a straight edge and silk thread and scribe it so as to bring the cylinder mouth to the right height then chip the sole plate to suit that height the cylinder must then be try on again and the part file wherever they bear hard until the whole surface be well fitted next chip the place for the frame set up the framing and scribe the horizontal part of the jaw with the scriber use for the bottom of the cylinder the upright part be set to suit the shaft centre and the angular flange of cylinder where the stay be attach have be previously chip plumb and level the stake wedge with which the framing be set up preparatorily to the operation of scribe must be set so as to support equally the superincumbent weight else the framing will spring from rest unequally and it will be altogether impossible to fit it well these direction obviously refer exclusively to the old description of side lever engine with cast iron framing but there be more art in erect a engine of that kind with accuracy than in erect one of the direct action engine where it be chiefly turn or bore surface that have to be deal with 720 _ q _ -- how do you lay out the position of the centre of a side lever engine _ a _ -- in fix the position of the centre in side lever engine it appear to be the most convenient way to begin with the main center the height of the center of the cross head at half stroke above the plane of the main center be fix by the drawing of the engine which give the distance from the center of cross head at half stroke to the flange of the cylinder and from thence it be easy to find the perpendicular distance from the cylinder flange to the plane of the main center merely by put a straight edge along level from the position of the main center to the cylinder and measure from the cylinder flauge down to it raise or lower the straight edge until it rest at the proper measurement the main center be in that plane and the fore and aft position be to be find by plumbing up from the center line on the sole plate to find the paddle shaft center plumb up from the center line mark on the edge of the sole plate and on this line lay off from the plane of the main center the length of the connect rod if that length be already fix or otherwise the height fix in the drawing of the paddle shaft above the main center to fix the center for the parallel motion shaft when the parallel bar be connect with the cross head lay off from the plane of main center the length of the parallel bar from the center of the cylinder deduct the length of the radius crank and plumb up the central line of motion shaft lay off on this line measure from the plane of main center the length of the side rod this give the center of parallel motion shaft when the radius bar join the cross head as be the preferable practice where parallel motion be use the length of the connect rod be the distance from the center of the beam when level or the plane of the main center to the center of the paddle shaft the length of the side rod be the distance from the center line of the beam when level to the center of the cross head when the piston be at half stroke the length of the radius rod of the parallel motion be the distance from the point of attachment on the cross head or side rod when the piston be at half stroke to the extremity of the radius crank when the crank be horizontal or in engine with the parallel motion attach to the cross head it be the distance from the center of the pin of the radius crank when horizontal to the center of the cylinder have fix the center of the parallel motion shaft in the manner just describe it only remain to put the part together when the motion be attach to the cross head but when the motion be attach to the side rod the end of the parallel bar must not move in a perpendicular line but in a arc the verse sine of which bear the same ratio to that of the side lever that the distance from the top of the side rod to the point of attachment bear to the total length of the side rod 721 _ q _ -- how do you ascertain the accuracy of the parallel motion _ a _ -- the parallel motion when put in its place should be test by raise and lower the piston by means of the crane first set the beam level and shift in or out the motion shaft plummer block or bearing until the piston rod be upright then move the piston to the two extreme of its motion if at both end the cross head be throw too much out the stud in the beam to which the motion side rod be attach be too far out and must be shift nearer to the main center if at the extremity the cross head be throw too far in the stud in the beam be not out far enough if the cross head be throw in at the one end and out equally at the other the fault be in the motion side rod which must be lengthen or shorten to remedy the defect 722 _ q _ -- will you describe the method pursue in erect oscillate engine _ a _ -- the column here be of work iron and in the case of small engine there be a template make of wood and sheet iron in which the hole be set in the proper position by which the upper and lower frame be adjust but in the case of large engine the hole be set off by means of trammel the hole for the reception of the column be cast in the frame and be recess out internally : the boss encircle the hole be make quite level across and make very true with a face plate and the pillar which have be turn to a gauge be then insert the top frame be next put on and must bear upon the collar of the column so evenly that one of the column will not be bind by it harder than another if this point be not attain the surface must be further scrape until a perfect fit be establish the whole of the bearing in the best oscillating engine be fit by means of scrape and on no other mode of fitting can the same reliance be place for exactitude 723 _ q _ -- how do you set out the trunnion of oscillate engine so that they shall be at right angle with the interior of the cylinder _ a _ -- have bore the cylinder face the flange and bore out the hole through which the boring bar pass put a piece of wood across the mouth of the cylinder and jam it in and put a similar piece in the hole through the bottom of the cylinder mark the center of the cylinder upon each of these piece and put into the bear of each trunnion a iron plate with a small indentation in the middle to receive the center of a lathe and adjust screw to bring the center into any require position the cylinder must then be set in a lathe and hang by the centre of the trunnion and a straight edge must be put across the cylinder mouth and level so as to pass through the line in which the center of the cylinder lie another similar straight edge and similarly level must be similarly place across the cylinder bottom so as to pass through the central line of the cylinder and the cylinder be then to be turn round in the trunnion centres-the straight edge remain stationary which will at once show whether the trunnion be in the same horizontal plane as the center of the cylinder and if not the screw of the plate in the trunnion must be adjust until the central point of the cylinder just come to the straight edge whichever end of the cylinder be present to ascertain whether the trunnion stand in a transverse plane parallel to the cylinder flange it be only necessary to measure down from the flange to each trunnion center and if both these condition be satisfy the position of the centre may be suppose to be right the trunnion bearing be then turn and be fit into block of wood in which they run while the packing space be be turn out where many oscillate engine be make a lathe with four centre be use which make the use of straight edge in set out the trunnion superfluous 724 _ q _ -- will you explain how the slide valve of a marine engine be set _ a _ -- place the crank in the position correspond to the end of the stroke which can easily be do in the shop with a level or plumb line but in a steam vessel another method become necessary draw the transverse center line answering to the center line of the crank shaft on the sole plate of the engine or on the cylinder mouth if the engine be of the direct action kind describe a circle of the diameter of the crank pin upon the large eye of the crank and mark off on either side of the transverse center line a distance equal to the semi-diameter of the crank pin from the point thus find stretch a line to the edge of the circle describe on the large eye of the crank and bring round the crank shaft till the crank pin touch the stretch line the crank may thus be set at either end of its stroke when the crank be thus place at the end of the stroke the valve must be adjust so as to have the amount of lead or opening on the steam side which it be intend to give at the beginning of the stroke the eccentric must then be turn round upon the shaft until the notch in the eccentric rod come opposite the pin on the valve lever and fall into gear : mark upon the shaft the situation of the eccentric and put on the catch in the usual way the same process must be repeat for go astern shift round the eccentric to the opposite side of the shaft until the rod again fall into gear in set valve regard must of course be have to the kind of engine the arrangement of the lever and the kind of valve employ and in any general instruction it be impossible to specify every modification in the procedure that circumstance may render advisable 725 _ q _ -- be a similar method of set the valve adopt when the link motion be employ _ a _ -- each end of the link of the link motion have the kind of motion communicate to it that be due to the action of the particular eccentric with which that end be in connection in that form of the link motion in which the link itself be move up or down there be a different amount of lead for each different position of the link since to raise or lower the link be tantamount to turn the eccentric round on the shaft in that form of the link motion in which the link itself be not raise or lower but be susceptible of a motion round a center in the manner of a double end lever the lead continue uniform in both form of the link motion as the stroke of the valve may be vary to any require extent while the lap be a constant quantity the proportion of the lap relatively to the stroke of the valve may also be vary to any require extent and the amount of the lap relatively with the stroke of the valve determine the amount of the expansion in set the valve when fit with the link motion the mode of procedure be much the same as when it be move by a simple eccentric the first thing be to determine if the eccentric rod be of the proper length and this be do by set the valve at half stroke and turn round the eccentric mark each extremity of the travel of the end of the rod the valve attachment should be midway between these extreme and if it be not so it must be make so by lengthen or shorten the rod the forward and backward eccentric rod be to be adjust in this way and this be do the engine be to be put to the end of the stroke and the eccentric be to be turn round until the amount of lead have be give that be desire the valve must be try by turn the engine round to see that it be right at both centre for go ahead and also for go astern in some example of the link motion one of the eccentric rod be make a little longer than the other and the position of the point of suspension or point of support powerfully influence the action of the link in certain case especially if the link and this point be not in the same vertical line to reconcile all the condition proper to the satisfactory operation of the valve in the construction of the link motion be a problem require a good deal of attention and care for its satisfactory solution and to make sure that this result be attain the engine must be turn round a sufficient number of time to enable we to ascertain if the valve occupy the desire position both at the top and bottom centre whether the engine be go ahead or astern this should also be try with the start handle in the different notch or in other word with the slide block in the slot or opening of the link in different position management of marine boiler 726 _ q _ -- you have already state that the formation of salt or scale in marine boiler be to be prevent by blow out into the sea at frequent interval a portion of the concentrated water will you now explain how the proper quantity of water to be blow out be determine _ a _ -- by means of the salinometer which be a instrument for determine the density of the water construct on the principle of the hydrometer for tell the strength of spirit some of the water be draw off from the boiler from time to time and the salinometer be immerse in it after it have be cool by the graduation of the salinometer the saltness of this water be at once discover and if the saltness exceed 8 ounce of salt in the gallon more water should be blow out of the boiler to be replenish with fresher water from the sea until the prescribe limit of freshness be attain should the salinometer be accidentally break a temporary one may be construct of a phial weighted with a few grain of shot or other convenient weight the weighted phial be first to be float in fresh water and its line of floatation marked then to be float in salt water and its line of floatation marked and another mark of a equal height above the salt water mark will be the blow off point 727 _ q _ -- how often should boiler be blow off in order to keep they free from incrustation _ a _ -- flue boiler generally require to be blow off about twice every watch or about twice in the four hour but tubular boiler may require to be blow off once every twenty minute and such a amount of blow off should in every case be adopt as will effectually prevent any injurious amount of incrustation 728 _ q _ -- in the event of scale accumulate on the flue of a boiler what be the best way of remove it _ a _ -- if the boiler require to be scale the best method of perform the operation appear to be the following : -- lay a train of shaving along the flue open the safety valve to prevent the existence of any pressure within the boiler and light the train of shaving which by expand rapidly the metal of the flue while the scale from its imperfect conduct power can only expand slowly will crack off the scale by wash down the flue with a hose the scale will be carry to the bottom of the boiler or issue with the water from the mud-hole door this method of scale must be practice only by the engineer himself and must not be intrust to the fireman who in they ignorance might damage the boiler by overheate the plate it be only where the incrustation upon the flue be considerable that this method of remove it need be practice in partial case the scale may be chip off by a hatch face hammer and the flue may then be wash down with the hose in the manner before describe 729 _ q _ -- should the steam be let out of the boiler after it have blow out the water when the engine be stop _ a _ -- no it be better to retain the steam in the boiler as the heat and moisture it occasion soften any scale adhering to the boiler and cause it to peel off care must however be take not to form a vacuum in the boiler and the gauge cock if open will prevent this 730 _ q _ -- be tubular boiler liable to the formation of scale in certain place though generally free from it _ a _ -- in tubular boiler a good deal of care be require to prevent the end of the tube next the furnace from become coated with scale even when the boiler be tolerably clean in other place the scale will collect here and in many case where the amount of blow off previously find to suffice for flue boiler have be adopt a incrustation five eighth of a inch in thickness have form in twelve month round the furnace end of the tube and the stony husk envelop they have actually grow together in some part so as totally to exclude the water 731 _ q _ -- when a tubular boiler get incrust in the manner you have describe what be the best course to be adopt for the removal of the scale _ a _ -- when a boiler get into this state the whole of the tube must be pull out which may be do by a spanish windlass combine with a pair of block and three man when thus provide will be able to draw out from 50 to 70 tube per day -- those tube with the thickest and firmest incrustation be of course the most difficult to remove the act of draw out the tube remove the incrustation but the tube should afterward be scrape by draw they backward and forward between the old file fix in a vice in the form of the letter v the end of the tube should then be heat and dress with the hammer and plunge while at a blood heat into a bed of sawdust to make they cool soft so that they may be rivet again with facility a few of the tube will be so far damage at the end by the act of draw they out as to be too short for reinsertion : this result might be to a considerable extent obviate by set the tube plate at different angle so that the several horizontal row of tube would not be originally of the same length and the damage tube of the long row would serve to replace the short one but the practice would be attend with other inconvenience 732 _ q _ -- be there no other means of keep boiler free from scale than by blow off _ a _ -- muriatic acid or muriate of ammonia commonly call sal-ammoniac introduce into a boiler prevent scale to a great extent but it be liable to corrode the boiler internally and also to damage the engine by be carry over with the steam and the use of such intermixture do not appear to be necessary if blow off from the surface of the water be largely practice in old boiler however already incrust with scale the use of muriate of ammonia may sometimes be advantageous 733 _ q _ -- be not the tube of tubular boiler liable to be choke up by deposit of soot _ a _ -- the soot which collect in the inside of the tube of tubular boiler be remove by means of a brush like a large bottle brush and the carbonaceous scale which remain adhering to the interior of the tube be remove by a circular scraper ferule in the tube interfere with the action of this scraper and in the case of iron tube ferule be now generally discard but it will sometimes be necessary to use ferule for iron tube where the tube have be draw and reinsert as it may be difficult to refix the tube without such a auxiliary tube one tenth of a inch in thickness be too thin : one eighth of a inch be a better thickness and such tube will better dispense with the use of ferule and will not so soon wear into hole 734 _ q _ -- if the furnace or flue of a boiler be injure how do you proceed to repair it _ a _ -- if from any imperfection in the roof of a furnace or flue a patch require to be put upon it it will be better to let the patch be apply upon the upper rather than upon the lower surface of the plate as if apply within the furnace a recess will be form for the lodgment of deposit which will prevent the rapid transmission of the heat in that part and the iron will be very liable to be again burn away a crack in a plate may be close by bore hole in the direction of the crack and insert rivet with large head so as to cover up the imperfection if the top of the furnace be bent down from the boiler have be accidentally allow to get short of water it may be set up again by a screw jack -- a fire of wood have be previously make beneath the injured plate but it will in general be nearly as expeditious a course to remove the plate and introduce a new one and the result will be more satisfactory 735 _ q _ -- in the case of the chimney be carry away by shot or otherwise what course would you pursue _ a _ -- in some case of collision the funnel be carry away and lose overboard and such case be among the most difficult for which a remedy can be seek if flame come out of the chimney when the funnel be knock away so as to incur the risk of set the ship on fire the uptake of the boiler must be cover over with a iron plate or be sufficiently cover to prevent such injury a temporary chimney must then be make of such material as be on board the ship if there be brick and clay or lime on board a square chimney may be build with they or if there be sheet iron plate on board a square chimney may be construct of they in the absence of such material the awning stanchion may be set up round the chimney and chain rove in through among they in the manner of wicker work so as to make a iron wicker chimney which may then be plaster outside with wet ash mix with clay flour or any other material that will give the ash cohesion war steamer should carry short spare funnel which may easily be set up should the original funnel be shoot away and if a jet of steam be let into the chimney a very short and small funnel will suffice for the purpose of draught management of marine engine 736 _ q _ -- what be the most important of the point which suggest themselves to you in connection with the management of marine engine _ a _ -- the attendant upon engine should prepare themselves for any casualty that may arise by consider possible case of derangement and decide in what way they would act should certain accident occur the course to be pursue must have reference to particular engine and no general rule can therefore be give but every marine engineer should be prepare with the measure to be pursue in the emergency in which he may be call upon to act and where everything may depend upon he energy and decision 737 _ q _ -- what be the first point of a marine engineer 's duty _ a _ -- the safe custody of the boiler he must see that the feed be maintain be neither too high nor too low and that blow out the supersalted water be practice sufficiently the saltness of the water at every half hour should be enter in the log book together with the pressure of steam number of revolution of the engine and any other particulars which have to be record the economical use of the fuel be another matter which should receive particular attention if the coal be very small it should be wet before be put on the fire next to the safety of the boiler the bearing of the engine be the most important consideration these point indeed constitute the main part of the duty of a engineer suppose no accident to the machinery to have take place 738 _ q _ -- if the eccentric catch or hoop be disabled how would you work the valve _ a _ -- if the eccentric catch or hoop break or come off and the damage can not readily be repair the valve may be work by attach the end of the start handle to any convenient part of the other engine or to some part in connection with the connect rod of the same engine in side lever engine with the start bar hanging from the top of the diagonal stay as be a very common arrangement the valve might be work by lead a rope from the side lever of the other engine through block so as to give a horizontal pull to the hang start bar and the bar could be bring back by a weight another plan would be to lash a piece of wood to the cross tail butt of the damage engine so as to obtain a sufficient throw for work the valve and then to lead a piece of wood or iron from a suitable point in the piece of wood attach to the cross tail to the start handle whereby the valve would receive its proper motion in oscillate engine it be easy to give the required motion to the valve by derive it from the oscillation of the cylinder 739 _ q _ -- what would you do if a crank pin break _ a _ -- if the crank pin break in a paddle vessel with two engine the other engine must be make to work one wheel in a screw vessel the same course may be pursue provide the broken crank be not the one through which the force of the other engine be communicate to the screw in such a case the vessel will be as much disabled as if she break the screw shaft or screw 740 _ q _ -- will the unbroken engine in the case of disarrangement of one of the two engine of a screw or paddle vessel be able of itself to turn the center _ a _ -- it will sometimes happen when there be much lead upon the slide valve that the single engine on be start can not be get to turn the center if there be a strong oppose wind and sea the piston go up to near the end of the stroke and then come down again without the crank be able to turn the center in such case it will be necessary to turn the vessel 's head sufficiently from the wind to enable some sail to be set and if once there be weigh get upon the vessel the engine will begin to work properly and will continue to do so though the vessel be put head to wind as before 741 _ q _ -- what should be do if a crack show itself in any of the shaft or crank _ a _ -- if the shaft or crank crack the engine may nevertheless be work with moderate pressure to bring the vessel into port but if the crack be very bad it will be expedient to fit strong block of wood under the end of the side lever or other suitable part to prevent the cylinder bottom or cover from be knock out should the damaged part give way the same remark be applicable when flaw be discover in any of the main part of the engine whether they be malleable or cast iron but they must be carefully watch so that the engine may be stop if the crack be extend further should fracture occur the first thing obviously to be do be to throw the engine out of gear and should there be much weigh on the vessel the steam should at once be throw on the reverse side of the piston so as to counteract the pressure of the paddle wheel 742 _ q _ -- have you any information to offer relative to the lubrication of engine bearing _ a _ -- a very useful species of oil cup be now employ in a number of steam vessel and which it be say accomplish a considerable saving of oil at the same time that it more effectually lubricate the bearing a ratchet wheel be fix upon a little shaft which pass through the side of the oil cup and be put into slow revolution by a pendulum attach to its outside and in revolve it lift up little bucket of oil and empty they down a funnel upon the center of the bearing instead of bucket a few short piece of wire be sometimes hang on the internal revolving wheel the drop of oil which adhere on rise from the liquid be deposit upon a high part set upon the funnel and which in they revolution the hang wire touch by this plan however the oil be not well supply at slow speed as the drop fall before the wire be in proper position for feed the journal another lubricator consist of a cock or plug insert in the neck of the oil cup and set in revolution by a pendulum and ratchet wheel or any other means there be a small cavity in one side of the plug which be fill with oil when that side be uppermost and deliver the oil through the bottom pipe when it come opposite to it 743 _ q _ -- what be the prevail cause of the heating of bearing _ a _ -- bad fitting deficient surface and too tight screw down sometimes the oil hole will choke or the syphon wick for conduct the oil from the oil cup into the central pipe lead to the bearing will become clog with mucilage from the oil in some case bearing heat from the existence of a cruciform groove on the top brass for the distribution of the oil the effect of which be to leave the top of the bearing dry in the case of revolving journal the plan for cut a cruciform channel for the distribution of the oil do not do much damage but in other case as in beam journal for instance it be most injurious and the brass can not wear well wherever the plan be pursue the right way be to make a horizontal groove along the brass where it meet the upper surface of the bearing so that the oil may be all deposit on the highest point of the journal leave the force of gravity to send it downward this channel should of course stop short a small distance from each flange of the brass otherwise the oil would run out at the end 744 _ q _ -- if a bearing heat what be to be do _ a _ -- the first thing be to relax the screw slow or stop the engine and cool the bearing with water and if it be very hot then hot water may be first employ to cool it and then cold oil with sulphur intermingle be then to be administer and as the part cool down the screw may be again cautiously tighten so as to take any jump off the engine from the bearing be too slack the bearing of direct act screw engine require constant watch as if there be any disposition to heat manifest by they they will probably heat with great rapidity from the high velocity at which the engine work every bearing of a direct act screw engine should have a cock of water lay on to it which may be immediately open wide should heating occur and it be advisable to work the engine constantly partly with water and partly with oil apply to the bearing the water and oil be mix by the friction into a species of soap which both cool and lubricate and less oil moreover be use than if water be not employ it be proper to turn off the water some time before the engine be stop so as to prevent the rusting of the bearing management of locomotive 745 _ q _ -- what be the chief duty of the engine driver of a locomotive _ a _ -- he first duty be those which concern the safety of the train he next those which concern the safety and right management of the engine and boiler the engine driver 's first solicitude should be relative to the observation and right interpretation of the signal and it be only after these demand upon he attention have be satisfy that he can look to the state of he engine 746 _ q _ -- as regard the engine and boiler what should he main duty be _ a _ -- the engineer of a locomotive should constantly be upon the foot board of the engine so that the regulator the whistle or the reverse handle may be use instantly if necessary he must see that the level of the water in the boiler be duly maintain and that the steam be keep at a uniform pressure in feed the boiler with water and the furnace with fuel a good deal of care and some tact be necessary as irregularity in the production of steam will often occasion priming even though the water be maintain at a uniform level and a excess of water will of itself occasion priming while a deficiency be a source of obvious danger the engine be generally furnish with three gauge cock and water should always come out of the second gauge cock and steam out of the top one when the engine be run : but when the engine be at rest the water in the boiler be lower than when in motion so that when the engine be at rest the water will be high enough if it just reach to the middle gauge cock in all boiler which generate steam rapidly the volume of the water be increase by the mingled steam and in feed with cold water the level at first fall but it rise on open the safety valve which cause the steam in the water to swell to a larger volume in locomotive boiler the rise of the water level due to the rapid generation of steam be term false water to economize fuel the variable expansion gear if the engine have one should be adjust to the load and the blast pipe should be work with the least possible contraction and at station the damper should be close to prevent the dissipation of heat 747 _ q _ -- in start from a station what precaution should be observe with respect to the feed _ a _ -- in start from a station and also in ascend inclined plane the feed water be generally shut off and therefore before stop or ascend inclined plane the boiler should be well fill up with water in descend inclined plane a extra supply of water may be introduce into the boiler and the fire may be feed as there be at such time a superfluity of steam in descend inclined plane the regulator must be partially close and it should be entirely close if the plane be very steep the same precaution should be observe in the case of curve or rough place on the line and in pass over point or crossing 748 _ q _ -- in approach a station how should the supply of water and fuel be regulate _ a _ -- the boiler should be well fill with water on approach a station as there be then steam to spare and additional water can not be conveniently supply when the engine be stationary the furnace should be feed with small quantity of fuel at a time and the feed should be turn off just before a fresh supply of fuel be introduce the regulator may at the same time be partially close and if the blast pipe be a variable one it will be expedient to open it widely while the fuel be be introduce to check the rush of air in through the furnace door and then to contract it very much so soon as the furnace door be close in order to recover the fire quickly the proper thickness of coke upon the grate depend upon the intensity of the draught but in heavily loaded engine it be usually keep up to the bottom of the fire door care however must be take that the coke do not reach up to the bottom row of tube so as to choke they up the fuel be usually dispose on the grate like a vault and if the fire box be a square one it be heap high in the corner the better to maintain the combustion 749 _ q _ -- how can you tell whether the feed pump be operate properly _ a _ -- to ascertain whether the pump be act well the pet cock must be turn and if any of the valve stick they will sometimes be induce to act again by work with the pet cock open or alternately open and shut should the defect arise from a leakage of steam into the pump which prevent the pump from draw the pet cock remedy the evil by permit the steam to escape 750 _ q _ -- what precaution should be take against priming in locomotive _ a _ -- should priming occur from the water in the boiler be dirty a portion of it may be blow out and should there be much boil down through the glass gauge tube the stop cock may be partially close the water should be wholly blow out of locomotive boiler three time a week and at those time two mud-hole door at opposite corner of the boiler should be open and the boiler be wash internally by means of a hose if the boiler be habitually feed with dirty water the priming will be a constant source of trouble 751 _ q _ -- what measure should the locomotive engineer take to check the velocity of the train on approach a station where he have to stop _ a _ -- on approach a station the regulator should be gradually close and it should be completely shut about half a mile from the station if the train be a very heavy one : the train may then be bring to rest by means of the break too much reliance however must not be put upon the break as they sometimes give way and in frosty weather be nearly inoperative in case of urgency the steam may be throw upon the reverse side of the piston but it be desirable to obviate this necessity as far as possible at terminal station the steam should be shut off earlier than at roadside station as a collision will take place at terminal station if the train overshoot the place where it ought to stop there should always be a good supply of water when the engine stop but the fire may be suffer gradually to burn low toward the conclusion of the journey 752 _ q _ -- what be the duty of a engine man on arrive at the end of he journey _ a _ -- so soon as the engine stop it should be wipe down and be then carefully examine : the brass should be try to see whether they be slack or have be heat and by the application of a gauge it should be ascertain occasionally whether the wheel be square on they axle and whether the axle have end play which should be prevent the stuffing box must be tighten and the valve gear examine and the eccentric be occasionally look at to see that they have not shift on they axle though this defect will be generally intimate by the irregular beating of the engine the tube should also be examine and clean out and the ash empty out of the smoke box through the small ash door at the end if the engine be a six-wheeled one with the drive wheel in the middle it will be liable to pitch and oscillate if too much weight be throw upon the drive wheel and where such fault be find to exist the weight upon the driving wheel should be diminish the practice of blow off the boiler by the steam as be always do in marine boiler should not be permit as a general rule in locomotive boiler when the tube be of brass and the fire box of copper but when the tube and fire box be of iron there will not be a equal risk of injury before start on a journey the engine man should take a summary glance beneath the engine -- but before do so he ought to assure himself that no other engine be come up at the time the regulator when the engine be stand should be close and lock and the eccentric rod be fix out of gear and the tender break screw down the cock of the oil vessel should at the same time be shut but should all be open a short time before the train start 753 _ q _ -- what should be do if a tube burst in the boiler _ a _ -- when a tube burst a wooden or iron plug must be drive into each end of it and if the water or steam be rush out so fiercely that the exact position of the imperfection can not be discover it will be advisable to diminish the pressure by increase the supply of feed water should the leak be so great that the level of the water in the boiler can not be maintain it will be expedient to drop the bar and quench the fire so as to preserve the tube and fire box from injury 754 _ q _ -- if any of the work part of a locomotive break or become deranged what should be do _ a _ -- should the piston rod or connect rod break or the cutter fall out or be clip off -- as sometimes happen to the piston cutter when the engine be suddenly reverse upon a heavy train -- the part should be disconnect if the connection can not be restore so as to enable one engine to work and of course the valve of the faulty engine must be keep close if one engine have not power enough to enable the train to proceed with the blast pipe full open the engine may perhaps be able to take on a part of the carriage or it may run on by itself to fetch assistance the same course must be pursue if any of the valve gear become deranged and the defect can not be rectify upon the spot 755 _ q _ -- what be the most usual cause of railway collision _ a _ -- probably fog and inexactness in the time keep by the train collision have sometimes occur from carriage have be blow from a siding on to the rail by a high wind and the slippery state of the rail or the fracture of a break have sometimes occasion collision at terminal station collision have also repeatedly take place from one engine have overtake another from the failure of a tube in the first engine or from some other slight disarrangement and collision have also take place from the switch have be accidentally so leave as to direct the train into a siding instead of continue it on the main line every train now carry fog signal which be detonate packet which be fix upon the rail in advance or in the rear of a train which whether from get off the rail or otherwise be stop upon the line and which be explode by the wheel of any approach train 756 _ q _ -- what other duty of a engine-driver be there deserving attention _ a _ -- they be too various to be all enumerate here and they also vary somewhat with the nature of the service one rule however of universal application be for the driver to look after matter himself and not delegate to the stoker the duty which the person in charge of the engine should properly perform before leave a station the engine-driver should assure himself that he have the requisite supply of coke and water besides the firing tool and rake for clear the tube he should have with he in the tender a set of signal lamp and torch for tunnel and for night detonate signal screw key a small tank of oil a small cask of tallow and a small box of waste a coal hammer a chip hammer some wooden and iron plug for the tube and a iron tube holder
